الباب الثالث: الفصل الأول - الحس
١ - تسخير الله تعالى الكون للإنسان وثمة آيات كثيرة بهذا الخصوص لعل من أبرزها قوله تعالى: ﴿ اللهُ الَّذِي خَلَقَ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالأَرْضَ وَأَنْزَلَ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً فَأَخْرَجَ بِهِ مِنَ الثَّمَرَاتِ رِزْقاً لَكُمْ وَسَخَّرَ لَكُمُ الْفُلْكَ لِتَجْرِيَ فِي الْبَحْرِ بِأَمْرِهِ وَسَخَّرَ لَكُمُ الأَنْهَارَ، وَسَخَّرَ لَكُمُ الشَّمْسَ وَالْقَمَرَ الْبَيِّنَيْنِ وَسَخَّرَ لَكُمُ اللَّيْلَ وَالنَّهَارَ ﴾ [إبراهيم: ٣٢/١٤-٣٣].
٢ - العرض الواقعي لحال الكون حيث يعرض الكون أمام الإنسان في صورته المتحركة: ﴿ وَتَرَى الأَرْضَ هَامِدَةً فَإِذَا أَنْزَلْنَا عَلَيْهَا الْمَاءَ اهْتَزَّتْ وَرَبَتْ وَأَنْبَتَتْ مِنْ كُلِّ زَوْجٍ بَهِيجٍ ﴾ [الحج: ٥/٢٢]. ﴿ وَالشَّمْسُ تَجْرِي لِمُسْتَقَرٍّ لَهَا ذَلِكَ تَقْدِيرُ الْعَزِيزِ الْعَلِيمِ، وَالْقَمَرَ قَدَّرْنَاهُ مَنَازِلَ حَتَّى عَادَ كَالْعُرْجُونِ الْقَدِيمِ، لا الشَّمْسُ يَنْبَغِي لَهَا أَنْ تُدْرِكَ الْقَمَرَ وَلَا اللَّيْلُ سَابِقُ النَّهَارِ وَكُلٌّ فِي فَلَكٍ يَسْبَحُونَ ﴾ [يس: ٣٨/٣٦-٤٠]. فاعلية الإنسان أي إن الله تعالى دفع الإنسان لاستخدام حواسه وعقله من خلال الآيات المتحدثة عن الكون والمختتمة بمثل قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَإِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لَآيَاتٍ لِقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ .. يَتَفَكَّرُونَ .. وَيَفْقَهُونَ ﴾، بل وتجعل آيــات القرآن الكريم المهمة العملية للإنسان هي القيام بدوره الفاعل في الكون والحياة: ﴿ قُلْ سِيرُوا فِي الأَرْضِ ﴾ [الأنعام: ١١/٦]، ﴿ فَامْشُوا فِي مَنَاكِبِهَا ﴾ [الملك: ١٥/٦٧]، ﴿ وَكُلُوا مِمَّا رَزَقَكُمُ اللهُ حَلالاً طَيِّباً ﴾ [النحل: ١١٤/١٦]، ﴿ وَهُوَ أَنْشَأَكُمْ مِنَ الْأَرْضِ وَاسْتَعْمَرَكُمْ فِيهَا ﴾ [هود: ٦١/١١].
تعليم منهج البحث التجريبي وذلك في إشارات القرآن الكريم إلى الاطّراد والسببية بين الحوادث ومسألة الكميات والمقادير (العد والوزن والإحصاء) في ذكره للحوادث المختلفة ﴿ وَاللهُ يُقَدِّرُ اللَّيْلَ وَالنَّهَارَ ﴾ [المزمل: ٢٠/٧٣]، و ﴿ وَجَعَلْنَا اللَّيْلَ وَالنَّهَارَ آيَتَيْنِ فَمَحَوْنَا آيَةَ اللَّيْلِ وَجَعَلْنَا آيَةَ النَّهَارِ مُبْصِرَةً لِتَبْتَغُوا فَضْلاً مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ وَلِتَعْلَمُوا عَدَدَ السِّنِينَ وَالْحِسَابَ وَكُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَصَّلْنَاهُ تَفْصِيلاً ﴾ [الإسراء: ١٢/١٧]. وكذلك أشار إلى فكرة التصنيف، والتي تعدّ اليوم إحدى قواعد المنهج التجريبي: ﴿ وَاللهُ خَلَقَ كُلَّ دَابَّةٍ مِنْ مَاءٍ فَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ يَمْشِي عَلَى بَطْنِهِ وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ يَمْشِي عَلَى رِجْلَيْنِ وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ يَمْشِي عَلَى أَرْبَعٍ يَخْلُقُ اللهُ مَا يَشَاءُ ﴾ [النور: ١٤٥/٢٤]. إن القرآن الكريم يولي النهج التجريبي اهتماماً ملحوظاً، فهو يلفت النظر إلى أهمية استخدامه من خلال بعض الإشارات الرامية إلى توصيل هذا المدلول. فقد دعا إلى استخدام أداة النظر الحسيّة لملاحظة التغيرات الطارئة، والنفاذ منها إلى الاستدلال على قدرة الله تعالى على إحياء الأجساد بعد فنائها بما يؤكـد مـا أشرنا إليه سابقاً من الإيماء إلى أهمية الاختبارين القبلي والبعــدي المتأثرين بالمتغيرات الطارئة وتلك هي صورة الشكل المنهجي الموصل إلى الحقيقة الأخروية: ﴿ أَوْ كَالَّذِي مَرَّ عَلَى قَرْيَةٍ وَهِيَ خَاوِيَةٌ عَلَى عُرُوشِهَا قَالَ أَنَّى يُحْيِي هَذِهِ اللَّهُ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَا فَأَمَاتَهُ اللهُ مِئَةَ عَامٍ ثُمَّ بَعَثَهُ قَالَ كَمْ لَبِثْتَ قَالَ لَبِثْتُ يَوْماً أَوْ بَعْضَ يَوْمٍ قَالَ بَلْ لَبِثْتَ مِئَةَ عَامٍ فَانْظُرْ إِلَى طَعَامِكَ وَشَرَابِكَ لَمْ يَتَسَنَّهْ وَانْظُرْ إِلَى حِمَارِكَ وَلِنَجْعَلَكَ آيَةً لِلنَّاسِ وَانْظُرْ إِلَى الْعِظَامِ كَيْفَ نُنْشِرُهَا ثُمَّ نَكْسُوهَا لَحْماً فَلَمَّا تَبَيَّنَ لَهُ قَالَ أَعْلَمُ أَنَّ اللهَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٩/٢].
Part Three: The First Chapter: The Sense. 1- God's subjugation of the universe for man, and there are many verses in this regard, perhaps the most prominent of which is His saying: 'It is Allah who created the heavens and the earth and sent down from the sky rain and brought forth thereby fruits as provision for you. And He subjected for you the ships to sail through the sea by His command, and He subjected for you the rivers. And He subjected for you the sun and the moon, both constantly pursuing their courses, and He subjected for you the night and the day.' [Ibrahim 14:32-33]. 2- The realistic presentation of the state of the universe, where the universe is presented before man in its moving form: 'And you see the earth barren, but when We send down upon it rain, it quivers and swells and grows of every beautiful kind.' [Al-Hajj 22:5]. 'And the sun runs on to a term determined for it; that is the determination of the Exalted in Might, the Knowing. And the moon – We have determined for it phases until it returns like the old dried curved date stalk. It is not for the sun to overtake the moon, nor does the night outstrip the day. And all float in an orbit.' [Ya-Sin 36:38-40]. The effectiveness of man: that is, God Almighty urges man to use his senses and intellect through the verses that speak about the universe and conclude with His saying: 'Indeed in that are signs for a people who use reason... who reflect... who understand.' Rather, the verses of the Noble Quran make the practical task of man to be his active role in the universe and life: 'Say, travel through the land' [Al-An'am 6:11], 'and walk among its slopes' [Al-Mulk 67:15], 'and eat from what Allah has provided for you [as] lawful and good' [An-Nahl 16:114], 'and He has produced you from the earth and settled you in it' [Hud 11:61]. Teaching the method of empirical research, and that is in the Quran's indications of regularity and causality between events and the issue of quantities and measures (counting, weighing, and enumeration) in its mentioning of various events: 'And Allah determines the night and the day' [Al-Muzzammil 73:20], and 'And We have made the night and the day two signs, and We erased the sign of the night and made the sign of the day giving sight that you may seek bounty from your Lord and that you may know the number of years and the account. And We have detailed everything in detail.' [Al-Isra' 17:12]. It also indicated the idea of classification, which today is one of the rules of the empirical method: 'And Allah has created every living creature from water. And of them are those that move on their bellies, and of them are those that move on two legs, and of them are those that move on four. Allah creates what He wills.' [An-Nur 24:45]. The Noble Quran gives significant attention to the empirical approach, as it draws attention to the importance of using it through some indications aimed at conveying this meaning. It called for the use of the sensory observation tool to note the changes that occur, and to penetrate from them to infer the power of God Almighty to revive bodies after their annihilation, confirming what we indicated earlier of the allusion to the importance of the pre- and post-tests affected by the variables that occur, and that is the form of the methodological path that leads to the eschatological truth: 'Or like the one who passed by a town that had collapsed on its foundations and said, 'How will Allah bring this to life after its death?' So Allah caused him to die for a hundred years; then He revived him and said, 'How long have you remained?' He said, 'I have remained a day or part of a day.' He said, 'Rather, you have remained a hundred years. Look at your food and your drink; it has not changed. And look at your donkey; and We will make you a sign for the people. And look at the bones, how We raise them and then We cover them with flesh.' And when it became clear to him, he said, 'I know that Allah is over all things competent.' ' [Al-Baqarah 2:259].
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion about the Quran's emphasis on sensory experience and empirical methodology. The author begins by stating that this chapter is about 'the sense' (الحس), then presents three main points: (1) God's subjugation of the universe for mankind, citing Quranic verses that list how God has subjected celestial bodies, seas, rivers, and day and night for human benefit. (2) The realistic presentation of the universe in motion, showing the alternation of day and night, the phases of the moon, and the cycle of seasons, all of which invite reflection. (3) The effectiveness of man, meaning that God urges humans to use their senses and intellect through verses that call for reasoning, reflecting, and understanding. Then the author discusses how the Quran teaches the empirical research method through references to regularity and causality, measurement and counting, and classification. The author emphasizes that the Quran calls for using sensory observation to note changes and infer God's power, as exemplified in the story of the man who passed by a ruined town and witnessed resurrection. The commentary should follow the author's order: first the three points, then the empirical method, and finally the example. It explains that the Quran is not just a book of spiritual guidance but also a call to observe the natural world using the senses, forming a foundation for empirical science.

The Quran commands humans to observe the natural world with their senses and to use reason to derive knowledge.

Method of Learning

Empirical Method Components in the Quran
Author discusses how the Quran's references to regularity, measurement, and classification indicate an empirical methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify three key components of the empirical method—causality, measurement, and classification—as alluded to in specific Quranic verses.

Core Idea
The Quran teaches the empirical method through concepts of cause-effect, quantification, and categorization.

This lesson unpacks the author's claim that the Quran contains the foundations of the empirical method. By examining verses on regularity and causality, counting and measurement, and classification of creatures, you will see how the Quran anticipates key elements of scientific methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three components the author mentions.
The author explicitly lists: (1) regularity and causality (الاطراد والسببية), (2) quantities and measures (الكميات والمقادير: counting, weighing, enumeration), and (3) classification (التصنيف).
These correspond to modern empirical method.
2
For causality, find the Quranic verse(s) and explain how they imply cause-effect.
The verse 'And Allah determines the night and the day' (Al-Muzzammil 73:20) suggests a fixed system; the description of cause and effect is implicit in the alternation. Also the verse about night and day in Al-Isra' 17:12 links them to seeking bounty and calculating years.
Causality is the backbone of empirical science.
3
For measurement, identify the verse that discusses counting and calculation.
Al-Isra' 17:12 explicitly says 'that you may know the number of years and the account.' This highlights quantification.
4
For classification, examine An-Nur 24:45.
The verse categorizes creatures by their mode of movement: on belly, two legs, four legs. This is a clear act of classification.
Classification is a fundamental scientific activity.
5
Synthesize: how do these three components form the empirical method?
Empirical method involves observing regularities (causality), measuring (quantification), and organizing (classification). The Quran thus provides the conceptual toolkit for scientific investigation.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الأول - الحس
١ - تسخير الله تعالى الكون للإنسان وثمة آيات كثيرة بهذا الخصوص لعل من أبرزها قوله تعالى: ﴿ اللهُ الَّذِي خَلَقَ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالأَرْضَ وَأَنْزَلَ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً فَأَخْرَجَ بِهِ مِنَ الثَّمَرَاتِ رِزْقاً لَكُمْ وَسَخَّرَ لَكُمُ الْفُلْكَ لِتَجْرِيَ فِي الْبَحْرِ بِأَمْرِهِ وَسَخَّرَ لَكُمُ الأَنْهَارَ، وَسَخَّرَ لَكُمُ الشَّمْسَ وَالْقَمَرَ الْبَيِّنَيْنِ وَسَخَّرَ لَكُمُ اللَّيْلَ وَالنَّهَارَ ﴾ [إبراهيم: ٣٢/١٤-٣٣].
٢ - العرض الواقعي لحال الكون حيث يعرض الكون أمام الإنسان في صورته المتحركة: ﴿ وَتَرَى الأَرْضَ هَامِدَةً فَإِذَا أَنْزَلْنَا عَلَيْهَا الْمَاءَ اهْتَزَّتْ وَرَبَتْ وَأَنْبَتَتْ مِنْ كُلِّ زَوْجٍ بَهِيجٍ ﴾ [الحج: ٥/٢٢]. ﴿ وَالشَّمْسُ تَجْرِي لِمُسْتَقَرٍّ لَهَا ذَلِكَ تَقْدِيرُ الْعَزِيزِ الْعَلِيمِ، وَالْقَمَرَ قَدَّرْنَاهُ مَنَازِلَ حَتَّى عَادَ كَالْعُرْجُونِ الْقَدِيمِ، لا الشَّمْسُ يَنْبَغِي لَهَا أَنْ تُدْرِكَ الْقَمَرَ وَلَا اللَّيْلُ سَابِقُ النَّهَارِ وَكُلٌّ فِي فَلَكٍ يَسْبَحُونَ ﴾ [يس: ٣٨/٣٦-٤٠]. فاعلية الإنسان أي إن الله تعالى دفع الإنسان لاستخدام حواسه وعقله من خلال الآيات المتحدثة عن الكون والمختتمة بمثل قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَإِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لَآيَاتٍ لِقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ .. يَتَفَكَّرُونَ .. وَيَفْقَهُونَ ﴾، بل وتجعل آيــات القرآن الكريم المهمة العملية للإنسان هي القيام بدوره الفاعل في الكون والحياة: ﴿ قُلْ سِيرُوا فِي الأَرْضِ ﴾ [الأنعام: ١١/٦]، ﴿ فَامْشُوا فِي مَنَاكِبِهَا ﴾ [الملك: ١٥/٦٧]، ﴿ وَكُلُوا مِمَّا رَزَقَكُمُ اللهُ حَلالاً طَيِّباً ﴾ [النحل: ١١٤/١٦]، ﴿ وَهُوَ أَنْشَأَكُمْ مِنَ الْأَرْضِ وَاسْتَعْمَرَكُمْ فِيهَا ﴾ [هود: ٦١/١١].
تعليم منهج البحث التجريبي وذلك في إشارات القرآن الكريم إلى الاطّراد والسببية بين الحوادث ومسألة الكميات والمقادير (العد والوزن والإحصاء) في ذكره للحوادث المختلفة ﴿ وَاللهُ يُقَدِّرُ اللَّيْلَ وَالنَّهَارَ ﴾ [المزمل: ٢٠/٧٣]، و ﴿ وَجَعَلْنَا اللَّيْلَ وَالنَّهَارَ آيَتَيْنِ فَمَحَوْنَا آيَةَ اللَّيْلِ وَجَعَلْنَا آيَةَ النَّهَارِ مُبْصِرَةً لِتَبْتَغُوا فَضْلاً مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ وَلِتَعْلَمُوا عَدَدَ السِّنِينَ وَالْحِسَابَ وَكُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَصَّلْنَاهُ تَفْصِيلاً ﴾ [الإسراء: ١٢/١٧]. وكذلك أشار إلى فكرة التصنيف، والتي تعدّ اليوم إحدى قواعد المنهج التجريبي: ﴿ وَاللهُ خَلَقَ كُلَّ دَابَّةٍ مِنْ مَاءٍ فَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ يَمْشِي عَلَى بَطْنِهِ وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ يَمْشِي عَلَى رِجْلَيْنِ وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ يَمْشِي عَلَى أَرْبَعٍ يَخْلُقُ اللهُ مَا يَشَاءُ ﴾ [النور: ١٤٥/٢٤]. إن القرآن الكريم يولي النهج التجريبي اهتماماً ملحوظاً، فهو يلفت النظر إلى أهمية استخدامه من خلال بعض الإشارات الرامية إلى توصيل هذا المدلول. فقد دعا إلى استخدام أداة النظر الحسيّة لملاحظة التغيرات الطارئة، والنفاذ منها إلى الاستدلال على قدرة الله تعالى على إحياء الأجساد بعد فنائها بما يؤكـد مـا أشرنا إليه سابقاً من الإيماء إلى أهمية الاختبارين القبلي والبعــدي المتأثرين بالمتغيرات الطارئة وتلك هي صورة الشكل المنهجي الموصل إلى الحقيقة الأخروية: ﴿ أَوْ كَالَّذِي مَرَّ عَلَى قَرْيَةٍ وَهِيَ خَاوِيَةٌ عَلَى عُرُوشِهَا قَالَ أَنَّى يُحْيِي هَذِهِ اللَّهُ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَا فَأَمَاتَهُ اللهُ مِئَةَ عَامٍ ثُمَّ بَعَثَهُ قَالَ كَمْ لَبِثْتَ قَالَ لَبِثْتُ يَوْماً أَوْ بَعْضَ يَوْمٍ قَالَ بَلْ لَبِثْتَ مِئَةَ عَامٍ فَانْظُرْ إِلَى طَعَامِكَ وَشَرَابِكَ لَمْ يَتَسَنَّهْ وَانْظُرْ إِلَى حِمَارِكَ وَلِنَجْعَلَكَ آيَةً لِلنَّاسِ وَانْظُرْ إِلَى الْعِظَامِ كَيْفَ نُنْشِرُهَا ثُمَّ نَكْسُوهَا لَحْماً فَلَمَّا تَبَيَّنَ لَهُ قَالَ أَعْلَمُ أَنَّ اللهَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٩/٢].
Part Three: The First Chapter: The Sense. 1- God's subjugation of the universe for man, and there are many verses in this regard, perhaps the most prominent of which is His saying: 'It is Allah who created the heavens and the earth and sent down from the sky rain and brought forth thereby fruits as provision for you. And He subjected for you the ships to sail through the sea by His command, and He subjected for you the rivers. And He subjected for you the sun and the moon, both constantly pursuing their courses, and He subjected for you the night and the day.' [Ibrahim 14:32-33]. 2- The realistic presentation of the state of the universe, where the universe is presented before man in its moving form: 'And you see the earth barren, but when We send down upon it rain, it quivers and swells and grows of every beautiful kind.' [Al-Hajj 22:5]. 'And the sun runs on to a term determined for it; that is the determination of the Exalted in Might, the Knowing. And the moon – We have determined for it phases until it returns like the old dried curved date stalk. It is not for the sun to overtake the moon, nor does the night outstrip the day. And all float in an orbit.' [Ya-Sin 36:38-40]. The effectiveness of man: that is, God Almighty urges man to use his senses and intellect through the verses that speak about the universe and conclude with His saying: 'Indeed in that are signs for a people who use reason... who reflect... who understand.' Rather, the verses of the Noble Quran make the practical task of man to be his active role in the universe and life: 'Say, travel through the land' [Al-An'am 6:11], 'and walk among its slopes' [Al-Mulk 67:15], 'and eat from what Allah has provided for you [as] lawful and good' [An-Nahl 16:114], 'and He has produced you from the earth and settled you in it' [Hud 11:61]. Teaching the method of empirical research, and that is in the Quran's indications of regularity and causality between events and the issue of quantities and measures (counting, weighing, and enumeration) in its mentioning of various events: 'And Allah determines the night and the day' [Al-Muzzammil 73:20], and 'And We have made the night and the day two signs, and We erased the sign of the night and made the sign of the day giving sight that you may seek bounty from your Lord and that you may know the number of years and the account. And We have detailed everything in detail.' [Al-Isra' 17:12]. It also indicated the idea of classification, which today is one of the rules of the empirical method: 'And Allah has created every living creature from water. And of them are those that move on their bellies, and of them are those that move on two legs, and of them are those that move on four. Allah creates what He wills.' [An-Nur 24:45]. The Noble Quran gives significant attention to the empirical approach, as it draws attention to the importance of using it through some indications aimed at conveying this meaning. It called for the use of the sensory observation tool to note the changes that occur, and to penetrate from them to infer the power of God Almighty to revive bodies after their annihilation, confirming what we indicated earlier of the allusion to the importance of the pre- and post-tests affected by the variables that occur, and that is the form of the methodological path that leads to the eschatological truth: 'Or like the one who passed by a town that had collapsed on its foundations and said, 'How will Allah bring this to life after its death?' So Allah caused him to die for a hundred years; then He revived him and said, 'How long have you remained?' He said, 'I have remained a day or part of a day.' He said, 'Rather, you have remained a hundred years. Look at your food and your drink; it has not changed. And look at your donkey; and We will make you a sign for the people. And look at the bones, how We raise them and then We cover them with flesh.' And when it became clear to him, he said, 'I know that Allah is over all things competent.' ' [Al-Baqarah 2:259].
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion about the Quran's emphasis on sensory experience and empirical methodology. The author begins by stating that this chapter is about 'the sense' (الحس), then presents three main points: (1) God's subjugation of the universe for mankind, citing Quranic verses that list how God has subjected celestial bodies, seas, rivers, and day and night for human benefit. (2) The realistic presentation of the universe in motion, showing the alternation of day and night, the phases of the moon, and the cycle of seasons, all of which invite reflection. (3) The effectiveness of man, meaning that God urges humans to use their senses and intellect through verses that call for reasoning, reflecting, and understanding. Then the author discusses how the Quran teaches the empirical research method through references to regularity and causality, measurement and counting, and classification. The author emphasizes that the Quran calls for using sensory observation to note changes and infer God's power, as exemplified in the story of the man who passed by a ruined town and witnessed resurrection. The commentary should follow the author's order: first the three points, then the empirical method, and finally the example. It explains that the Quran is not just a book of spiritual guidance but also a call to observe the natural world using the senses, forming a foundation for empirical science.

Method of Learning
intermediate
5 min
The Resurrection Story as an Empirical Model
Author presents the resurrection story as an example of empirical investigation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the story of the man and the donkey (Baqara 2:259) as a model of empirical investigation with pre- and post-test observation.

Core Idea
The resurrection story is a controlled demonstration of empirical method.

The author uses the striking story of a man who passed by a ruined town to illustrate how empirical observation can lead to certainty about resurrection. This lesson dissects the story as a methodological model with before-and-after observation, comparable to a scientific experiment.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse (Baqara 2:259) carefully.
The verse describes a man who sees a town collapsed, wonders about resurrection, is caused to die for a hundred years, then revived and shown evidence: his food and drink unchanged, his donkey dead then bones reassembled and covered with flesh.
This is the entire story.
2
Identify the initial observation and the question.
The man observes a destroyed town and asks 'How will Allah bring this to life after its death?' This is the research question.
Observation triggers inquiry.
3
Identify the 'experimental intervention': death and revival.
God causes him to die for 100 years and then revives him. This is akin to a controlled experiment where the variable is time and state.
Pre-test: before death. Post-test: after revival.
4
Analyze the observations after revival.
He is asked to look at his food and drink (unchanged) and his donkey (dead, then bones resurrected). The changes are noted: some things remained unchanged, others were utterly transformed.
This corresponds to control and experimental variables.
5
Explain how this leads to certainty about resurrection.
The man concludes 'I know that Allah is over all things competent.' His empirical observation of the resurrection process firsthand gives him certitude.
This is the epistemological payoff of empirical method.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الأول - الحس
١ - تسخير الله تعالى الكون للإنسان وثمة آيات كثيرة بهذا الخصوص لعل من أبرزها قوله تعالى: ﴿ اللهُ الَّذِي خَلَقَ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالأَرْضَ وَأَنْزَلَ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً فَأَخْرَجَ بِهِ مِنَ الثَّمَرَاتِ رِزْقاً لَكُمْ وَسَخَّرَ لَكُمُ الْفُلْكَ لِتَجْرِيَ فِي الْبَحْرِ بِأَمْرِهِ وَسَخَّرَ لَكُمُ الأَنْهَارَ، وَسَخَّرَ لَكُمُ الشَّمْسَ وَالْقَمَرَ الْبَيِّنَيْنِ وَسَخَّرَ لَكُمُ اللَّيْلَ وَالنَّهَارَ ﴾ [إبراهيم: ٣٢/١٤-٣٣].
٢ - العرض الواقعي لحال الكون حيث يعرض الكون أمام الإنسان في صورته المتحركة: ﴿ وَتَرَى الأَرْضَ هَامِدَةً فَإِذَا أَنْزَلْنَا عَلَيْهَا الْمَاءَ اهْتَزَّتْ وَرَبَتْ وَأَنْبَتَتْ مِنْ كُلِّ زَوْجٍ بَهِيجٍ ﴾ [الحج: ٥/٢٢]. ﴿ وَالشَّمْسُ تَجْرِي لِمُسْتَقَرٍّ لَهَا ذَلِكَ تَقْدِيرُ الْعَزِيزِ الْعَلِيمِ، وَالْقَمَرَ قَدَّرْنَاهُ مَنَازِلَ حَتَّى عَادَ كَالْعُرْجُونِ الْقَدِيمِ، لا الشَّمْسُ يَنْبَغِي لَهَا أَنْ تُدْرِكَ الْقَمَرَ وَلَا اللَّيْلُ سَابِقُ النَّهَارِ وَكُلٌّ فِي فَلَكٍ يَسْبَحُونَ ﴾ [يس: ٣٨/٣٦-٤٠]. فاعلية الإنسان أي إن الله تعالى دفع الإنسان لاستخدام حواسه وعقله من خلال الآيات المتحدثة عن الكون والمختتمة بمثل قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَإِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لَآيَاتٍ لِقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ .. يَتَفَكَّرُونَ .. وَيَفْقَهُونَ ﴾، بل وتجعل آيــات القرآن الكريم المهمة العملية للإنسان هي القيام بدوره الفاعل في الكون والحياة: ﴿ قُلْ سِيرُوا فِي الأَرْضِ ﴾ [الأنعام: ١١/٦]، ﴿ فَامْشُوا فِي مَنَاكِبِهَا ﴾ [الملك: ١٥/٦٧]، ﴿ وَكُلُوا مِمَّا رَزَقَكُمُ اللهُ حَلالاً طَيِّباً ﴾ [النحل: ١١٤/١٦]، ﴿ وَهُوَ أَنْشَأَكُمْ مِنَ الْأَرْضِ وَاسْتَعْمَرَكُمْ فِيهَا ﴾ [هود: ٦١/١١].
تعليم منهج البحث التجريبي وذلك في إشارات القرآن الكريم إلى الاطّراد والسببية بين الحوادث ومسألة الكميات والمقادير (العد والوزن والإحصاء) في ذكره للحوادث المختلفة ﴿ وَاللهُ يُقَدِّرُ اللَّيْلَ وَالنَّهَارَ ﴾ [المزمل: ٢٠/٧٣]، و ﴿ وَجَعَلْنَا اللَّيْلَ وَالنَّهَارَ آيَتَيْنِ فَمَحَوْنَا آيَةَ اللَّيْلِ وَجَعَلْنَا آيَةَ النَّهَارِ مُبْصِرَةً لِتَبْتَغُوا فَضْلاً مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ وَلِتَعْلَمُوا عَدَدَ السِّنِينَ وَالْحِسَابَ وَكُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَصَّلْنَاهُ تَفْصِيلاً ﴾ [الإسراء: ١٢/١٧]. وكذلك أشار إلى فكرة التصنيف، والتي تعدّ اليوم إحدى قواعد المنهج التجريبي: ﴿ وَاللهُ خَلَقَ كُلَّ دَابَّةٍ مِنْ مَاءٍ فَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ يَمْشِي عَلَى بَطْنِهِ وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ يَمْشِي عَلَى رِجْلَيْنِ وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ يَمْشِي عَلَى أَرْبَعٍ يَخْلُقُ اللهُ مَا يَشَاءُ ﴾ [النور: ١٤٥/٢٤]. إن القرآن الكريم يولي النهج التجريبي اهتماماً ملحوظاً، فهو يلفت النظر إلى أهمية استخدامه من خلال بعض الإشارات الرامية إلى توصيل هذا المدلول. فقد دعا إلى استخدام أداة النظر الحسيّة لملاحظة التغيرات الطارئة، والنفاذ منها إلى الاستدلال على قدرة الله تعالى على إحياء الأجساد بعد فنائها بما يؤكـد مـا أشرنا إليه سابقاً من الإيماء إلى أهمية الاختبارين القبلي والبعــدي المتأثرين بالمتغيرات الطارئة وتلك هي صورة الشكل المنهجي الموصل إلى الحقيقة الأخروية: ﴿ أَوْ كَالَّذِي مَرَّ عَلَى قَرْيَةٍ وَهِيَ خَاوِيَةٌ عَلَى عُرُوشِهَا قَالَ أَنَّى يُحْيِي هَذِهِ اللَّهُ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَا فَأَمَاتَهُ اللهُ مِئَةَ عَامٍ ثُمَّ بَعَثَهُ قَالَ كَمْ لَبِثْتَ قَالَ لَبِثْتُ يَوْماً أَوْ بَعْضَ يَوْمٍ قَالَ بَلْ لَبِثْتَ مِئَةَ عَامٍ فَانْظُرْ إِلَى طَعَامِكَ وَشَرَابِكَ لَمْ يَتَسَنَّهْ وَانْظُرْ إِلَى حِمَارِكَ وَلِنَجْعَلَكَ آيَةً لِلنَّاسِ وَانْظُرْ إِلَى الْعِظَامِ كَيْفَ نُنْشِرُهَا ثُمَّ نَكْسُوهَا لَحْماً فَلَمَّا تَبَيَّنَ لَهُ قَالَ أَعْلَمُ أَنَّ اللهَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٩/٢].
Part Three: The First Chapter: The Sense. 1- God's subjugation of the universe for man, and there are many verses in this regard, perhaps the most prominent of which is His saying: 'It is Allah who created the heavens and the earth and sent down from the sky rain and brought forth thereby fruits as provision for you. And He subjected for you the ships to sail through the sea by His command, and He subjected for you the rivers. And He subjected for you the sun and the moon, both constantly pursuing their courses, and He subjected for you the night and the day.' [Ibrahim 14:32-33]. 2- The realistic presentation of the state of the universe, where the universe is presented before man in its moving form: 'And you see the earth barren, but when We send down upon it rain, it quivers and swells and grows of every beautiful kind.' [Al-Hajj 22:5]. 'And the sun runs on to a term determined for it; that is the determination of the Exalted in Might, the Knowing. And the moon – We have determined for it phases until it returns like the old dried curved date stalk. It is not for the sun to overtake the moon, nor does the night outstrip the day. And all float in an orbit.' [Ya-Sin 36:38-40]. The effectiveness of man: that is, God Almighty urges man to use his senses and intellect through the verses that speak about the universe and conclude with His saying: 'Indeed in that are signs for a people who use reason... who reflect... who understand.' Rather, the verses of the Noble Quran make the practical task of man to be his active role in the universe and life: 'Say, travel through the land' [Al-An'am 6:11], 'and walk among its slopes' [Al-Mulk 67:15], 'and eat from what Allah has provided for you [as] lawful and good' [An-Nahl 16:114], 'and He has produced you from the earth and settled you in it' [Hud 11:61]. Teaching the method of empirical research, and that is in the Quran's indications of regularity and causality between events and the issue of quantities and measures (counting, weighing, and enumeration) in its mentioning of various events: 'And Allah determines the night and the day' [Al-Muzzammil 73:20], and 'And We have made the night and the day two signs, and We erased the sign of the night and made the sign of the day giving sight that you may seek bounty from your Lord and that you may know the number of years and the account. And We have detailed everything in detail.' [Al-Isra' 17:12]. It also indicated the idea of classification, which today is one of the rules of the empirical method: 'And Allah has created every living creature from water. And of them are those that move on their bellies, and of them are those that move on two legs, and of them are those that move on four. Allah creates what He wills.' [An-Nur 24:45]. The Noble Quran gives significant attention to the empirical approach, as it draws attention to the importance of using it through some indications aimed at conveying this meaning. It called for the use of the sensory observation tool to note the changes that occur, and to penetrate from them to infer the power of God Almighty to revive bodies after their annihilation, confirming what we indicated earlier of the allusion to the importance of the pre- and post-tests affected by the variables that occur, and that is the form of the methodological path that leads to the eschatological truth: 'Or like the one who passed by a town that had collapsed on its foundations and said, 'How will Allah bring this to life after its death?' So Allah caused him to die for a hundred years; then He revived him and said, 'How long have you remained?' He said, 'I have remained a day or part of a day.' He said, 'Rather, you have remained a hundred years. Look at your food and your drink; it has not changed. And look at your donkey; and We will make you a sign for the people. And look at the bones, how We raise them and then We cover them with flesh.' And when it became clear to him, he said, 'I know that Allah is over all things competent.' ' [Al-Baqarah 2:259].
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion about the Quran's emphasis on sensory experience and empirical methodology. The author begins by stating that this chapter is about 'the sense' (الحس), then presents three main points: (1) God's subjugation of the universe for mankind, citing Quranic verses that list how God has subjected celestial bodies, seas, rivers, and day and night for human benefit. (2) The realistic presentation of the universe in motion, showing the alternation of day and night, the phases of the moon, and the cycle of seasons, all of which invite reflection. (3) The effectiveness of man, meaning that God urges humans to use their senses and intellect through verses that call for reasoning, reflecting, and understanding. Then the author discusses how the Quran teaches the empirical research method through references to regularity and causality, measurement and counting, and classification. The author emphasizes that the Quran calls for using sensory observation to note changes and infer God's power, as exemplified in the story of the man who passed by a ruined town and witnessed resurrection. The commentary should follow the author's order: first the three points, then the empirical method, and finally the example. It explains that the Quran is not just a book of spiritual guidance but also a call to observe the natural world using the senses, forming a foundation for empirical science.

Method of Learning
beginner
5 min
The Quranic Experiment: Pre/Post-Test in the Story of the Man
Author uses Quran 2:259 to illustrate pre/post-test observation in empirical methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the elements of a pre/post-test experimental design in the Quranic story of the man (Q 2:259) and explain how it demonstrates empirical verification.

Core Idea
The Quran uses the story of a man's death and resurrection as a controlled experiment to teach empirical methodology.

The Quran not only commands belief in resurrection but provides a detailed narrative that functions as a scientific demonstration. The story of the man who passed by a ruined town illustrates the principles of observation, constancy of variables, and cause-and-effect reasoning. Let's unpack this Quranic lesson in empirical inquiry.

Guided Path
1
Identify the event
Read the verse (Q 2:259) and identify the initial state of the town (ruined) and the man's question about how Allah will revive it.
2
Distinguish pre-test and post-test
Note the 'pre-test' state: the man's death for 100 years, the food and drink unchanged, the donkey dead, the bones scattered. The 'post-test' state: after resurrection, the food and drink remain unchanged, but the bones are reassembled and clothed with flesh.
This is a controlled experiment where some variables (food, drink) are constant and the key variable (the body) changes.
3
Recognize the variables
Identify which elements are held constant (food, drink, donkey's location) and which are manipulated (the bones). The constancy of the food and drink shows that time did not affect them, while the bones being revived demonstrates Allah's power.
4
Understand the conclusion
The man's certainty ('I know that Allah is over all things competent') results from direct sensory observation of the experimental outcome.
This mirrors the empirical method where observation leads to conclusion.

Source Text

الباب الثالث: الفصل الأول - الحس
تعليم منهج البحث التجريبي وذلك في إشارات القرآن الكريم إلى الاطّراد والسببية بين الحوادث ومسألة الكميات والمقادير العـد والوزن والإحصاء) في ذكره للحوادث المختلفة وَاللهُ يُقَدِّرُ اللَّيْلَ وَالنَّهار المزمل: ۲۰/۷۳]، و ﴿وَجَعَلْنَا اللَّيْلَ وَالنَّهارَ آيَتَيْنِ فَمَحَوْنَا آيَةَ اللَّيْلِ وَجَعَلْنَا آيَةَ النَّهارِ مُبْصِرَةً لِتَبْتَغُوا فَضْلاً مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ وَلَتَعْلَمُوا عَدَدَ السِّنِينَ وَالْحِسَابَ وَكُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَصَّلْنَاهُ تَفْصِيلا) [الإسراء: ۱۲/۱۷].
- وكذلك أشار إلى فكرة التصنيف، والتي تعدّ اليوم إحدى قواعد المنهج التجريبي:
﴿ وَاللهُ خَلَقَ كُلَّ دابَّةٍ مِنْ مَاء فَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ يَمْشِي عَلَى بَطْنِهِ وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ يَمْشِي عَلَى رِجْلَيْنِ وَمِنْهُمْ مَنْ يَمْشِي عَلَى أَرْبَعٍ يَخْلُقُ اللهُ مَا يَشَاءُ) [النور: ١٤٥/٢٤). إن القرآن الكريم يولي النهج التجريبي اهتماماً ملحوظاً، فهو يلفت النظر إلى أهمية استخدامه من خلال بعض الإشارات الرامية إلى توصيل هذا المدلول. فقد دعا إلى استخدام أداة النظر الحسيّة لملاحظة التغيرات الطارئة، والنفاذ منها إلى الاستدلال على قدرة الله تعالى على إحياء الأجسام بعد فنائها بما يؤكـد مـا أشرنا إليه سابقاً من الإيماء إلى أهمية الاختبارين القبلي والبعــدي المتأثرين بالمتغيرات الطارئة وتلك هي صورة الشكل المنهجي الموصل إلى الحقيقة الأخروية: أَوْ كَالَّذِي مَرَّ عَلَى قَرْيَةٍ وَهِيَ حَاوِيَةٌ عَلَى عُرُوشِهَا قَالَ أَنَّى يُحْيِي هَذِهِ اللَّهُ بَعْدَ مَوْتِها فَأَمَاتَهُ اللهُ مِئَةَ عامٍ ثُمَّ بَعَثَهُ قالَ كَمْ لَبِثْتَ قَالَ لَبِثْتُ يَوْماً أَوْ بَعْضٍ يَوْمٍ قَالَ بَلْ لَبِثْتَ مِئَةَ عامٍ فَانظُرْ إِلَى طَعَامِكَ وَشَرابِكَ لَمْ يَتَسَنَّهُ وَانْظُرْ إِلَى حِمارِكَ وَلَنَجْعَلَكَ آيَةً لِلنَّاسِ وَانْظُرْ إِلَى الْعِظامِ كَيْفَ تُنشرها ثُمَّ نَكْسُوه لَحْماً فَلَمَّا تَبَيَّنَ لَهُ قالَ أَعْلَمُ أَنَّ اللهَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٩/٢]. (۱) الزنيدي، مرجع سابق، ٥٠٥-٥١٠.

ثم يذكر: وجاء الرد على سؤال إبراهيم عن كيفية إحياء الموتى حسياً تجريبياً قائماً على التجربة والملاحظة:
﴿وَإِذْ قالَ إِبْرَاهِيمُ رَبِّ أَرِنِي كَيْفَ تُحْيِي الْمَوْتَى قَالَ أَوَلَمْ تُؤْمِنْ قَالَ بَلَى وَلَكِنْ لِيَطْمَئِنَّ قَلْبي قالَ فَخُذْ أَرْبَعَةً مِنَ الطَّيْرِ فَصُرْهُنَّ إِلَيْكَ ثُمَّ اجْعَلْ عَلَى كُلِّ ا جَبَلٍ مِنْهُنَّ جُزْءاً ثُمَّ ادْعُهُنَّ يَأْتِيَنَكَ سَعْيَا وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ اللَّهَ عَزِيزٌ حَكِيمٌ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٦٠/٢]. ويشير أحد الباحثين إلى أن السؤال عن معرفة الكيفيات (know-how-كما سبق عند إبراهيم- يمثل حقيقة تجريبية يمكن الاعتماد عليها في توظيف إنتاج المعرفة الكيفية(1). ويمكن الإفادة من ذلك أيضاً في تنمية التربية التساؤلية لدى المتعلم، لينتقل من طور التلقين بصورة تحمل قدراً من السلبية إلى طور أفضل فيه من التفاعل الإيجابي ما يدفع به إلى القيام بعملية الاختبار التجريبي، ومن ثم الحصول على المعرفة واكتشاف نتائجها بمفرده، وذلك ضرب من ضروب التعلم الذاتي. ونجد في قصد هداية إبراهيم عليه السلام - لمعرفة الخالق - جل وعلا - استخدام إبراهيم لخطوات المنهج العلمي، الذي بدأ من الإحساس بوجود مشكلة قائمة في الواقع، وهي ضرورة وجود خالق للوجود ، ثم حدّدها بمشكلة الضلال والخرافة التي وقع فيها أبوه وقومه، وانتقل إلى وضع فرضيات لخالق الوجود، وفحصها واحدة بعد الأخرى، عن طريق الأداة الكلية هنا وهي الحس (البصر) وحينما توصل إلى بطلان كل تلك الفرضيات، انتقل إلى فرضية رابعة وهي ضرورة وجود خالق لهذا الوجود، ليس كمثله شيء، فتحققت سلامة هذه الفرضية وحصل اليقين العلمي.
وبذلك يكون تدرج عبر خطوات خمس هي خطوات البحث العلمي التجريبي، وقد تقدّم على النحو التالي:
(1) أحمد المهدي عبد الحليم نحو صيغة إسلامية للبحث الاجتماعي والتربوي، ۳۸.
Chapter Three: Section One - Sense. Teaching the empirical research method as indicated in the noble Quran's references to consistency and causality between events, and the issue of quantities and measurements (counting, weighing, and enumeration) in its mention of various events: 'And Allah determines the night and day' [73:20], and 'And We made the night and day two signs, then We erased the sign of night and made the sign of day giving sight, that you may seek bounty from your Lord and that you may know the number of years and the account, and We have detailed everything in detail' [17:12]. And it also indicated the idea of classification, which today is considered one of the bases of the empirical method: 'And Allah created every animal from water; among them are those that walk on their bellies, and among them are those that walk on two legs, and among them are those that walk on four. Allah creates what He wills' [24:45]. Indeed, the noble Quran gives notable attention to the empirical approach; it draws attention to the importance of its use through some indications aimed at conveying this meaning. It called for the use of the tool of sensory observation to note occurring changes, and to penetrate from them to infer the ability of Allah Almighty to revive bodies after their destruction, confirming what we previously indicated about hinting at the importance of pre- and post-tests affected by occurring variables. That is the image of the methodological form leading to the eschatological truth: 'Or like he who passed by a town while it was collapsed on its roofs. And look at the bones how We raise them, then We clothe them with flesh. So when it became clear to him, he said: I know that Allah is over all things competent' [2:259]. Then he mentions: And the response to Ibrahim's question about how to revive the dead came sensibly empirically, based on experiment and observation: 'And when Ibrahim said: My Lord, show me how You give life to the dead. And we find in the purpose of guiding Ibrahim, peace be upon him – to know the Creator – Almighty and Majestic – that Ibrahim used the steps of the scientific method, which began from sensing the existence of a problem existing in reality, which is the necessity of a creator for existence. And when he reached the invalidity of all those hypotheses, he moved to a fourth hypothesis: the necessity of a creator for this existence, nothing like Him, so the soundness of this hypothesis was verified, and scientific certainty was obtained. Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is an extended explanation of how the Quran teaches the empirical method. The author begins by asserting that the Quran contains references to consistency and causality between events, as well as quantitative measures like counting and weighing, citing verses about the determination of night and day and the detailed enumeration of years. Next, the author points to the Quranic concept of classification, using the example of animals walking on different numbers of limbs. This, the author argues, is a foundational principle of the empirical method. The main thrust of the passage is to demonstrate that the Quran explicitly encourages sensory observation to infer divine power, especially regarding resurrection. Two key Quranic stories are analyzed. The first story (Quran 2:259) involves a man who passed by a ruined town and questioned how Allah could revive it; Allah caused him to die for a hundred years and then resurrected him, showing him the bones being reassembled and clothed with flesh. The author interprets this as an example of pre- and post-test observation, a core feature of the experimental method. The second story (Quran 2:260) is that of Prophet Ibrahim, who asked to see how Allah gives life to the dead. Allah instructed him to take four birds, cut and place them on separate mountains, then call them; the birds came to him. The author describes this as an empirical experiment based on observation. Furthermore, the author notes that Ibrahim's broader quest for the Creator followed a structured scientific method: sensing a problem (the need for a true Creator), defining the problem (the misguidance of his people), formulating hypotheses (about celestial bodies), testing each via sensory observation (sight), rejecting false hypotheses, and finally arriving at the correct hypothesis (the existence of a unique Creator), resulting in certainty. The author concludes that this sequence constitutes the five steps of empirical scientific research. The passage serves to argue that the Quran not only permits but actively promotes empirical investigation as a path to knowledge and certainty.

Method of Learning
intermediate

Ibrahim's Five-Step Scientific Method: Hypothesis Testing in the Quran
Author extracts five steps of empirical scientific research from Ibrahim's search for the Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the five steps of the scientific method as derived from Prophet Ibrahim's search for the Creator and apply them to evaluate other Quranic arguments.

Core Idea
Ibrahim's journey from doubt to certainty models the scientific method: problem, hypothesis, testing, rejection, and confirmation.

The Quran presents Prophet Ibrahim as a model of rational inquiry. His quest to understand the Creator follows a clear methodological path: sensing a problem, forming hypotheses, testing them through sensory observation, rejecting false ones, and arriving at certainty. This mirrors the modern empirical research process, as highlighted by the author.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Ibrahim sensed a problem: his people worshipped celestial bodies, but these are transient. He realized the need for a true Creator.
The problem is the existence of false gods and the necessity of a real deity.
2
List the hypotheses
Ibrahim considered three hypotheses: the Creator is the star, the moon, or the sun. He tested each by observing their movement and disappearance.
The universal tool is sensory observation (sight).
3
Testing and rejection
Each celestial body set or disappeared, showing they are not eternal or all-powerful. Ibrahim rejected each hypothesis as invalid.
The rejection is based on empirical observation: 'I do not like those that set.'
4
Formulate the validated hypothesis
After rejecting the false ones, Ibrahim hypothesised a Creator who does not set, is unlike anything, and is the cause of all existence.
This hypothesis is confirmed through reason and the evidence of creation.
5
Achieve certainty
Ibrahim attains al-yaqin al-ilmi (scientific certainty) through this process, as the author states: 'so the soundness of this hypothesis was verified, and scientific certainty was obtained.'

Commentary
This passage is an extended explanation of how the Quran teaches the empirical method. The author begins by asserting that the Quran contains references to consistency and causality between events, as well as quantitative measures like counting and weighing, citing verses about the determination of night and day and the detailed enumeration of years. Next, the author points to the Quranic concept of classification, using the example of animals walking on different numbers of limbs. This, the author argues, is a foundational principle of the empirical method. The main thrust of the passage is to demonstrate that the Quran explicitly encourages sensory observation to infer divine power, especially regarding resurrection. Two key Quranic stories are analyzed. The first story (Quran 2:259) involves a man who passed by a ruined town and questioned how Allah could revive it; Allah caused him to die for a hundred years and then resurrected him, showing him the bones being reassembled and clothed with flesh. The author interprets this as an example of pre- and post-test observation, a core feature of the experimental method. The second story (Quran 2:260) is that of Prophet Ibrahim, who asked to see how Allah gives life to the dead. Allah instructed him to take four birds, cut and place them on separate mountains, then call them; the birds came to him. The author describes this as an empirical experiment based on observation. Furthermore, the author notes that Ibrahim's broader quest for the Creator followed a structured scientific method: sensing a problem (the need for a true Creator), defining the problem (the misguidance of his people), formulating hypotheses (about celestial bodies), testing each via sensory observation (sight), rejecting false hypotheses, and finally arriving at the correct hypothesis (the existence of a unique Creator), resulting in certainty. The author concludes that this sequence constitutes the five steps of empirical scientific research. The passage serves to argue that the Quran not only permits but actively promotes empirical investigation as a path to knowledge and certainty.

Limitations of the Experimental Method in Islamic Epistemology
Author critiques experimental method and lists five limitations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the five limitations of the experimental method as presented in the passage, and contrast them with the Islamic epistemological framework.

Core Idea
The experimental method is powerful but limited; Islamic epistemology embraces multiple sources, including revelation.

This passage critically examines the experimental method from an Islamic perspective. The author argues that sense perception is relative, not absolute, and then lists five specific limitations of the experimental method. This critique helps us understand why Islamic epistemology does not rely solely on empiricism but incorporates revelation and other sources. The discussion highlights the moderation of Islamic thought compared to Western pragmatism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's target
The author targets the experimental method as used by Western pragmatism, which treats sense perception as the primary or only source of knowledge. What is the author's fundamental objection?
The objection is not that the method is useless, but that it is limited in scope.
2
Understand the basis: relativity of senses
The author starts by asserting that sense perception is relative, not providing absolute certainty. This is the epistemological foundation for the limitations. How does this contrast with the Western view?
In Islamic thought, sensory knowledge varies in certainty, starting from certainty and ending with weak conjecture.
3
List the five limitations
The passage enumerates five specific limitations. Work through each one: (1) only material observable phenomena; (2) must be reproducible; (3) unknown elements remain hypotheses; (4) cannot study past social events; (5) distinguishes speculation from genuine science.
Pay attention to the ordering and the examples given.
4
Connect to Islamic science
For each limitation, think of an example from Islamic sciences where the experimental method is inadequate. For instance, the nature of the soul (point 3) or the study of prophetic miracles (point 1).
These examples will help you internalize why Islamic epistemology is broader.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باستحالة وجوده في الخارج. وما ذلك إلا استنباط شيء من شيء، وهذا يخالف مذهب الحسيين أنفسهم (1). وإذا تأكدت لنا هذه النسبية فإن التربية الإسلامية لا ترى في مصدرية الحس وطريقتها درجة القطع واليقين والإطلاق، بحيث إن أي معرفة يحتوي عليها منهجها معتمداً على الحس ليست على مستوى واحد من هذه الزاوية. فهو يبدأ من اليقين، وينتهي بالظن المرجوح كما أشرنا سلفاً. ومن هنا يبرز الفرق الجوهري بين فلسفة التربية الإسلامية والفكر التربوي الغربي المتمثل في (البراجماتية) غالباً حيث جعلت الأولى الحس واحداً من المصادر الرئيسة لا أنه المصدر الرئيس - إن لم يكن الوحيد لدى بعض غلاة الفكر التربوي الغربي. وهذا الاعتدال في فلسفة التربية الإسلامية يدلل على سعة الأفق، وامتلاك المقدرة لديها على استيعاب المصادر والطرائق الأخرى، ويجعل - من ثَمّ - من حكمها على الظواهر المختلفة، ومن النتائج التي تنتهي إليها أكثر موضوعية وانسجاماً مع المنهج العلمي الدقيق المنبثق من التصور الإسلامي للإنسان والكون والحياة، وليس المنهج العلمي الغربي المتسم بأحادية النظرة والمتأثر برد الفعل الجامح إزاء التيار العقلي. ومن جانب آخر فإن نسبية الحواس التي تؤمن بها فلسفة التربية الإسلامية تكسبها موضوعية في تعاملها مع الحس والتجريب، رغم النشأة الإسلامية للمنهج التجريبي. ذلك أن هذا المنهج يتسم بجملة سمات من خلالها يتبين أوجه الخلاف بينه وبين المنهج الديني:
١ - لا يصلح المنهج التجريبي إلا لدراسة الماديات الكائنة تحت الحس هنا فما لا يخضع للمشاهدة مع الملاحظة، كأمور الغيب لا يمكن البشري، ومن أن يصلح معها هذا المنهج.
٢- يجب أن تكون الظاهرة قابلة للتحضير معملياً - وليس مادياً أو محسوساً فقط - أو بتكررها طبيعياً ليتمكن الباحث من إخضاع الظاهرة لشروط التجربة، والتي تعني توافر عوامل الزمان والمكان والكيفيات والأحوال التي يستلزمها تحقيق الفرض في المعمل أو مراقبتها في الطبيعة عبر الأزمنة والأمكنة المختلفة وبحسب القياس الكمي والوصف الكمي والوصف النوعي.
-۳- نظراً لشرط ضبط متغيرات الظاهرة المشار إليها في (٢) فإن الأشياء المجهولة لبعض العناصر أو كلها تظل فروضاً ذهنية مفسرة لبعض الظواهر الكونية في الفضاء الكوني. ومن باب أولى فإن دراسة النفس الإنسانية وفق هذا المنهج أمرٌ لا يستقيم بإطلاق، لأن النفس - في حقيقتها - من جنس قضايا الغيب.
٤- لا يمكن استخدام المنهج التجريبي كذلك في دراسة الأحداث والظواهر الاجتماعية الغابرة، ذلك لأنها لم تتكرر ، مما يحول دون إخضاعها للتجربة.
٥- هناك فرق بين حالتين في المنهج التجريبي: الحالة الأولى: كون الباحث مفكراً ومخمناً ومفترضاً ومتحيلاً ومتأملاً. والحالة الأخرى كون الباحث عالماً لأنه قد انتقل من التفكير والتخمين إلى التفسير الصحيح للظاهرة (١).
By the impossibility of its existence in the external world. And that is nothing but deducing something from something else, and this contradicts the doctrine of the sensualists themselves (1). And if this relativity is established for us, then Islamic education does not see in the sensory source and its method a degree of certainty, conviction, and absoluteness, such that any knowledge contained in its method based on the senses is not on one level from this angle. It begins with certainty and ends with weak conjecture as we indicated previously. From here emerges the essential difference between the philosophy of Islamic education and Western educational thought represented mainly by (Pragmatism), where the former made the senses one of the main sources, not the main source - if not the only one among some extremists of Western educational thought. This moderation in the philosophy of Islamic education demonstrates its breadth of horizon, its possession of the ability to accommodate other sources and methods, and consequently makes its judgments on various phenomena and the results it reaches more objective and in harmony with the precise scientific method emanating from the Islamic conception of man, the universe, and life - not the Western scientific method characterized by a monocular view and influenced by an unbridled reaction against intellectualism. On the other hand, the relativity of the senses believed in by the philosophy of Islamic education gives it objectivity in dealing with sense and experimentation, despite the Islamic origin of the experimental method. That is because this method is characterized by a set of features through which the aspects of difference between it and the religious method become clear: 1- The experimental method is only suitable for studying material things under the sense here, so what is not subject to observation and notice, such as matters of the unseen, humans cannot, and this method cannot be suitable with them. 2- The phenomenon must be capable of laboratory preparation - not just material or sensory - or by its natural repetition so that the researcher can subject the phenomenon to the conditions of the experiment, which means the availability of factors of time, place, qualities, and circumstances required to achieve the hypothesis in the laboratory or monitor it in nature across different times and places and according to quantitative measurement and quantitative description and qualitative description. 3- Due to the condition of controlling the variables of the phenomenon referred to in (2), things unknown in some or all of their elements remain mental hypotheses explaining some cosmic phenomena in the cosmic space. A fortiori, the study of the human soul according to this method is absolutely not sound, because the soul - in its reality - is of the kind of matters of the unseen. 4- The experimental method cannot be used also in studying past social events and phenomena, because they did not repeat, which prevents subjecting them to experiment. 5- There is a difference between two states in the experimental method: the first state: the researcher being a thinker, guesser, supposer, contriver, and contemplator. And the other state: the researcher being a scientist because he has moved from thinking and guessing to the correct interpretation of the phenomenon (1).
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage critically examines the experimental method from an Islamic epistemological perspective. The author begins by asserting the relativity of sense perception, which is the basis for the Islamic view that sensory knowledge is not absolute but varies in certainty. He contrasts this with Western pragmatism, which often treats the senses as the sole source of knowledge. The Islamic position is moderate, incorporating other sources and methods, leading to more objective judgments. The author then lists five limitations of the experimental method. First, it only applies to material, observable phenomena, not the unseen. Second, the phenomenon must be reproducible in a lab or naturally. Third, unknown variables remain hypotheses, and the human soul cannot be studied this way. Fourth, past social events cannot be repeated and thus not experimented on. Fifth, there is a distinction between being a speculator and a scientist who provides correct explanations. These points illustrate the author's critique of the empirical method's scope and its incompatibility with religious methodology in certain domains.

Key Terms
الحس
النسبية
المنهج التجريبي
المنهج الديني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the experimental method unsuitable for studying the human soul?
A) Because the soul is material and observable.
B) Because the soul is from the unseen and cannot be subjected to laboratory conditions.
C) Because the soul is not quantifiable.
D) Because the soul does not repeat.

Key Takeaway
The experimental method, while useful for material and repeatable phenomena, cannot access the unseen, the soul, past events, or uncontrolled variables; Islamic epistemology supplements it with revelation.

Limitations of the Experimental Method in Islamic Epistemology
Author lists five conditions and limitations of the experimental method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five conditions/limitations of the experimental method as outlined by al-Dasouqi and evaluate their implications for Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
The experimental method cannot access the unseen or unique historical events, limiting its scope in Islamic knowledge.

This passage from al-Dasouqi's 'Islam and Experimental Science' clarifies the boundaries of the experimental method. While it is valuable for material, repeatable phenomena, it fails for metaphysical realities (ghayb), the human soul, and past social events. Understanding these limitations protects Islamic scholars from misapplying empirical methods to revealed knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five conditions/limitations
List each of the five points the author makes about the experimental method. These include the requirement of material observability, reproducibility, variable control, and the exclusion of ghayb and unique historical events.
2
Distinguish between material and spiritual
For each limitation, note whether it concerns materiality, reproducibility, control of variables, or the nature of the subject matter. The first point stresses that only material things under sense are suitable.
3
Apply the ghayb principle
Recognize that the soul and metaphysical realities are classified under al-ghayb, which is outside empirical observation. The author explicitly states the soul is 'of the genus of matters of the unseen'.
In Islamic theology, ghayb includes Allah, angels, the afterlife, etc.
4
Evaluate the criterion of reproducibility
Understand that unrepeatable historical events (like the Prophet's life) cannot be subjected to experiment. The author gives the example of past social events that did not recur.
5
Contrast the two researcher states
Differentiate between mere hypothesizing (thinker) and genuine scientific explanation (scientist) based on correct interpretation. The author emphasizes that moving from guessing to correct explanation defines true science.

Chapter Three: Section One - Sense
1. The experimental method is only suitable for studying material things that are under sense, so what is not subject to observation with note, like matters of the unseen, cannot be [studied] by humans, and it is not possible for this method to be suitable for it.
2. The phenomenon must be capable of being prepared in a laboratory - not just materially or sensibly - or by its natural repetition so that the researcher can subject the phenomenon to the conditions of experiment, which means the availability of factors of time, place, qualities, and conditions required to realize the hypothesis in the lab or to observe it in nature across different times and places according to quantitative measurement, quantitative description, and qualitative description.
3. Given the condition of controlling the variables of the phenomenon referred to in (2), things that are unknown in some or all of their elements remain mental hypotheses explaining some cosmic phenomena in outer space. A fortiori, the study of the human soul according to this method is absolutely not sound, because the soul - in its reality - is of the genus of matters of the unseen.
4. The experimental method also cannot be used in studying past social events and phenomena, because they did not recur, which prevents subjecting them to experiment.
5. There is a difference between two states in the experimental method:
The first state: the researcher is a thinker, guesser, hypothesizer, estimator, and contemplator. The other state: the researcher is a scientist because he has moved from thinking and guessing to the correct explanation of the phenomenon.
(1) Farouq al-Dasouqi, Islam and Experimental Science, 130-133.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage enumerates five conditions and limitations of the experimental method, arguing that it is not universally applicable. The author begins by stating that the experimental method is only suitable for studying material, observable things; matters of the unseen (ghayb), such as metaphysical realities, cannot be investigated through this method. Second, the phenomenon must be reproducible either in a laboratory or naturally, and the researcher must be able to control the variables of time, place, and conditions. Third, because unknown elements remain mere mental hypotheses, the study of the human soul—which is of the nature of the unseen—cannot be done experimentally. Fourth, past social events and phenomena are not repeatable, so experiment is impossible. Fifth, the author distinguishes between two states of the researcher: one who is only hypothesizing and guessing, and one who has arrived at a correct explanation, thus becoming a scientist. The examples illustrate that empirical investigation is limited to material, repeatable, observable phenomena, and cannot access the unseen or unique historical events.

التجربة
المشاهدة

C) Because the soul does not repeat itself naturally.
D) Because the soul is of the nature of the unseen (ghayb).

Key Takeaway
The experimental method is epistemologically limited to material, observable, repeatable phenomena and cannot access the unseen or unique historical events.

Analogical Reasoning (Qiyas) in Islamic Thought
Author introduces the importance of analogical reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the structure of analogical reasoning (qiyas) as described in the passage and apply it to a new case from fiqh.

Core Idea
Analogical reasoning compares a disputed case to an agreed case to reach a conclusion.

The author introduces qiyas as a method to reach rational conclusions by comparing a disputed matter to an agreed one. This lesson unpacks that process and its significance in Islamic sciences, especially usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Find the 'agreed-upon first' (أ) and the 'disputed second' (ب) in the passage. The first is the known ruling, the second is the new case.
2
Understand the comparison
The passage says we compare the second to the first to bring out aspects of greatness. In fiqh, this means identifying the 'illa (cause) that links them.
3
Derive the conclusion
The rational conclusion is reached 'by the primal method' (طريق الأولى). This means if the first has a ruling, the second deserves it even more due to greater need or clarity.
This is a higher-order analogy called qiyas al-awla.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن طريق مقارنة أو قياس الثانية المتنازع حولها على الأولى المتفق عليها، فتنتج أمامنا جوانب العظمة والإبداع في الثانية بما يفوق الأولى، فنصل إلى النتيجة العقلية بطريق الأولى. ومعلوم عند التربويين أن أزمة التربية العقلية المعروفة في بلادنا العربية والإسلامية تتمثل في تعطيل عقل المتعلم بسبب إقصاء المهارات العقلية المتقدمة عن حياته التعليمية والاكتفاء بالمهارات الدنيا: الحفظ والتذكر.
Through comparison or analogy of the disputed second to the agreed-upon first, we produce before us aspects of greatness and creativity in the second surpassing the first, so we reach the rational conclusion by the primal method. It is known among educators that the crisis of rational education in our Arab and Islamic countries is represented by the disabling of the learner's mind due to the exclusion of advanced mental skills from their educational life and limiting to lower skills: memorization and recall.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage discusses two points: first, the method of reasoning by analogy (qiyas) where a disputed matter is compared to an agreed one to derive a rational conclusion. Second, it notes the educational crisis where only lower-order skills like memorization are taught, neglecting higher reasoning. The author implies that Islamic education should cultivate reasoning skills.

Key Terms

عقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The first is seen as greater
B) Aspects of greatness in the second emerge
C) Both become equal
D) The second is rejected

Key Takeaway
Analogical reasoning in Islamic thought involves comparing a disputed case to an agreed case, often leading to a conclusion by priority (al-awla).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the passage's description of qiyas, outline how you would apply analogical reasoning to derive the ruling on a new financial transaction (like cryptocurrency) by comparing it to an established transaction like selling (bay').

The Crisis of Rational Education in the Muslim World
Author criticizes the neglect of higher mental skills in education.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the symptoms of the educational crisis as described in the passage and propose remedies based on Islamic principles of reasoning.

Core Idea
Neglecting higher reasoning in education disables the Muslim mind.

The passage points to a known crisis: education in many Arab and Islamic countries focuses only on lower skills like memorization, excluding advanced mental skills. This lesson analyzes that diagnosis and its implications for Islamic education.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two skill levels
The passage distinguishes between 'lower skills' (memorization and recall) and 'advanced mental skills' (reasoning, analysis, etc.).
2
Understand the disabling effect
The author says this exclusion 'disables the learner's mind' (تعطيل عقل المتعلم). Think about what that means for critical thinking.
3
Relate to Islamic education
Islamic sources emphasize tafakkur (reflection) and tadabbur (deliberation). The current crisis contradicts that ideal.
Consider Quranic verses that command reflection on nature and revelation.

Reasoning by Cosmic Signs in the Quran
Author explains how Quranic verses direct attention to cosmic phenomena as evidence for the Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how Quranic verses use cosmic phenomena as rational evidence for the Creator and explain the epistemological purpose.

Core Idea
The cosmos is a rational sign, not just emotional inspiration.

The Quran repeatedly calls attention to the natural world—the heavens, earth, water, and life—as evidence for the Creator. This lesson examines how these 'signs of the horizons' (ayat al-afaq) function as a rational method of reasoning (istidlal) that engages the mind, not merely the emotions. The passage shows that observing nature is meant to stimulate the intellect to reach the truth of Allah and to fulfill humanity's role as vicegerent.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Quranic verses cited
The author quotes three verses (21:30, 29:61-63, 41:39). Identify each verse and note what cosmic phenomenon it points to: the splitting of heavens and earth, creation and subjugation of sun/moon, sending rain and reviving the earth.
These verses are selected because they each present a clear natural observation that leads to a theological conclusion.
2
Extract the rational inference
For each verse, ask: what is the observable fact (sign), and what conclusion is drawn? For example, the revival of dead land after rain is a sign that the One who gives life to the earth can give life to the dead. This is an argument from analogy or sign-inference.
The inference is implicit in the Quranic structure: the sign points directly to Allah's power and existence.
3
Identify the purpose of reasoning
The author states the goal is to 'rouse the powers of the mind and its higher processes to reach the truth of the Creator of existence.' Note that the reasoning is not just intellectual—it leads to action: fulfilling the role of vicegerency (khalifah) in light of divine guidance.
This connects cognitive knowledge to practical responsibility.
4
Understand the educational framework
The passage calls the natural world a 'vast laboratory' (mukhtabar) for applying educational objectives: cognitive, affective, and psychomotor. Realize that the cosmic signs serve a holistic educational purpose within an Islamic worldview.
This frames science and observation as part of faith-based education.
5
Contrast with skepticism
The author notes that even disbelievers acknowledge Allah as the creator when asked (Quran 29:61-63), yet they still turn away. This highlights that reasoning from signs is available to all, but acceptance requires further will and reflection.
This addresses a common misunderstanding that the signs are only for believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
- الاستدلال بآيات الآفاق
ويلاحظ ذلك في كثير من مظاهر الكون الطبيعي والهدف منه استنفار قوى العقل وعملياته العليا كي تصل إلى حقيقة خالق الوجود، فيسارع الإنسان إلى القيام بدوره في الاستخلاف في ضوء هداية الخالق وتوجيهاته بما يحقق الفلسفة التربوية المؤمنة، ومن ذلك:
اوَلَمْ يَرَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا أَنَّ السَّماواتِ وَالْأَرْضَ كَانَتَا رَتْقًا فَفَتَقْنَاهُما وَجَعَلْنا مِنَ الْماءِ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ حَيٍّ أَفَلا يُؤْمِنُونَ ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٣٠/٢١].
وَلَئِنْ سَأَلْتَهُمْ مَنْ خَلَقَ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ وَسَحْرَ الشَّمْسَ وَالْقَمَرَ لَيَقُولُنَّ اللهُ فَأَنَّى يُؤفَكُونَ اللَّهُ يَبْسُطُ الرِّزْقَ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ مِنْ عِبَادِهِ وَيَقْدِرُ لَهُ إِنَّ اللَّهَ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ، وَلَئِن سَأَلْتَهُمْ مَنْ نَزَّلَ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً فَأَحْيَا بِهِ الْأَرْضَ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَوْتِها لَيَقُولُنَّ اللَّهُ قُلِ الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ بَلْ أَكْثَرُهُمْ لَا يَعْقِلُونَ﴾ (العنكبوت: ٦١/٢٩ - ٦٣]. ﴿وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ أَنَّكَ تَرَى الْأَرْضَ خَاشِعَةً فَإِذا أَنْزَلْنَا عَلَيْهَا الْمَاءَ اهْتَزَّتْ وَرَبَتْ إِنَّ الَّذِي أَحْيَاهَا لَمُحْيِي الْمَوْتَى إِنَّهُ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ) (فصلت: ٣٩/٤١). إن ذاك يجعل من ميدان الآفاق مختبراً ضخماً لتطبيق الأهداف التعليمية المتنوعة : المعرفية والوجدانية و المهارية في إطار الفلسفة التربوية المؤمنة، وتقويم مدى تحققها من خلاله فيما يتصل بالدراسات الطبيعية والكونية.
Reasoning by signs of the horizons: And this is observed in many manifestations of the natural universe, and the goal is to rouse the powers of the mind and its higher processes to reach the truth of the Creator of existence, so that man hastens to fulfill his role as vicegerent in light of the Creator's guidance and directions, achieving the believing educational philosophy. And from that: 'Do not the disbelievers see that the heavens and the earth were a joined entity, and We split them apart, and We made from water every living thing? Then will they not believe?' [Quran 21:30]. 'And if you ask them who created the heavens and the earth and subjected the sun and the moon, they will surely say, 'Allah.' So how are they deluded? Allah extends provision to whom He wills of His servants and restricts it. Indeed Allah is of all things Knowing. And if you ask them who sends down rain from the sky and revives thereby the earth after its death, they will surely say, 'Allah.' Say, 'Praise be to Allah.' But most of them do not reason.' [Quran 29:61-63]. 'And among His signs is that you see the earth barren, but when We send down upon it rain, it quivers and grows. Indeed, He who gives it life is the Giver of life to the dead. Indeed, He is over all things competent.' [Quran 41:39]. That makes the field of the horizons a vast laboratory for applying diverse educational objectives: cognitive, affective, and psychomotor within the framework of the believing educational philosophy, and evaluating the extent of their achievement through it in relation to natural and cosmic studies.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage presents the first method of Quranic reasoning: looking at cosmic signs. It cites several verses that call for reflection on the creation of the heavens and earth, the water cycle, and the revival of dead land. The author explains that these observations are intended to stimulate the mind to know the Creator and to fulfill the role of vicegerency. Moreover, the natural world becomes a laboratory for educational goals.

Key Terms

Key Takeaway
Quranic cosmic signs are rational evidence designed to engage the intellect, leading to knowledge of Allah and active vicegerency.

Method of Learning
beginner

The Method of Reasoning by Signs Within the Self (Ayat al-Anfus)
Author discusses how Quranic verses about human creation and development serve as signs for reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic method of reasoning from internal human signs (ayat al-anfus) and compare it to reasoning from external signs (ayat al-afaq).

Core Idea
The human self is a laboratory for divine signs; reasoning from it mirrors reasoning from the cosmos.

This lesson explores how the Quran uses the human self as a source of signs (ayat) that lead to knowledge of God and resurrection. We will examine the verses cited and the reasoning structure they imply, and see how this method extends to educational and social sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic method described
Read the first sentence: the Quran aims to 'rouse the mind and its higher processes' (استنفار العقل وعملياته العليا) to know the reality of man and his destiny. This is a call to use reason on internal human phenomena.
The method is deliberate and goal-oriented: it seeks knowledge through reflection on the self.
2
Extract the verses and their implicit reasoning
The passage cites two sets of verses: one on aging (Q 36:68) and another on human development from a drop to a fully formed being, ending with the question of resurrection (Q 75:36-40). Notice how the verses move from observed facts (creation) to a conclusion (power to resurrect).
This is a form of analogical reasoning: if God created man from a drop, He can recreate him.
3
Recognize the comparison to reasoning by horizons
The author explicitly says reasoning by signs of the selves is like reasoning by signs of the horizons. Both involve observing God's signs in creation to draw conclusions. The difference is the subject: internal vs external.
This parallel is important for Islamic epistemology: both sources of knowledge are valid and complementary.
4
Understand the application to human and social sciences
The passage states that the human soul is like a 'vast laboratory' for educational objectives. This means that studying human psychology, development, and society can be done through the lens of Quranic signs, evaluating how teachings are realized in humans.
This opens up a methodology for Islamic social sciences based on self-reflection and Quranic guidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاستدلال بآيات الأنفس: ويهدف القرآن من وراء ذلك إلى استنفار العقل وعملياته العليا لمعرفة حقيقة الإنسان ومصيره في ضوء إرشادات الخلق وهدايته سبحانه، ومن هذه الآيات: وَمَنْ نُعَمِّرْهُ نُنَكِّسْهُ فِي الْخَلْقِ أَفَلَا يَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [يس: ٦٨/٣٦]. أَيَحْسَبُ الإِنسانُ أَن يُتْرَكَ سُدَى، أَلَمْ يَكُ نُطْفَةٌ مِنْ مَنِي يُمْنَى، ثُمَّ كَانَ عَلَقَةً فَخَلَقَ فَسَوَّى فَجَعَلَ مِنْهُ الزَّوْجَيْنِ الذَّكَرَ وَالْأُنْثَى، أَلَيْسَ ذَلِكَ بِقَادِرٍ عَلَى أَن يُحْيِيَ الْمَوْتَى [القيامة: ٣٦/٧٥-٤٠] وعلاوة على الفلسفة المؤمنة التي تنضح بها هذه الآيات فإن الاستدلال بآيات الأنفس كالاستدلال بآيات الآفاق من حيث إن النفس الإنسانية أشبه بمختبر هائل لتطبيق الأهداف التعليمية المختلفة، و تقويم تحققها من خلالها، ولكن فيما يتصل بالدراسات الإنسانية و الاجتماعية ومنها التربوية.
Reasoning by signs of the selves: The Quran aims thereby to rouse the mind and its higher processes to know the reality of man and his destiny in light of the Creator's guidance and His directions. And from these verses: 'And whoever We grant long life, We reverse him in creation. Then will they not reason?' [Quran 36:68]. 'Does man think that he will be left uncontrolled? Was he not a drop of emitted semen? Then he was a clinging clot, and [Allah] created and proportioned [him], and made of him two mates, the male and the female. Is not that [Creator] able to give life to the dead?' [Quran 75:36-40]. Moreover, besides the believing philosophy that these verses exude, reasoning by signs of the selves is like reasoning by signs of the horizons in that the human soul is like a vast laboratory for applying various educational objectives and evaluating their achievement through it, but in relation to human and social studies, including educational ones.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage presents the second method: reasoning by signs within the human self. It cites verses about aging and human development from a drop of fluid to a fully formed human, culminating in the question of resurrection. The author notes that just as the universe is a laboratory, so is the human soul a laboratory for educational goals, particularly in human and social sciences.

Key Terms
آيات الأنفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The diversity of languages
D) The cycles of the moon

Key Takeaway
Reasoning by signs of the selves is a Quranic method that uses reflection on human creation and development to arrive at knowledge of God and the afterlife, and it parallels reasoning by external signs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Method of Learning
intermediate
