Reasoning by Signs in Both Horizons and Selves
Author presents Quranic verses that combine reasoning from both cosmic and human signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic method of combining two domains of signs (afaq and anfus) and explain its epistemological purpose.

Core Idea
Quran unites cosmic and human signs to compel rational certainty.

The Quran does not rely on mere emotional appeal; it repeatedly calls for intellectual engagement. In this lesson, we explore a powerful method where Allah combines signs from the outer universe (afaq) and the inner self (anfus) to provoke the highest level of rational reflection. Understanding this method sharpens your ability to appreciate the Quran's argumentative structure and its appeal to reason.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Domains
Look at the verses cited (45:3-6 and 7:185). Identify which signs come from the 'horizons' (cosmos, heavens, earth) and which from the 'selves' (human creation, animals). Note the distinct groups addressed: believers, those who are certain, and those who reason.
The term 'ya'qilun' (they reason) is explicitly mentioned for the third set of signs.
2
Analyze the Combined Appeal
Recognize that the Quran presents signs from both domains together in a single argument. This is not a simple list but a cumulative proof. The combination eliminates excuses for disbelief because it covers all possible evidence.
The verse ends with a rhetorical question: 'Then in what statement after Allah and His verses will they believe?' emphasizing the sufficiency of these combined signs.
3
Determine the Epistemological Purpose
The author states the Quran aims to rouse the powers of the mind and its higher processes. The goal is certainty and conviction, not mere information. Reflect on how this method targets different levels of human cognition (belief, certainty, reasoning).
This aligns with the Islamic epistemological hierarchy: from belief (iman) to certainty (yaqin) to rational understanding (aql).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ه- الاستدلال بالأنفس والآفاق معاً: ويهدف القرآن من وراء ذلك إلى استنفار قوى العقل وعملياته العليا للبحث في ميداني الآفاق والأنفس معاً، وفي هذا جاء قوله تعالى: إِنَّ فِي السَّماواتِ وَالْأَرْضِ لَآيَاتِ لِلْمُؤْمِنِينَ، وَفِي خَلْقِكُمْ وَمَا يَبُثُّ مِنْ دابَّةٍ آيات لِقَوْمٍ يُوقِنُونَ، وَاخْتِلافِ اللَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَمَا أَنْزَلَ اللهُ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مِنْ رِزْقٍ فَأَحْيَا بِهِ الْأَرْضَ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَا وَتَصْرِيفِ الرِّياحِ آياتٌ لِقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ تِلْكَ آيَاتُ اللهِ نَتْلُوها عَلَيْكَ بِالْحَقِّ فَبِأَيِّ حَدِيثٍ بَعْدَ اللهِ وَآيَاتِهِ يُؤْمِنُونَ [الجاثية: ٣/٤٥-٦]. أَوَلَمْ يَنظُرُوا فِي مَلَكُوتِ السَّماواتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَمَا خَلَقَ اللَّهُ مِنْ شَيْءٍ وَأَن عَسَى أَن يَكُونَ قَدِ اقْتَرَبَ أَجَلُهُمْ فَبِأَيِّ حَدِيثٍ بَعْدَهُ يُؤْمِنُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ١٨٥/٧].
E. Reasoning by the selves and horizons together: The Quran aims thereby to rouse the powers of the mind and its higher processes to search in the fields of both horizons and selves together. In this, the Almighty says: 'Indeed, within the heavens and earth are signs for the believers. And in your creation and what He disperses of moving creatures are signs for people who are certain. And the alternation of night and day and what Allah sends down from the sky of provision and revives thereby the earth after its lifelessness and the directing of the winds are signs for people who reason. These are the verses of Allah which We recite to you in truth. Then in what statement after Allah and His verses will they believe?' [Quran 45:3-6]. 'Did they not look into the dominion of the heavens and the earth and everything that Allah has created, and that perhaps their term has already approached? So in what statement after it will they believe?' [Quran 7:185].
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This third method combines both afaq and anfus. The author cites two comprehensive verses that call for reflection on the universe, creation, animals, and the cycle of day and night, all as signs for those who reason. These verses emphasize that after such clear signs, there is no excuse for disbelief.

Key Terms
ملكوت

Key Takeaway
The Quran combines cosmic and human signs in a layered argument that moves from general belief to rational certainty, leaving no excuse for disbelief.

Method of Learning

The Quranic Liberation of Reason from Ancestral Authority
Author critiques ancestral adherence and presents the Quran's rational method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quran's method of rational critique against ancestral adherence as exemplified in the Abrahamic dialogues.

Core Idea
The Quran frees the intellect by challenging ancestral custom with rational dialogue, not mere rejection.

In this passage, the author argues that the Quran liberates the intellect from the tyranny of ancestral tradition by presenting Abraham's rational method. Instead of simply condemning idolatry, Abraham engages his people with logical questions. This lesson unpacks how that method works and why it matters for Islamic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of critique
Notice that the Quran criticizes blind adherence to ancestors (تقليد) as a shackle on the intellect. The passage begins by condemning those who call upon others besides Allah who cannot respond.
The target is not tradition itself but uncritical acceptance.
2
Extract the Quranic method
The Quran responds to ancestral adherence by presenting the Abrahamic method: rational dialogue. Abraham does not reject his father's beliefs without argument; he asks questions that expose their irrationality.
This method liberates the intellect from authority.
3
Analyze Abraham's argument
Examine the verses from Surah Ash-Shu'ara and Al-Anbiya. Abraham asks: Do the idols hear? Do they benefit or harm? When the people reply they follow their fathers, Abraham points out that both they and their fathers are in clear error. He then affirms tawhid based on creation, sustenance, and guidance.
The argument moves from questioning efficacy to rejecting inherited error to establishing monotheism.
4
Derive the epistemological principle
The author concludes that when a person cancels rational knowledge and depends solely on inherited legacy, the intellect becomes shackled. Guidance (هداية) depends on intellectual powers like thinking and reasoning.
Reason is the foundation for doctrinal and legislative guidance.
5
Apply to contemporary context
The problem of ancestralism is universal; even Muslims can fall into it if they imitate their fathers without insight. Islamic education must be disciplined by the brakes of the intellect.
This principle applies to all forms of blind following.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي موضع آخر:
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل
وَمَنْ أَضَلُّ مِمَّنْ يَدْعُو مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ مَنْ لا يَسْتَجِيبُ لَهُ إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَهُمْ عَنْ دُعَائِهِمْ غَافِلُونَ، وَإِذا حُشِرَ النَّاسُ كَانُوا لَهُمْ أَعْدَاءً وَكَانُوا بعِبادَتِهِمْ كَافِرِينَ ﴾ [الأحقاف: ٥/٤٦-٦].
وفي سبيل تحرير العقل من سلطان الآباء والعشيرة يورد القرآن المنهج الإبراهيمي، القائم على أسلوب الحوار العقلي، لكشف ما هم عليه ضلال من.
وبالمقابل فإن غرس قيمة التوحيد ما انفك ملازماً للحوار معهم: وَاتْلُ عَلَيْهِمْ نَبَا إِبْرَاهِيمَ إِذْ قالَ لأَبِيهِ وَقَوْمِهِ مَا تَعْبُدُونَ، قَالُوا نَعْبُدُ أَصْناماً فَنَظَلُّ لَها عاكِفِينَ ، قَالَ هَلْ يَسْمَعُونَكُمْ إِذْ تَدْعُونَ، أَوْ يَنْفَعُونَكُمْ أَوْ يَضُرُّونَ قالُوا بَلْ وَجَدْنَا آبَاءَنَا كَذَلِكَ يَفْعَلُونَ، قَالَ أَفَرَأَيْتُمْ مَا كُنتُمْ تَعْبُدُونَ، أَنتُمْ وَآبَاؤُكُمُ الأَقْدَمُونَ، فَإِنَّهُمْ عَدُوٌّ لِي إِلا رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ الَّذِي خَلَقَنِي فَهُوَ يَهْدِينِ، وَالَّذِي هُوَ يُطْعِمُنِي وَيَسْقِينِ، وَإِذا مَرِضْتُ فَهُوَ يَشْفِينِ، وَالَّذِي يُمِيتُي ثُمَّ يُحْيِينِ، وَالَّذِي أَطْمَعُ أَنْ يَغْفِرَ لِي خَطِيئَتِي يَوْمَ الدِّينِ ﴾ [الشعراء: ٦٩/٢٦ - ٨٢].
وَلَقَدْ آتَيْنَا إِبْرَاهِيمَ رُشْدَهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ وَكُنَا بِهِ عَالِمِينَ، إِذْ قَالَ لِأَبِيهِ وَقَوْمِهِ ما هَذِهِ التِّمَاثِيلُ الَّتِي أَنْتُمْ لَها عاكِفُونَ قالُوا وَجَدْنَا آبَاءَنَا لَها عابدِينَ، قَالَ لَقَدْ كُنتُمْ أَنتُمْ وَآبَاؤُكُمْ فِي ضَلالٍ مُبِينِ، قَالُوا أَجتَنا بِالْحَقِّ أَمْ أَنْتَ مِنَ اللَّاعِبِينَ، قَالَ بَلْ رَبُّكُمْ رَبُّ السَّماواتِ وَالأَرْضِ الَّذِي فَطَرَهُنَّ وَأَنا عَلَى ذَلِكُمْ مِنَ الشَّاهِدِينَ، وتاللَّهِ لأَكِيدَنَّ أَصْنَامَكُمْ بَعْدَ أَنْ تُوَلُّوا مُدْبِرِينَ [الأنبياء: ٥١/٢١ - ٥٧].
وصفوة القول أن الإنسان حين يلغي مصدر معرفته العقلية وأدواتها، ويعيش عالة على ما خلّفه الآباء من ميراث - على أهمية ميراث الآباء فيما يتصل بالمعرفة التراكمية – فإن ذلك يغدو تحولاً إلى آصار وأغلال للعقل.
ولعلنا قد لاحظنا أن القرآن الكريم حين أدان اتباع الآباء على ذلك النحو من التشديد فإنما يرجع ذلك - فيما يرجع - إلى الجاذبية الشديدة الإغراء التي تربط الناس بميراث الآباء، بصرف النظر عن نوعية هذا الموروث. ودون أن تلفت إلى سنن الله وقوانينه الثابتة (۱) . ومن هنا فإن مشكلة النزعة الآبائية عند الكافرين؛ تعني جميع من يقع في مشكلة مخالفة السنن حتى وإن كان مسلماً، إذ المشكلة إنسانية بالدرجة الأولى، لا يستثنى منها المسلمون، كما قد يغفل بعضهم أو يتوهم حين يظن لنفسه مزية خاصة على غيره من الأمم، مع أن القرآن الكريم حين سفه تلك المعتقدات تضمن بطريق الإشارة خطورة أن يقع المسلمون في تقليد آبائهم على غير بصيرة . وبتعبير آخر فإنه إذا ما غلبت (۲ ) . على العقل سطوة التقليد لموروث الآباء من التقاليد والعادات، وقيدت بذلك حريته في النظر، فإنه ينصرف عن النظر في مشكلة الحياة الواقعية ليتخذ من غابر الآباء، وغائب تاريخهم مادة للنظر ، يصوغ منها موازين وأحكاماً يسقطها على مشاكل الواقع في شيء من المثالية التاريخية على سبيل الانقياد لموروث الآباء، لا على سبيل البحث في وقائع التاريخ للاعتبار)) (۳).
وعلى هذا الأساس يمكن وصف التربية الإسلامية بأنها تربية منضبطة بكوابح العقل. وفي ذلك انعكاس إيجابي على المعلم المتحرر والمتعلم المتسائل، والباحث الذي يحرص على إزالة عوائق الموضوعية في مسار أبحاثه العلمية.
ه - العقل سبيل الهداية
ونعني بالهداية هنا الهداية العقدية والتشريعية المعتمدة على العقل وقواه ممثلة في التفكير والتذكر والتعقل والتدبر وسواها:
And in another place: Chapter Three: Section Two - The Intellect. "And who is more astray than one who invokes besides Allah those who will not respond to him until the Day of Resurrection, and they are unaware of their invocation. And when the people are gathered, they will be enemies to them and will deny their worship." [Quran 46:5-6]. And in the way of liberating the intellect from the authority of fathers and clan, the Quran presents the Abrahamic method, based on the style of rational dialogue, to uncover the deviation they are in. Conversely, instilling the value of monotheism never ceases to accompany dialogue with them: "And recite to them the news of Abraham, when he said to his father and his people, 'What do you worship?' They said, 'We worship idols and to them we are devoted.' He said, 'Do they hear you when you call, or benefit you or harm you?' They said, 'Rather, we found our fathers doing thus.' He said, 'Have you considered what you have been worshiping, you and your ancient fathers? Indeed, they are enemies to me, except the Lord of the worlds, who created me, and He guides me, and who feeds me and gives me drink, and when I am ill, He cures me, and who causes me to die and then revives me, and who I hope will forgive me my sin on the Day of Judgment.'" [Quran 26:69-82]. "And We had certainly given Abraham his sound judgment before, and We were of him well-Knowing, when he said to his father and his people, 'What are these statues to which you are devoted?' They said, 'We found our fathers worshippers of them.' He said, 'You and your fathers have been in clear error.' They said, 'Have you come to us with truth, or are you of those who jest?' He said, 'Rather, your Lord is the Lord of the heavens and the earth who created them, and I am, to that, of the witnesses. And by Allah, I will surely plan against your idols after you have turned your backs.'" [Quran 21:51-57]. In sum, when a person cancels his source of rational knowledge and its tools, and lives dependent on what the fathers have left as legacy—despite the importance of the fathers' legacy in cumulative knowledge—that becomes a transformation into shackles and fetters for the intellect. Perhaps we have noticed that when the Holy Quran condemned following the fathers in such a severe manner, that is due—among other reasons—to the extremely enticing attractiveness that binds people to the legacy of the fathers, regardless of the quality of that inheritance, and without drawing attention to Allah's established ways and laws. Hence, the problem of ancestralism among the disbelievers means all who fall into the problem of violating the established ways even if he is a Muslim, for the problem is primarily human, not excluding Muslims, as some may neglect or imagine that they have a special merit over other nations, while the Holy Quran, when it belittled those beliefs, implied by way of indication the danger that Muslims may fall into imitating their fathers without insight. In other words, if the authority of imitating the inherited traditions and customs overpowers the intellect, and thereby restricts its freedom of inquiry, it turns away from examining the real problems of life and takes the past of the fathers and their absent history as material for contemplation, formulating from them criteria and judgments that it projects onto real problems in something of historical idealism, out of submission to the inherited legacy of the fathers, not out of research into historical facts for admonition. On this basis, Islamic education can be described as education disciplined by the brakes of the intellect. And that is a positive reflection on the liberated teacher and the questioning learner, and the researcher who is keen to remove obstacles to objectivity in the course of his scientific research. H - The Intellect as the Path to Guidance. By guidance here we mean doctrinal and legislative guidance based on the intellect and its powers represented in thinking, remembering, reasoning, pondering, and so forth.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage discusses the Quran's critique of blind adherence to ancestral traditions and its promotion of rational inquiry. It begins with a Quranic verse (46:5-6) condemning those who call upon others besides Allah who cannot respond. The author then argues that the Quran liberates the intellect from the authority of fathers and clan by presenting the Abrahamic method of rational dialogue. The story of Abraham (Ibrahim) is cited extensively (from Surah Ash-Shu'ara and Al-Anbiya) as an example of using reason to challenge idolatry and ancestral customs. Abraham does not simply reject his father's beliefs but engages in logical questioning, asking whether the idols can hear, benefit, or harm. When the people reply that they found their fathers doing so, Abraham points out that both they and their fathers were in clear error. He then asserts the oneness of Allah as the Creator and Sustainer. The passage then summarizes: when a person abandons rational knowledge and depends solely on inherited legacy, the intellect becomes shackled. The author notes that the Quran's severe condemnation of following ancestors stems from the strong attractiveness of ancestral heritage, which often diverts people from Allah's fixed laws. Importantly, the problem of ancestralism is not limited to disbelievers; Muslims can also fall into it if they imitate their fathers without insight. When the intellect is dominated by the power of imitation, it loses freedom of inquiry and begins to impose idealized historical notions on present realities. The author concludes that Islamic education is disciplined by the brakes of the intellect, fostering liberated teachers and questioning learners. Finally, a new heading introduces 'the intellect as the path to guidance,' defining guidance as doctrinal and legislative guidance based on intellectual powers such as thinking, remembering, reasoning, and pondering.

تقليد

A) Because ancestral heritage is always false and useless.
B) Because it binds people to inherited traditions regardless of their truth, distracting from Allah's laws.
C) Because the fathers themselves were all disbelievers.
D) Because the intellect is inherently evil.

The Quran's critique of ancestral adherence is not a rejection of tradition but a call to use reason to evaluate inherited beliefs.

Method of Learning
beginner
10 min
The Supremacy of Revelation over Reason and Sense
Author defends revelation's supremacy over reason and sense

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to defend the epistemological supremacy of revelation over reason and empirical senses using Quranic evidence provided in the passage.

Core Idea
Revelation dominates both reason and sense as the only source of certain knowledge.

In this lesson, we explore the author's argument that revelation is not just one source among many, but the supreme epistemic authority. Building on Quranic affirmations of Allah's absolute knowledge and human limitation, the author establishes that true certainty (al-ilm al-yaqini) comes only through revelation. This has profound implications for how we evaluate claims about the unseen and how we approach Islamic methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic proof texts for human cognitive limitation
Locate the verses that state human knowledge is relative, limited, and dependent on Allah's will. The passage cites Al-Baqarah 255, Al-Isra 85, Yusuf 76, and Saba 3.
These verses establish that human reason and sense cannot attain comprehensive knowledge without divine aid.
2
Trace the author's inference from limitation to revelation's necessity
The author argues that because human knowledge is limited and relative, revelation must dominate both reason and sense. This is not an anti-reason stance, but a claim about epistemic ranking.
The phrase 'هيمنة الوحي على كل من الحس والعقل' is key.
3
Distinguish revelation from superstitious claims
The passage explicitly contrasts revelation with sorcery, astrology, etc. Identify how revelation provides a legitimate methodology while other claims are mere superstition.
This distinction is crucial for aqidah; only revelation connects us to the unseen with certainty.
4
Derive the methodological conclusion
The passage ends by stating that revelation alone provides a legitimate methodology (منهجاً مشروعاً). This means that in Islamic sciences, revelation is the ultimate arbiter.
This has implications for how we approach hadith, tafsir, and usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثالث - الوحي

عالِم الْغَيْبِ لا يَعْزُبُ عَنْهُ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ فِي السَّمَاواتِ وَلَا فِي الْأَرْضِ وَلَا أَصْغَرُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ وَلَا أَكْبَرُ إِلَّا فِي كِتَابٍ مُبِين﴾ [سبأ: ٣/٣٤].
وكل ما عندنا من معرفة فهي نسبية لا تمثل سوى جزء لا يتجزأ من علم الله الواسع المحيط، ولا ننالها إلا بمشيئته سبحانه ... وَلَا يُحِيطُونَ بِشَيْءٍ مِنْ عِلْمِهِ إلا بما شاء... [البقرة: ٢٥٥/٢].
... وَما أُوتِيتُمْ مِنَ الْعِلْمِ إِلا قَلِيلاً ... [الإسراء: ٨٥/١٧].
﴿وَفَوْقَ كُلِّ ذِي عِلْمٍ عَلِيمٍ﴾ [يوسف: ٧٦/١٢].
وإذا تقرر ذلك فإن هيمنة الوحي على كل من الحس والعقل - فضلاً عن المصادر التبعية الأخرى - تجعل من طريق النبوة وحدها وحياً يمتلك تلك القوة اليقينية، سواء في وروده أم في بعض دلالته وبذلك تتحصن عقول الناشئة ومسالكهم من أي ادعاءات تزعم أن لها صلة بالعالم العلوي عن طريق آخر كالشعوذة أو التنجيم والكهانة والعرافة.. إلخ ضروب التفكير الخرافي. ويحل محلها التفكير العلمي المعتمد على مصدر النبوة وطريقها وحدها منهجاً مشروعاً.
غاية الوحي
وبوسعنا إدراك غاية الوحي من جملة النصوص التالية:
البشارة والإنذار كغاية رئيسة
﴿وَما أَرْسَلْنَاكَ إِلا كافةً لِلنَّاسِ بَشِيرًا وَنَذِيراً (سبا: ٢٨/٣٤].
وإخراج الناس من الظلمات إلى النور:
الر كِتابٌ أَنْزَلْنَاهُ إِلَيْكَ لِتُخْرِجَ النَّاسَ مِنَ الظُّلُمَاتِ إِلَى النُّورِ بِإِذْنِ رَبِّهِمْ... [إبراهيم: ١/١٤].
وبصائر تنير الدروب: هَذا بَصائِرُ لِلنَّاسِ [الجاثية: ٢٠/٤٥]. ... قُلْ إِنما أَتَّبِعُ ما يُوحَى إِلَيَّ مِنْ رَبِّي هَذَا بَصَائِرُ مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ وَهُدَى وَرَحْمَةٌ لِقَوْمٍ يُؤْمِنُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ٢٠٣/٧].
ولبيان مواضع الاختلاف في الأصول والكليات، وليكون هداية للمؤمنين:
﴿وَما أَنْزَلْنَا عَلَيْكَ الْكِتابَ إِلا لِتُبَيِّنَ لَهُمُ الَّذِي اخْتَلَفُوا فِيهِ وَهُدَى وَرَحْمَةً لِقَوْمٍ يُؤْمِنُونَ) (النحل: ٦٤/١٦].
وبوجه خاص فإنه يهدف إلى هداية المؤمنين:
يا أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ قَدْ جَاءَكُمْ رَسُولُنَا يُبَيِّنُ لَكُمْ كَثِيراً مِمَّا كُنتُمْ تُخْفُونَ مِنَ الْكِتابِ وَيَعْفُو عَنْ كَثِيرٍ قَدْ جَاءَكُمْ مِنَ اللهِ نُورٌ وَكِتابٌ مُبِينٌ، يَهْدِي بِهِ اللهُ مَنِ اتَّبَعَ رِضْوَانَهُ سُبُلَ السَّلامِ وَيُخْرِجُهُمْ مِنَ الظُّلُمَاتِ إِلَى النُّورِ بِإِذْنِهِ وَيَهْدِيهِمْ إِلَى صِرَاطٍ مُسْتَقِيمٍ﴾ [المائدة: ١٥/٥-١٦].
إن غاية الوحي تمثل هدفاً غائياً بالنسبة إلى التربية الإسلامية، فهدفها الكلي: تعريف الإنسان طريق الهداية ليصبح كائنا مهدياً، أو صالحاً مصلحاً.
خصائص الوحي
وللوحي جملة خصائص يمكن متابعة أحد الباحثين في إجمالها على النحو التالي:
١ - الصدق.
۲ - الإحاطة بأحداث الماضي، والكشف عن أمور المستقبل.
٣ - التوحيد: حيث تتضافر جميع الدعوات الإلهية على قضية التوحيد.
Chapter Three: Section Three - Revelation

'Knower of the Unseen, not absent from Him is the weight of an atom in the heavens or in the earth, nor anything smaller than that nor larger, except [it is] in a clear book' [Saba: 34/3].
And all that we have of knowledge is relative, representing only an indivisible part of Allah's vast encompassing knowledge, and we do not attain it except by His will, the Exalted... 'And they encompass not anything of His knowledge except what He wills' [Al-Baqarah: 255/2].
'...And you have not been given of knowledge except a little' [Al-Isra: 85/17].
'And above every possessor of knowledge is the All-Knowing' [Yusuf: 76/12].
And if that is established, then the dominance of revelation over both sense and reason - not to mention other subsidiary sources - makes the path of prophethood alone a revelation possessing that certain power, both in its coming and in some of its indication. And thereby the minds and paths of the youth are fortified from any claims that claim connection to the higher world through another path, such as sorcery, astrology, soothsaying, divination, etc., kinds of superstitious thinking. And it is replaced by scientific thinking based on the source of prophethood and its path alone as a legitimate methodology.
The Purpose of Revelation
And we can perceive the purpose of revelation from the following texts:
Glad tidings and warning as a main purpose:
'And We have not sent you except comprehensively to mankind, as a bringer of glad tidings and a warner' [Saba: 28/34].
And bringing people out of darkness into light:
'Alif Lam Ra. A book which We have sent down to you that you might bring people out of darkness into light by permission of their Lord...' [Ibrahim: 1/14].
And insights that illuminate paths: 'This is insight for mankind' [Al-Jathiyah: 20/45]. '...Say, I only follow what is revealed to me from my Lord. This is insight from your Lord, and guidance and mercy for a people who believe' [Al-A'raf: 203/7].
And to clarify points of difference in fundamentals and universals, and to be guidance for the believers:
'And We have not sent down to you the Book except that you may make clear to them that concerning which they differed, and as guidance and mercy for a people who believe' [An-Nahl: 64/16].
And specifically, it aims to guide the believers:
'O People of the Scripture, there has come to you Our Messenger making clear to you much of what you used to conceal of the Scripture, and pardoning much. There has come to you from Allah a light and a clear book. By which Allah guides those who pursue His pleasure to the ways of peace, and brings them out of darkness into light by His permission, and guides them to a straight path.' [Al-Ma'idah: 15-16/5].
Indeed, the purpose of revelation represents an ultimate goal for Islamic education. Its overall goal is to define for man the path of guidance so that he becomes a guided being, or righteous and reformer.
Characteristics of Revelation
And for revelation are a number of characteristics that one can follow the summary of one of the researchers as follows:
1 - Truthfulness.
2 - Encompassing past events and revealing future matters.
3 - Monotheism: where all divine calls cooperate on the issue of monotheism.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion establishing the supremacy of revelation over all other sources of knowledge. The author begins by quoting Quranic verses that affirm the absolute and all-encompassing knowledge of Allah, emphasizing that human knowledge is relative and limited. The verse from Saba (34:3) states that nothing escapes Allah's knowledge, from the smallest atom to the largest. Then the author argues that all human knowledge is merely a part of Allah's vast knowledge and is only attained by His will, citing Al-Baqarah (255:2) and Al-Isra (85:17). The verse from Yusuf (12:76) reinforces that above every learned person is the All-Knowing.

Having established this, the author asserts that revelation dominates both sense and reason, making the prophetic path alone the source of certain knowledge. This protects minds from superstitions like sorcery and astrology, replacing them with a legitimate scientific methodology based solely on prophecy.

The author then defines the purposes of revelation. The primary purpose is giving glad tidings and warnings (Saba 28:34). Another purpose is to bring people from darkness to light (Ibrahim 1:14). Revelation provides insights that illuminate paths (Al-Jathiyah 20:45, Al-A'raf 203/7). It also clarifies points of disagreement in fundamental principles and provides guidance for believers (An-Nahl 64:16). Specifically, it guides the believers to the straight path (Al-Ma'idah 15-16/5). The overall goal of revelation in Islamic education is to define the path of guidance so that humans become guided and righteous reformers.

Finally, the author lists three characteristics of revelation, summarized from another researcher: truthfulness, encompassment of past events and revealing of future matters, and monotheism in that all divine calls unite on tawhid.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the 'dominance of revelation' (haimanat al-wahy) over sense and reason imply?
A) Reason and sense are completely useless and should be discarded.
B) Revelation takes precedence when there is a conflict, but sense and reason remain valid instruments.
C) Only empirical senses are subordinate, reason is independent.
D) Revelation only dominates in matters of worship, not in natural sciences.

Key Takeaway
Revelation is the supreme epistemic authority in Islam, providing certain knowledge that dominates both reason and empirical senses.

Using the Quranic verses cited in the lesson, construct a concise argument that revelation is the only source of yaqini (certain) knowledge about the unseen. Identify the premises and conclusion.

The Purposes of Revelation: Glad Tidings, Guidance, and Clarification
Author lists the purposes of revelation with scriptural evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to categorise the main purposes of revelation as stated in the passage and cite the corresponding Quranic verses.

Core Idea
Revelation aims to give glad tidings, warn, bring from darkness to light, clarify differences, and guide to the straight path.

The passage not only establishes revelation's supremacy but also details its purposes. Understanding these purposes helps us see why revelation is essential for human guidance. The author lists several Quranic verses that each highlight a different facet of revelation's mission. This lesson will help you memorize and articulate these purposes.

Guided Path
1
List each purpose mentioned
Scan the passage under 'غاية الوحي' and extract each distinct purpose. There are at least four: giving glad tidings and warning, bringing from darkness to light, providing insights, and clarifying points of difference.
The passage also mentions guiding the believers specifically.
2
Match purposes to Quranic verses
For each purpose, locate the verse(s) that the author uses to support it. For example, glad tidings and warning is linked to Saba 28; bringing from darkness to light to Ibrahim 1; insights to Al-Jathiyah 20 and Al-A'raf 203; clarifying differences to An-Nahl 64.
This exercise trains you to connect concepts with textual evidence.
3
Understand the ultimate goal
The author concludes that the overall purpose is 'to define for man the path of guidance so that he becomes a guided being, or righteous and reformer.' Identify how each specific purpose contributes to this ultimate goal.
This is the teleological dimension of revelation in Islamic education.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثالث - الوحي

عالِم الْغَيْبِ لا يَعْزُبُ عَنْهُ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ فِي السَّمَاواتِ وَلَا فِي الْأَرْضِ وَلَا أَصْغَرُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ وَلَا أَكْبَرُ إِلَّا فِي كِتَابٍ مُبِين﴾ [سبأ: ٣/٣٤].
وكل ما عندنا من معرفة فهي نسبية لا تمثل سوى جزء لا يتجزأ من علم الله الواسع المحيط، ولا ننالها إلا بمشيئته سبحانه ... وَلَا يُحِيطُونَ بِشَيْءٍ مِنْ عِلْمِهِ إلا بما شاء... [البقرة: ٢٥٥/٢].
... وَما أُوتِيتُمْ مِنَ الْعِلْمِ إِلا قَلِيلاً ... [الإسراء: ٨٥/١٧].
﴿وَفَوْقَ كُلِّ ذِي عِلْمٍ عَلِيمٍ﴾ [يوسف: ٧٦/١٢].
وإذا تقرر ذلك فإن هيمنة الوحي على كل من الحس والعقل - فضلاً عن المصادر التبعية الأخرى - تجعل من طريق النبوة وحدها وحياً يمتلك تلك القوة اليقينية، سواء في وروده أم في بعض دلالته وبذلك تتحصن عقول الناشئة ومسالكهم من أي ادعاءات تزعم أن لها صلة بالعالم العلوي عن طريق آخر كالشعوذة أو التنجيم والكهانة والعرافة.. إلخ ضروب التفكير الخرافي. ويحل محلها التفكير العلمي المعتمد على مصدر النبوة وطريقها وحدها منهجاً مشروعاً.
غاية الوحي
وبوسعنا إدراك غاية الوحي من جملة النصوص التالية:
البشارة والإنذار كغاية رئيسة
﴿وَما أَرْسَلْنَاكَ إِلا كافةً لِلنَّاسِ بَشِيرًا وَنَذِيراً (سبا: ٢٨/٣٤].
وإخراج الناس من الظلمات إلى النور:
الر كِتابٌ أَنْزَلْنَاهُ إِلَيْكَ لِتُخْرِجَ النَّاسَ مِنَ الظُّلُمَاتِ إِلَى النُّورِ بِإِذْنِ رَبِّهِمْ... [إبراهيم: ١/١٤].
وبصائر تنير الدروب: هَذا بَصائِرُ لِلنَّاسِ [الجاثية: ٢٠/٤٥]. ... قُلْ إِنما أَتَّبِعُ ما يُوحَى إِلَيَّ مِنْ رَبِّي هَذَا بَصَائِرُ مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ وَهُدَى وَرَحْمَةٌ لِقَوْمٍ يُؤْمِنُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ٢٠٣/٧].
ولبيان مواضع الاختلاف في الأصول والكليات، وليكون هداية للمؤمنين:
﴿وَما أَنْزَلْنَا عَلَيْكَ الْكِتابَ إِلا لِتُبَيِّنَ لَهُمُ الَّذِي اخْتَلَفُوا فِيهِ وَهُدَى وَرَحْمَةً لِقَوْمٍ يُؤْمِنُونَ) (النحل: ٦٤/١٦].
وبوجه خاص فإنه يهدف إلى هداية المؤمنين:
يا أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ قَدْ جَاءَكُمْ رَسُولُنَا يُبَيِّنُ لَكُمْ كَثِيراً مِمَّا كُنتُمْ تُخْفُونَ مِنَ الْكِتابِ وَيَعْفُو عَنْ كَثِيرٍ قَدْ جَاءَكُمْ مِنَ اللهِ نُورٌ وَكِتابٌ مُبِينٌ، يَهْدِي بِهِ اللهُ مَنِ اتَّبَعَ رِضْوَانَهُ سُبُلَ السَّلامِ وَيُخْرِجُهُمْ مِنَ الظُّلُمَاتِ إِلَى النُّورِ بِإِذْنِهِ وَيَهْدِيهِمْ إِلَى صِرَاطٍ مُسْتَقِيمٍ﴾ [المائدة: ١٥/٥-١٦].
إن غاية الوحي تمثل هدفاً غائياً بالنسبة إلى التربية الإسلامية، فهدفها الكلي: تعريف الإنسان طريق الهداية ليصبح كائنا مهدياً، أو صالحاً مصلحاً.
خصائص الوحي
وللوحي جملة خصائص يمكن متابعة أحد الباحثين في إجمالها على النحو التالي:
١ - الصدق.
۲ - الإحاطة بأحداث الماضي، والكشف عن أمور المستقبل.
٣ - التوحيد: حيث تتضافر جميع الدعوات الإلهية على قضية التوحيد.
Chapter Three: Section Three - Revelation

'Knower of the Unseen, not absent from Him is the weight of an atom in the heavens or in the earth, nor anything smaller than that nor larger, except [it is] in a clear book' [Saba: 34/3].
And all that we have of knowledge is relative, representing only an indivisible part of Allah's vast encompassing knowledge, and we do not attain it except by His will, the Exalted... 'And they encompass not anything of His knowledge except what He wills' [Al-Baqarah: 255/2].
'...And you have not been given of knowledge except a little' [Al-Isra: 85/17].
'And above every possessor of knowledge is the All-Knowing' [Yusuf: 76/12].
And if that is established, then the dominance of revelation over both sense and reason - not to mention other subsidiary sources - makes the path of prophethood alone a revelation possessing that certain power, both in its coming and in some of its indication. And thereby the minds and paths of the youth are fortified from any claims that claim connection to the higher world through another path, such as sorcery, astrology, soothsaying, divination, etc., kinds of superstitious thinking. And it is replaced by scientific thinking based on the source of prophethood and its path alone as a legitimate methodology.
The Purpose of Revelation
And we can perceive the purpose of revelation from the following texts:
Glad tidings and warning as a main purpose:
'And We have not sent you except comprehensively to mankind, as a bringer of glad tidings and a warner' [Saba: 28/34].
And bringing people out of darkness into light:
'Alif Lam Ra. A book which We have sent down to you that you might bring people out of darkness into light by permission of their Lord...' [Ibrahim: 1/14].
And insights that illuminate paths: 'This is insight for mankind' [Al-Jathiyah: 20/45]. '...Say, I only follow what is revealed to me from my Lord. This is insight from your Lord, and guidance and mercy for a people who believe' [Al-A'raf: 203/7].
And to clarify points of difference in fundamentals and universals, and to be guidance for the believers:
'And We have not sent down to you the Book except that you may make clear to them that concerning which they differed, and as guidance and mercy for a people who believe' [An-Nahl: 64/16].
And specifically, it aims to guide the believers:
'O People of the Scripture, there has come to you Our Messenger making clear to you much of what you used to conceal of the Scripture, and pardoning much. There has come to you from Allah a light and a clear book. By which Allah guides those who pursue His pleasure to the ways of peace, and brings them out of darkness into light by His permission, and guides them to a straight path.' [Al-Ma'idah: 15-16/5].
Indeed, the purpose of revelation represents an ultimate goal for Islamic education. Its overall goal is to define for man the path of guidance so that he becomes a guided being, or righteous and reformer.
Characteristics of Revelation
And for revelation are a number of characteristics that one can follow the summary of one of the researchers as follows:
1 - Truthfulness.
2 - Encompassing past events and revealing future matters.
3 - Monotheism: where all divine calls cooperate on the issue of monotheism.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion establishing the supremacy of revelation over all other sources of knowledge. The author begins by quoting Quranic verses that affirm the absolute and all-encompassing knowledge of Allah, emphasizing that human knowledge is relative and limited. The verse from Saba (34:3) states that nothing escapes Allah's knowledge, from the smallest atom to the largest. Then the author argues that all human knowledge is merely a part of Allah's vast knowledge and is only attained by His will, citing Al-Baqarah (255:2) and Al-Isra (85:17). The verse from Yusuf (12:76) reinforces that above every learned person is the All-Knowing.

Having established this, the author asserts that revelation dominates both sense and reason, making the prophetic path alone the source of certain knowledge. This protects minds from superstitions like sorcery and astrology, replacing them with a legitimate scientific methodology based solely on prophecy.

The author then defines the purposes of revelation. The primary purpose is giving glad tidings and warnings (Saba 28:34). Another purpose is to bring people from darkness to light (Ibrahim 1:14). Revelation provides insights that illuminate paths (Al-Jathiyah 20:45, Al-A'raf 203/7). It also clarifies points of disagreement in fundamental principles and provides guidance for believers (An-Nahl 64:16). Specifically, it guides the believers to the straight path (Al-Ma'idah 15-16/5). The overall goal of revelation in Islamic education is to define the path of guidance so that humans become guided and righteous reformers.

Finally, the author lists three characteristics of revelation, summarized from another researcher: truthfulness, encompassment of past events and revealing of future matters, and monotheism in that all divine calls unite on tawhid.

بيان الاختلاف
الهداية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which verse is used to support the purpose of clarifying points of difference in fundamentals?
A) Saba 28
B) Ibrahim 1
C) Al-Jathiyah 20
D) An-Nahl 64

Key Takeaway
Revelation serves multiple integrated purposes: warning, enlightenment, clarification, and guidance, all aiming to produce a guided and reforming individual.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Select one of the purposes mentioned (e.g., clarifying differences). Find a concrete example from Islamic history where revelation clarified a dispute (e.g., the issue of the 'Ifk incident or inheritance laws). Write a short paragraph explaining how revelation achieved that purpose.

Characteristics of Revelation: Truthfulness, Comprehensiveness, and Monotheism
Author lists three key characteristics of revelation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and explain the three main characteristics of revelation as summarised in the passage.

Core Idea
Revelation is characterised by truthfulness, exhaustive knowledge, and the central message of monotheism.

After discussing the supremacy and purposes of revelation, the author briefly lists three characteristics that distinguish it from other claims of divine communication. These characteristics serve as criteria to evaluate any claim of revelation. This lesson will help you internalize these criteria.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three characteristics
The passage lists three characteristics under 'خصائص الوحي': truthfulness (al-sidq), encompassment of past and future events (al-ihata), and monotheism (al-tawhid).
These are taken from a researcher's summary, so they are likely well-known in the tradition.
2
Understand each characteristic
Truthfulness means that revelation is free from falsehood. Encompassment means it contains accurate information about the past and future. Monotheism means that all divine messages agree on tawhid.
These characteristics also serve as authentication marks.
3
Apply them to evaluate claims
Using these characteristics, one can distinguish true revelation from false claims. For example, a false prophet's claim might contain internal contradictions (lack of truthfulness), errors about past events, or promote polytheism.
This is a practical tool for aqidah.

Finally, the author lists three characteristics of revelation, summarized from another researcher: truthfulness, encompassment of past events and revealing of future matters, and monotheism in that all divine calls unite on tawhid.

Universality and Eternity of Islamic Education
Author argues Islamic education is universal and eternal based on revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the two key characteristics of Islamic education—universality and eternal validity—by tracing the author's argument from revelation.

Core Idea
Islamic education is universal and eternal because it is based on divine revelation, not on any particular culture or time.

In this passage, the author asserts two foundational characteristics of Islamic education: universality and eternal validity. These are not simply claims but are derived from the nature of revelation itself. Let's unpack the logical steps the author uses to support this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two characteristics
Read the passage and locate the two main characteristics the author attributes to Islamic education. They are directly stated in the first and second sentences.
Universality and eternity/absolute validity.
2
Find the evidence for each
For universality, the author argues that Islamic education is not merely a reflection of the Arab environment but is revelation from Allah. For eternity, the author cites Quran 5:3 and argues that since the source is Allah, it is valid for all times and places.
The verse is used as evidence for finality and perfection.
3
Understand the logical connection
The author connects the source (revelation) to the characteristics: because Islamic education is from Allah, it cannot be limited to a specific culture or time. This is a deductive argument: if it is divine revelation, then it is universal and eternal.
Revelation (wahy) is the key premise.
4
Identify the implications for institutions
The passage concludes that Islamic educational institutions must engage in comparative studies and interfaith dialogue to demonstrate humanity's need for the final message.
This is a practical application of the characteristics.

And that confirms the characteristic of universality in Islamic education, meaning that it is not merely a reflection of the Arab environment in which Muhammad appeared, but rather because it is revelation from Allah, it is not specific to these people or those. And this necessitates educating the learner on Islamic values of a human character, and necessitates that the goals and content include attention to human problems, issues, and concerns, such that this reflects on the social education of the Muslim learner. Eternity and absolute validity: meaning there is no religion after Islam and no messenger or prophet after Muhammad, and no temporal limits for the final message: ... Today I have perfected for you your religion and completed My favor upon you and have approved for you Islam as a religion... [Al-Ma'idah 5:3]. And that means that Islamic education is not temporary in its principles and universals, but rather it is eternal, absolutely valid for all times and places, because its original source is Allah - glorified and exalted - possessor of the most beautiful names and the highest attributes - majestic and sublime - and this requires from Islamic educational institutions attention to comparative studies, especially in the science of religions, and attention to the field of religious dialogue that crystallizes humanity's need for the final message and the final prophet.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage defines two fundamental characteristics of Islamic education: universality and eternal validity. The author begins by affirming that Islamic education is universal, meaning it is not merely a product of the Arab environment where Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) emerged. Instead, because it originates from divine revelation (wahy), it transcends any particular ethnic group or culture. This universality requires that the learner be educated on Islamic values that have a human dimension, and that educational objectives and content address global human problems and concerns, thereby shaping the Muslim learner's social education. The second characteristic is eternity and absolute validity. The author cites the verse from Surah Al-Ma'idah (5:3) which declares the perfection of Islam as a religion, implying that no religion or prophet comes after Muhammad. Therefore, Islamic education is not temporary or limited to a specific era; it is eternal and suitable for all times and places because its ultimate source is Allah, who possesses perfect attributes. This conclusion calls upon Islamic educational institutions to engage in comparative studies, particularly in religious studies, and in interfaith dialogue that demonstrates humanity's need for the final message and the final prophet.

Three Conditions for Integrating Islamic Knowledge
Author states three conditions for integrating Islamic knowledge sources and methods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three conditions for integrating Islamic knowledge sources and methods, and support each with a Quranic verse from the passage.

Core Idea
Integration of knowledge in Islam requires firmness, comprehensiveness, and unity—three conditions rooted in the Quran.

In this passage, the author presents three objective conditions that must be met for the integration of knowledge sources (revelation, reason, experience) to be valid. These conditions are not merely theoretical; they are derived from Quranic principles and have direct implications for education. As you read, notice how each condition is defined and supported with Quranic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching claim
The passage begins by asserting that integration of sources is necessary but conditional. Identify the author's main claim about the three conditions.
The author says these conditions are necessary for cooperation between sources and methods.
2
Extract the three conditions
List the three conditions: firmness in knowledge (al-rusukh), comprehensiveness and inclusiveness (al-ihata wa al-shumul), and unity of knowledge (wahdat al-ma'rifa). For each, note the author's definition.
Conditions are presented with Quranic verses as evidence.
3
Locate the Quranic evidence
For each condition, identify the Quranic verse cited. Explain how the verse supports the condition.
Verses: Al Imran 3:7 and Ar-Rum 30:7 for firmness; Yunus 10:39 and An-Naml 27:84 for comprehensiveness; Al-An'am 6:159, Ar-Rum 30:32, and Al-Baqarah 2:136-138 for unity.
4
Analyze the educational implication
The author derives educational applications. For firmness, what does it imply for learners and teachers? For comprehensiveness? For unity?
Firmness implies mastery and logical sequence; teachers must be specialized. Comprehensiveness guards against partial knowledge. Unity prevents fragmentation of knowledge.
5
Synthesize the unity condition
The third condition is based on Tawhid. How does the author argue that knowledge becomes a single unity despite its branches?
Unity of knowledge is rooted in the oneness of Allah; all branches are connected.

الشرط الثالث: مراعاة وحدة المعرفة
أي إنه باسترجاع الذهن لمصادر المعرفة وطرائقها، وميادينها، ووحـــدة المعرفة والتي تجسدت هذه الأخيرة أكثر ما تجسّدت في أساس الوحدانية لله
تعالى، فإن المعرفة تصبح وحدة واحدة أياً ما تشعبت فروعها، وتوسعت ميادينها. ولذلك فإن هناك آيات تحذر من تجزئة المعرفة في المنهج الكلـي وهـو الدين:
وإِنَّ الَّذِينَ فَرَّقُوا دِينَهُمْ وَكَانُوا شِيَعًا لَسْتَ مِنْهُمْ فِي شَيْءٍ..)) [الأنعام: ١٥٩/٦]. مِنَ الَّذِينَ فَرَّقُوا دِينَهُمْ وَكَانُوا شِيَعاً كُلُّ حِزْبٍ بِمَا لَدَيْهِمْ فَرِحُونَ [الروم: ٣٢/٣٠].
وإزاء ذلك فإن ثمة حثاً على وحدة المعرفة الكلية: قُولُوا آمَنَّا بِاللهِ وَمَا أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْنا وَما أُنزِلَ إِلَى إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَإِسْمَاعِيلَ وإسحاق وَيَعْقُوبَ وَالأَسْبَاطِ وَمَا أُوتِيَ مُوسَى وَعِيسَى وَمَا أُوتِيَ النَّبِيُّونَ مِنْ رَبِّهِمْ لا نُفَرِّقُ بَيْنَ أَحَدٍ مِنْهُمْ وَنَحْنُ لَهُ مُسْلِمُونَ، فَإِنْ آمَنُوا بِمِثْلِ ما آمَنتُمْ بِهِ فَقَدِ اهْتَدَوْا وَإِن تَوَلَّوْا فَإِنَّما هُمْ فِي شِقاق فَسَيَكْفِيكَهُمُ اللهُ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْعَلِيمُ، صِبْغَةَ اللهِ وَمَنْ أَحْسَنُ مِنَ اللهِ صِبْغَةً وَنَحْنُ لَهُ عابدون) [البقرة: ١٣٦/٢-١٣٨] (۱).
وحين نتحدث عن هذه الشروط فإن كلاً منها يتضمن جوانب تربوية مباشرة، تتفاعل فيها مصادر المعرفة وطرائقها الرئيسة، ويمكن الإفادة منها في واقع التربية الإسلامية الراهن. فشرط الرسوخ في العلم يتضمن ضرورة إتقان المتعلم للمادة العلمية التي يدرسها، بحيث لا ينتقل منها إلى سواها حتى يصير راسخاً فيها بحق، فيتحقق التسلسل المنطقي في المنهج. كما أن المعلم – من باب أولى - لا يقدم على تدريس مادة عملية حتى يكون متخصصاً فيها، أو على اطلاع غزير يجعل منه راسخاً في حديثه وتناوله لفقرات تلك المادة يغدو تناول العالم وليس المهتم المثقف فحسب. وحين بدأت ظاهرة هجران التخصصات الأصلية تتفشى في المؤسسات التعليمية الأكاديمية، وصار كــل علـم كلاً مباحاً (۱) الكيلاني، فلسفة التربية الإسلامية، ٢٣٨-٢٤٠ .
Proceeding from the objectivity of this tripartite classification, the necessity of integration between these sources and methods becomes one of the prerequisites for accepting it. However, there are three objective conditions that I consider necessary to be met for cooperation between these sources and methods, as follows:
First condition: Firmness in knowledge
The intended meaning of 'firmness' here is depth in understanding the subject in terms of its history and developments that brought it to the current stage: '...and those firmly rooted in knowledge say: We believe in it, all of it is from our Lord...' [Al Imran 3:7]. And the Quran criticizes those with superficial understandings, whose perception does not go beyond the current state of the subject of knowledge, as if it were the last link of this temporal development: 'They know what is apparent of the worldly life...' [Ar-Rum 30:7].
Second condition: Comprehensiveness and inclusiveness
By comprehensiveness and inclusiveness we mean total and detailed branching coverage of the spatial and temporal limits of the subject, and caution from partial knowledge: 'Rather, they denied that which they did not encompass in knowledge...' [Yunus 10:39]. 'He said: Have you denied My verses while you did not encompass them in knowledge?' [An-Naml 27:84].
Third condition: Observing the unity of knowledge
That is, by the mind recalling the sources of knowledge, its methods, and its fields, and the unity of knowledge – which has been manifested most in the foundation of the oneness of God Almighty – knowledge becomes a single unity no matter how its branches diverge and its fields expand. Therefore, there are verses that warn against fragmenting knowledge in the comprehensive methodology, which is religion: 'Indeed, those who have divided their religion and become sects – you are not [to be] with them in anything...' [Al-An'am 6:159]. 'Of those who have divided their religion and become sects, every faction rejoicing in what it has' [Ar-Rum 30:32]. And in response to that, there is encouragement for the unity of total knowledge: 'Say: We believe in Allah and what has been revealed to us and what has been revealed to Abraham, Ishmael, Isaac, Jacob, and the Descendants, and what was given to Moses and Jesus and what was given to the prophets from their Lord. We make no distinction between any of them, and we are Muslims to Him. So if they believe in the like of what you have believed, then they have been guided. But if they turn away, then they are only in dissension, and Allah will suffice you against them. And He is the Hearing, the Knowing. The religion of Allah, and who is better than Allah in religion? And we are worshippers of Him.' [Al-Baqarah 2:136-138].
And when we speak about these conditions, each of them includes direct educational aspects in which the main sources and methods of knowledge interact, and benefit can be derived from them in the current reality of Islamic education. So the condition of firmness in knowledge includes the necessity for the learner to master the academic subject he studies, so that he does not move from it to another until he becomes firmly rooted in it with truth, thus achieving logical sequence in the curriculum. Moreover, the teacher – with greater reason – should not proceed to teach a practical subject until he is specialized in it, or has extensive familiarity that makes him firm in his speech and handling of the topics of that subject, so that his approach becomes that of a scholar and not just an interested cultured person. And when the phenomenon of abandoning original specializations began to spread in academic educational institutions, and every science became permissible for everyone (1) al-Kilani, Philosophy of Islamic Education, pp. 238-240.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological and methodological exposition that establishes three objective conditions for the integration of the three sources and methods of knowledge (presumably revelation, reason, and experience, as indicated earlier in the book). The author proceeds in a structured manner: first stating the necessity of these conditions, then listing them one by one with Quranic evidence and brief explanation, and finally drawing educational implications.

Condition one: Firmness in knowledge (الرسوخ في العلم). The author defines this as deep understanding of a subject's history and its developments leading to the present. He supports this with Quranic verses (Al Imran 3:7 and Ar-Rum 30:7) that praise those who are firmly rooted and criticize superficial understanding. This condition guards against taking knowledge as a static snapshot and ignoring its development.

Condition two: Comprehensiveness and inclusiveness (الإحاطة والشمول). This means total and detailed coverage of a subject's spatial and temporal boundaries, avoiding partial knowledge. The author cites Yunus 10:39 and An-Naml 27:84, which condemn denying what one does not fully encompass in knowledge. This condition is a direct application of the principle that one must not judge without full understanding.

Condition three: Observing the unity of knowledge (وحدة المعرفة). The author explains that recalling the sources, methods, and fields of knowledge, and especially the concept of Tawhid (oneness of Allah), results in a unified knowledge despite its branches. He warns against fragmenting religion or knowledge (Al-An'am 6:159, Ar-Rum 30:32) and encourages the unity as expressed in Al-Baqarah 2:136-138, which stresses belief in all prophets without distinction.

Finally, the author extracts educational lessons: the firmness condition demands mastery and logical sequencing in learning; teachers must be specialized. This passage is an example of how Islamic epistemological principles inform educational methodology.

Key Terms

الإحاطة والشمول
وحدة المعرفة

Method of Learning

Three Conditions for Knowledge Integration in Islamic Education
Author enumerates and explains three conditions: rootedness, comprehensiveness, and unity of knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the three conditions for knowledge integration in Islamic education and apply them to evaluate educational practices.

Core Idea
Knowledge integration in Islam requires sequential mastery, holistic scope, and unity of truth.

This passage presents three essential conditions for integrating knowledge in Islamic education: rootedness (al-rusūkh), comprehensiveness (al-iḥāṭa wa al-shumūl), and unity of knowledge (waḥdat al-maʿrifa). The author warns against the dangers of superficial specialization and academic confusion, urging a return to deep mastery and interdisciplinary awareness. Understanding these conditions helps educators and students maintain scholarly integrity and avoid the pitfalls of generalisation and charlatanism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
From the passage, extract the three conditions for knowledge integration. The first two are explicitly discussed: rootedness in knowledge and comprehensiveness/inclusivity. The third, unity of knowledge, is introduced but not fully elaborated in this excerpt.
The third condition may appear in later sections.
2
Understand rootedness (al-rusūkh)
Rootedness requires the learner to master a subject before moving to another, ensuring logical progression. The teacher must be specialised, not a generalist. The author criticises the trend where anyone can teach any subject, leading to superficiality and confusion between experts and amateurs.
The term 'rusūkh' is used here in a modern educational sense; in classical tafsir it often means firmness in understanding.
3
Understand comprehensiveness (al-iḥāṭa wa al-shumūl)
Comprehensiveness affirms rootedness by requiring the teacher to master both cognitive and skill aspects of the subject, and to be familiar with related disciplines. It avoids narrow specialisation and promotes a holistic view.
This condition expands on rootedness, not replaces it.
4
Recognise the problem addressed
The author observes a crisis where specialisations are abandoned, leading to false equivalences (e.g., astronomer vs. astrologer). The conditions are proposed as remedies to restore the integrity of knowledge.
The author uses strong rhetorical questions to highlight the absurdity.
5
Apply the conditions to a real scenario
Imagine an Islamic studies curriculum. Check if students master fiqh before moving to usul al-fiqh. Verify if teachers hold deep expertise and are not teaching outside their field. Assess if the curriculum includes connections to related sciences like hadith and tafsir.
This step requires synthesising the conditions into a practical evaluation.

وحين نتحدث عن هذه الشروط فإن كلاً منها يتضمن جوانب تربوية مباشرة، تتفاعل فيها مصادر المعرفة وطرائقها الرئيسة، ويمكن الإفادة منها في واقع التربية الإسلامية الراهن. فشرط الرسوخ في العلم يتضمن ضرورة إتقان المتعلم للمادة العلمية التي يدرسها، بحيث لا ينتقل منها إلى سواها حتى يصير راسخاً فيها بحق، فيتحقق التسلسل المنطقي في المنهج. كما أن المعلم – من باب أولى - لا يقدم على تدريس مادة عملية حتى يكون متخصصاً فيها، أو على اطلاع غزير يجعل منه راسخاً في حديثه وتناوله لفقرات تلك المادة يغدو تناول العالم وليس المهتم المثقف فحسب. وحين بدأت ظاهرة هجران التخصصات الأصلية تتفشى في المؤسسات التعليمية الأكاديمية، وصار كل علم كلاً مباحاً لكل من قرأ وكتب بحيث إن بإمكانه التحدث في كل علم، والتدريس لكل تخصص، حينها اختلطت التخصصات وتداخلت - ولا أقول تكاملت – على نحو أفضى بها إلى التعميم والتسطيح وأتاح فرصة للادعاءات، وجعل من المتخصص والمثقف أقراناً بلا فرق بل غدا المنجم والفلكي، والطبيب والمشعوذ، والفيلسوف والمهرج جميعهم - مع الأسف - أمام المعرفة والعلم سواء بسواء!! فهل يتسق ذلك وشرط الرسوخ في العلم؟

إن ذلك يدعونا لإعادة النظر في أنظمتنا وقوانيننا التعليمية والأكاديمية السائدة، ليزول ذلك الخلط بين التخصصات، ولينص على ضرورة سنّ ضوابط لممارسات المهنة التعليمية والأكاديمية، وحدّ عقوبات أدبية تتخذ بحق كل مخالف لها.

أما الشرط الثاني: وهو الإحاطة والشمول فيتضمن تأكيداً على الشرط السابق من زاوية أن شرط المعلم إتقان مادة تخصصه وإتقان موضوع تدريسه، وذلك يستلزم الإحاطة بالجانب المعرفي منه كما يستلزم الإحاطة بالجانب المهاري المتعلق بالوسائل التعليمية والتربوية والأنشطة المختلفة الكفيلة بتحقيق هدف المنهج. كما أن من مستلزمات الإحاطة والشمول والإلمام الجيد بكل ما قد يكون ذا صلة بالتخصص أو موضوع الدرس من مختلف التخصصات الأخرى، وعدم الاقتصار على الكتاب المقرر، وبذلك تتحقق النظرة الكلية ويتم تجنب المعرفة الجزئية الضيقة.

وإذا التزم المعلم بهذا الشرط فإن انعكاسه المباشر سيظهر على تلامذته.
When we talk about these conditions, each of them includes direct educational aspects in which the sources of knowledge and its main methods interact, and benefit can be derived from them in the current reality of Islamic education. The condition of rootedness in knowledge includes the necessity of the learner mastering the scientific material he studies, so that he does not move from it to another until he becomes truly rooted in it, thereby achieving logical sequence in the curriculum. Likewise, the teacher – a fortiori – should not undertake to teach a practical subject until he is specialized in it, or has extensive knowledge that makes him rooted in his speech and handling of the paragraphs of that subject, so that he becomes like a scholar, not just an interested cultured person. When the phenomenon of abandoning original specializations began to spread in academic educational institutions, and every field became permissible for anyone who read and wrote, such that one could speak in every field and teach every specialization, then specializations became mixed and overlapped – I do not say integrated – in a way that led to generalization and superficiality, gave opportunity for claims, and made the specialist and the cultured person equals with no difference; rather, the astrologer and the astronomer, the doctor and the quack, the philosopher and the clown all became – unfortunately – before knowledge and science equal!! So does that align with the condition of rootedness in knowledge?

That calls us to reconsider our prevailing educational and academic systems and laws, so that this confusion between specializations is removed, and to stipulate the necessity of setting controls for the practices of the educational and academic profession, and to set ethical penalties to be taken against every violator.

As for the second condition: comprehensiveness and inclusivity, it includes an affirmation of the previous condition from the angle that the condition of the teacher is mastery of his specialization and mastery of the subject he teaches, and that requires comprehensiveness of the cognitive aspect of it as well as comprehensiveness of the skill aspect related to educational and pedagogical tools and various activities capable of achieving the goal of the curriculum. Also among the requirements of comprehensiveness and inclusivity is good familiarity with everything that may be related to the specialization or the subject of the lesson from various other specializations, and not limiting oneself to the prescribed book, thereby achieving a holistic view and avoiding narrow partial knowledge.

If the teacher adheres to this condition, its direct reflection will appear on his students.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage enumerates and explains three conditions for knowledge integration in Islamic education: rootedness in knowledge (الرسوخ في العلم), comprehensiveness and inclusivity (الإحاطة والشمول), and unity of knowledge (وحدة المعرفة), though the third is only introduced here. The author begins by stating that each condition has direct educational implications. The first condition, rootedness, requires the learner to master a subject before moving on, ensuring logical progression. The teacher must be specialized, not just a generalist. The author criticizes the trend where specialization is abandoned, leading to confusion between experts and amateurs, and between genuine scientists and charlatans. This condition calls for reform of academic systems to protect specialization. The second condition, comprehensiveness, complements the first by requiring the teacher to master both the cognitive and skill aspects of his field, and to be familiar with related disciplines, avoiding narrowness. The author emphasizes that this leads to a holistic view. The passage follows a logical flow: first identifying the problem (loss of specialization), then proposing the conditions as remedy. The commentary uses only the material present, explaining each point in the author's order.

Key Terms
الرسوخ في العلم
الإحاطة والشمول
وحدة المعرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the condition of 'rootedness in knowledge' primarily require from the learner?
A) To study multiple subjects simultaneously to gain breadth.
B) To master a subject before moving to another, ensuring logical sequence.
C) To rely only on the prescribed textbook.
D) To teach subjects without specialization.

Key Takeaway
The integration of knowledge in Islamic education begins with deep rootedness in one's specialization, followed by comprehensive coverage, all unified under the oneness of truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Evaluate a current Islamic studies curriculum: does it allow students to master one subject (e.g., ʿaqīdah) before moving to the next (e.g., fiqh)? If not, suggest how to incorporate the condition of rootedness.
?
Identify a real case where a teacher teaches a subject outside their specialization (e.g., a fiqh teacher teaching tafsīr without requisite knowledge). Explain how this violates the condition of rootedness and what the author would recommend.

Three Conditions for Teachers: From Depth to Unity of Knowledge
Author outlines three essential conditions for teachers and links them to revelation, reason, and sense.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and evaluate the three conditions for teachers outlined in the passage and apply them to the Islamic education context.

Core Idea
Mastering a subject is not enough; teachers must also have breadth and see knowledge as a unified whole.

The author warns against superficial claims to expertise and proposes three conditions that ensure genuine teaching: firm rooting (rusukh), comprehensiveness (ihatah), and unity of knowledge (wahdat al-ma'rifah). These conditions are not merely pedagogical but epistemological, rooted in the Islamic view of knowledge as integrated through revelation, reason, and sense.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
Find the three conditions the author states for teachers. They are: 1) firm rooting in knowledge, 2) comprehensiveness and inclusiveness, 3) observing the unity of knowledge.
2
Analyze how each condition prevents superficiality
The first condition prevents fake expertise, the second prevents narrowness, and the third prevents fragmentation. Write one sentence for each.
3
Connect conditions to epistemology
The author links these conditions to the sources of knowledge: revelation, reason, and sense. Identify how each condition relates to these sources.
4
Apply to Islamic education
The passage says these conditions are even more emphatic for Islamic education. Why? Because it is directly related to revelation.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الثالث - الوحي
لكل من قرأ وكتب بحيث إن بإمكانه التحدث في كل علم، والتدريس لكل تخصص، حينها اختلطت التخصصات وتداخلت - ولا أقول تكاملت – على نحو أفضى بها إلى التعميم والتسطيح وأتاح فرصة للادعاءات، وجعل من المتخصص والمثقف أقراناً بلا فرق بل غدا المنجم والفلكي، والطبيب والمشعوذ، والفيلسوف والمهرج جميعهم - مع الأسف - أمام المعرفة والعلم سواء بسواء!! فهل يتسق ذلك وشرط الرسوخ في العلم؟
•
إن ذلك يدعونا لإعادة النظر في أنظمتنا وقوانيننا التعليمية والأكاديمية السائدة، ليزول ذلك الخلط بين التخصصات، ولينص على ضرورة سنّ ضوابط لممارسات المهنة التعليمية والأكاديمية، وحدّ عقوبات أدبية تتخذ بحق كل مخالف لها.
أما الشرط الثاني: وهو الإحاطة والشمول فيتضمن تأكيداً على الشرط السابق من زاوية أن شرط المعلم إتقان مادة تخصصه وإتقان موضوع تدريسه، وذلك يستلزم الإحاطة بالجانب المعرفي منه كما يستلزم الإحاطة بالجانب المهاري المتعلق بالوسائل التعليمية والتربوية والأنشطة المختلفة الكفيلة بتحقيق هدف المنهج. كما أن من مستلزمات الإحاطة والشمول والإلمام الجيد بكل ما قد يكون ذا صلة بالتخصص أو موضوع الدرس من مختلف التخصصات الأخرى، وعدم الاقتصار على الكتاب المقرر ، وبذلك تتحقق النظرة الكلية ويتم تجنب المعرفة الجزئية الضيقة.
وإذا التزم المعلم بهذا الشرط فإن انعكاسه المباشر سيظهر على تلامذته. وأما الشرط الثالث: وهو مراعاة وحدة المعرفة فإنه يتضمن توازناً يكشف عن التلازم الموهوم بين إتقان التخصص مع الإحاطة والشمول بمفرداته وبين الضيق المعرفي الذي قد يوحي به التزام هذا المنحى. والحق أن الشرطين السابقين يكملان بعضهما، ولا يتعارضان أو يتضادان فمراعاة وحدة المعرفة تعني أن يكون المعلم عالماً بكل شيء - ما أمكنه – عن مادته وتخصصه، عالماً أو ملماً بشيء عن سائر المواد ولتخصصات الأخرى. وبذلك تتحد المعرفة وتتكامل ولا تتجزأ أو تتعارض، فيحصل اختلاف التنوع الإيجابي البناء، وينتفي اختلاف التضاد السلبي المدمر .
والحاصل أن هذه الشروط ومتضمناتها التربوية تنطبق على التخصصات جميعها، مثلما تنطبق على فروع التربية الإسلامية جميعها، بل هي في حق هذه الأخيرة أشد وأكد لأن النتائج المترتبة على الخطأ أو التقصير فيها ليست كالتقصير أو الخطأ في غيرها من التخصصات، إذ التربية الإسلامية على علاقة مباشرة بالوحي، في حين يتسع نطاق الاجتهاد وإعمال النظر الإنساني، ومصادر المعرفة الرئيسة والتبعية الأخرى في التخصصات غير الشرعية.
ومن إبداع البيان القرآني تلخيصه لعضوية العلاقة بين كل من الوحي والعقل والحس بقول الله تعالى:
وقَدْ جاءَكُمْ بَصَائِرُ مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ فَمَنْ أَبْصَرَ فَلِنَفْسِهِ وَمَنْ عَمِيَ فَعَلَيْهَا وَمَا أَنَا عَلَيْكُمْ بِحَفِيظيم [الأنعام: ١٠٤/٦].
إن هذه الآية - على سبيل المثال - تشير إلى القرآن الكريم باعتباره بصائر
حسية وعقلية بآن واحد. وحقاً فإن هذا أبلغ تعبير وأوجزه في تحديد المراد. وقد فَطِن إلى تلك الحقيقة ونبه عليها بعض أئمة المدارس الإسلامية الأقدمين فالإمام الرازي (ت: ٦٠٤هـ) من أئمة المتكلمين يقف عند تفسير الآية السابقة قائلا: (بصائر جمع البصيرة، وكما أن البصر اسم للإدراك التام الكامل الحاصل بالعين التي في الرأس، فالبصيرة للإدراك التام الحاصل في القلب. قال تعالى: بَلِ الإِنسانُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ بَصِيرَةً [القيامة: ١٤/٧٥] أي له نفسه معرفة تامة)(١).
(۱) الفخر الرازي، التفسير الكبير، ۱۰۹/۷ .
Chapter Three, Section Three: Revelation
Whoever reads and writes such that they can speak about every science and teach every specialization, then specializations become mixed and overlapped – I do not say integrated – in a way that led to generalization and superficiality, provided an opportunity for claims, and made the specialist and the cultured person peers without distinction. Rather, the astrologer and astronomer, the physician and the charlatan, the philosopher and the clown all became – unfortunately – before knowledge and science equal!! Is that consistent with the condition of being firmly rooted in knowledge?
•
That calls us to reconsider our prevailing educational and academic systems and laws, so that this confusion between specializations disappears, and to stipulate the necessity of enacting controls for educational and academic professional practices, and to set disciplinary penalties to be taken against every violator.
As for the second condition: which is comprehensiveness and inclusiveness, it includes an affirmation of the previous condition from the angle that the condition of the teacher is mastery of his specialization material and mastery of his teaching subject, and that requires comprehensive knowledge of its cognitive aspect, as well as comprehensive knowledge of the skill aspect related to educational and pedagogical methods and various activities capable of achieving the curriculum objective. Also among the requirements of comprehensiveness and inclusiveness is good familiarity with everything that may be related to the specialization or the subject of the lesson from various other specializations, and not limiting oneself to the prescribed textbook. Thus the holistic view is achieved and narrow partial knowledge is avoided.
If the teacher adheres to this condition, its direct effect will appear on his students. As for the third condition: which is observing the unity of knowledge, it includes a balance that reveals the illusory correlation between mastering the specialization with comprehensiveness and inclusiveness of its components and the cognitive narrowness that adhering to this approach may suggest. The truth is that the two previous conditions complement each other, and do not contradict or oppose each other. Observing the unity of knowledge means that the teacher should be knowledgeable about everything – as much as possible – concerning his subject and specialization, knowledgeable or familiar with something about all other materials and specializations. Thus knowledge unites and integrates and does not fragment or contradict, resulting in positive constructive diversity, and eliminating destructive negative conflicting difference.
The result is that these conditions and their educational implications apply to all specializations, just as they apply to all branches of Islamic education. Rather, they are more severe and emphatic with respect to the latter because the consequences of error or shortcoming in them are not like error or shortcoming in other specializations, since Islamic education is directly related to revelation, while the scope of ijtihad and human reasoning, and the primary and secondary sources of knowledge in non-Shar'i specializations, is wider.
Among the creativity of the Qur'anic explanation is its summary of the organic relationship between revelation, reason, and sense in the Almighty's saying: "Indeed, there have come to you insights from your Lord; so whoever sees clearly, it is for his own benefit, and whoever is blind, it is against himself; and I am not a keeper over you" [Al-An'am 6:104].
This verse – for example – refers to the Noble Qur'an as sensory and rational insights at once. Indeed, this is the most eloquent expression and the most concise in defining the intent. Some of the earlier imams of Islamic schools realized and alerted to that truth. Imam al-Razi (d. 604 AH), one of the imams of the theologians, when interpreting the previous verse, said: "Basa'ir is the plural of basirah. Just as 'basar' is the name for complete and perfect perception attained by the eye in the head, 'basirah' is for the complete perception attained in the heart. He said: 'Rather, man is a witness against himself' [Al-Qiyamah 75:14], meaning he has complete self-knowledge." (1) Fakhr al-Razi, al-Tafsir al-Kabir, 7/109.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage discusses three conditions for teachers, emphasizing the integration of knowledge and the relationship between revelation, reason, and sense. The author first criticizes the superficial mixing of specializations, where everyone claims expertise in everything, leading to dilution of knowledge. The first condition is 'rusukh fi al-'ilm' (firm rooting in knowledge), which requires genuine depth. The second condition is 'ihatah wa shumul' (comprehensiveness and inclusiveness), meaning the teacher must master both the cognitive content of their field and the pedagogical skills, while also being familiar with related disciplines to avoid narrowness. The third condition is 'ri'ayat wahdat al-ma'rifah' (observing the unity of knowledge), which balances specialization with breadth, ensuring that knowledge integrates rather than fragments. The author then applies these conditions especially to Islamic education because it is directly linked to revelation (wahy), whereas other fields can rely more on human reason and secondary sources. To illustrate the organic relationship between revelation, reason, and sense, the author cites Qur'an 6:104, which describes the Qur'an as 'basa'ir' (insights). He interprets this as the Qur'an being both sensory and rational insights simultaneously. He quotes Fakhr al-Razi's tafsir explaining 'basirah' as internal perception in the heart, analogous to 'basar' for the eye. This highlights that true knowledge integrates all sources: divine revelation, rational thought, and sensory experience.

The Quranic Epistemology: Revelation, Reason, and Sense as Unified Insights
Author links Quranic 'basa'ir' to the unity of revelation, reason, and sense.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to interpret the Quranic term 'basa'ir' as indicating the integration of sensory and rational knowledge, and relate it to the three sources of knowledge in Islam.

Core Idea
The Qur'an is described as 'basa'ir' — insights that are both sensory and rational, unifying the three sources of knowledge.

In this passage, the author uses Quran 6:104 to illustrate the organic relationship between revelation, reason, and sense. He explains that the Qur'an itself is described as 'basa'ir' (insights), which are both sensory and rational. Then he quotes Imam al-Razi's tafsir, which clarifies that 'basirah' is perception of the heart, analogous to 'basar' of the eye. This shows that true knowledge integrates all epistemic channels.

Guided Path
1
Locate the verse and its interpretation
Find Quran 6:104 and the author's claim that the Qur'an is 'sensory and rational insights at once'. Write down the key phrase.
2
Examine al-Razi's commentary
Al-Razi defines 'basirah' as perception of the heart. How does this connect to the idea that knowledge integrates senses and reason? Note the analogy: basar for eye, basirah for heart.
3
Identify the three sources
The passage mentions revelation (wahy), reason (aql), and sense (hiss). How does the verse capture all three? Revelation is the text itself, reason is the rational insight, sense is the sensory insight.
4
Apply the triad to a knowledge claim
Take a claim like 'the world is created'. How does each source contribute? Revelation affirms it, reason deduces it, senses observe contingency.
