أما الشرط الثاني: وهو الإحاطة والشمول فيتضمن تأكيداً على الشرط السابق من زاوية أن شرط المعلم إتقان مادة تخصصه وإتقان موضوع تدريسه، وذلك يستلزم الإحاطة بالجانب المعرفي منه كما يستلزم الإحاطة بالجانب المهاري المتعلق بالوسائل التعليمية والتربوية والأنشطة المختلفة الكفيلة بتحقيق هدف المنهج. كما أن من مستلزمات الإحاطة والشمول والإلمام الجيد بكل ما قد يكون ذا صلة بالتخصص أو موضوع الدرس من مختلف التخصصات الأخرى، وعدم الاقتصار على الكتاب المقرر ، وبذلك تتحقق النظرة الكلية ويتم تجنب المعرفة الجزئية الضيقة.
وإذا التزم المعلم بهذا الشرط فإن انعكاسه المباشر سيظهر على تلامذته. وأما الشرط الثالث: وهو مراعاة وحدة المعرفة فإنه يتضمن توازناً يكشف عن التلازم الموهوم بين إتقان التخصص مع الإحاطة والشمول بمفرداته وبين الضيق المعرفي الذي قد يوحي به التزام هذا المنحى. والحق أن الشرطين السابقين يكملان بعضهما، ولا يتعارضان أو يتضادان فمراعاة وحدة المعرفة تعني أن يكون المعلم عالماً بكل شيء - ما أمكنه – عن مادته وتخصصه، عالماً أو ملماً بشيء عن سائر المواد ولتخصصات الأخرى. وبذلك تتحد المعرفة وتتكامل ولا تتجزأ أو تتعارض، فيحصل اختلاف التنوع الإيجابي البناء، وينتفي اختلاف التضاد السلبي المدمر .
والحاصل أن هذه الشروط ومتضمناتها التربوية تنطبق على التخصصات جميعها، مثلما تنطبق على فروع التربية الإسلامية جميعها، بل هي في حق هذه الأخيرة أشد وأكد لأن النتائج المترتبة على الخطأ أو التقصير فيها ليست كالتقصير أو الخطأ في غيرها من التخصصات، إذ التربية الإسلامية على علاقة مباشرة بالوحي، في حين يتسع نطاق الاجتهاد وإعمال النظر الإنساني، ومصادر المعرفة الرئيسة والتبعية الأخرى في التخصصات غير الشرعية.
ومن إبداع البيان القرآني تلخيصه لعضوية العلاقة بين كل من الوحي والعقل والحس بقول الله تعالى:
وقَدْ جاءَكُمْ بَصَائِرُ مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ فَمَنْ أَبْصَرَ فَلِنَفْسِهِ وَمَنْ عَمِيَ فَعَلَيْهَا وَمَا أَنَا عَلَيْكُمْ بِحَفِيظيم [الأنعام: ١٠٤/٦].
إن هذه الآية - على سبيل المثال - تشير إلى القرآن الكريم باعتباره بصائر
حسية وعقلية بآن واحد. وحقاً فإن هذا أبلغ تعبير وأوجزه في تحديد المراد. وقد فَطِن إلى تلك الحقيقة ونبه عليها بعض أئمة المدارس الإسلامية الأقدمين فالإمام الرازي (ت: ٦٠٤هـ) من أئمة المتكلمين يقف عند تفسير الآية السابقة قائلا: (بصائر جمع البصيرة، وكما أن البصر اسم للإدراك التام الكامل الحاصل بالعين التي في الرأس، فالبصيرة للإدراك التام الحاصل في القلب. قال تعالى: بَلِ الإِنسانُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ بَصِيرَةً [القيامة: ١٤/٧٥] أي له نفسه معرفة تامة)(١).
(۱) الفخر الرازي، التفسير الكبير، ۱۰۹/۷ .
Chapter Three, Section Three: Revelation
Whoever reads and writes such that they can speak about every science and teach every specialization, then specializations become mixed and overlapped – I do not say integrated – in a way that led to generalization and superficiality, provided an opportunity for claims, and made the specialist and the cultured person peers without distinction. Rather, the astrologer and astronomer, the physician and the charlatan, the philosopher and the clown all became – unfortunately – before knowledge and science equal!! Is that consistent with the condition of being firmly rooted in knowledge?
•
That calls us to reconsider our prevailing educational and academic systems and laws, so that this confusion between specializations disappears, and to stipulate the necessity of enacting controls for educational and academic professional practices, and to set disciplinary penalties to be taken against every violator.
As for the second condition: which is comprehensiveness and inclusiveness, it includes an affirmation of the previous condition from the angle that the condition of the teacher is mastery of his specialization material and mastery of his teaching subject, and that requires comprehensive knowledge of its cognitive aspect, as well as comprehensive knowledge of the skill aspect related to educational and pedagogical methods and various activities capable of achieving the curriculum objective. Also among the requirements of comprehensiveness and inclusiveness is good familiarity with everything that may be related to the specialization or the subject of the lesson from various other specializations, and not limiting oneself to the prescribed textbook. Thus the holistic view is achieved and narrow partial knowledge is avoided.
If the teacher adheres to this condition, its direct effect will appear on his students. As for the third condition: which is observing the unity of knowledge, it includes a balance that reveals the illusory correlation between mastering the specialization with comprehensiveness and inclusiveness of its components and the cognitive narrowness that adhering to this approach may suggest. The truth is that the two previous conditions complement each other, and do not contradict or oppose each other. Observing the unity of knowledge means that the teacher should be knowledgeable about everything – as much as possible – concerning his subject and specialization, knowledgeable or familiar with something about all other materials and specializations. Thus knowledge unites and integrates and does not fragment or contradict, resulting in positive constructive diversity, and eliminating destructive negative conflicting difference.
The result is that these conditions and their educational implications apply to all specializations, just as they apply to all branches of Islamic education. Rather, they are more severe and emphatic with respect to the latter because the consequences of error or shortcoming in them are not like error or shortcoming in other specializations, since Islamic education is directly related to revelation, while the scope of ijtihad and human reasoning, and the primary and secondary sources of knowledge in non-Shar'i specializations, is wider.
Among the creativity of the Qur'anic explanation is its summary of the organic relationship between revelation, reason, and sense in the Almighty's saying: "Indeed, there have come to you insights from your Lord; so whoever sees clearly, it is for his own benefit, and whoever is blind, it is against himself; and I am not a keeper over you" [Al-An'am 6:104].
This verse – for example – refers to the Noble Qur'an as sensory and rational insights at once. Indeed, this is the most eloquent expression and the most concise in defining the intent. Some of the earlier imams of Islamic schools realized and alerted to that truth. Imam al-Razi (d. 604 AH), one of the imams of the theologians, when interpreting the previous verse, said: "Basa'ir is the plural of basirah. Just as 'basar' is the name for complete and perfect perception attained by the eye in the head, 'basirah' is for the complete perception attained in the heart. He said: 'Rather, man is a witness against himself' [Al-Qiyamah 75:14], meaning he has complete self-knowledge." (1) Fakhr al-Razi, al-Tafsir al-Kabir, 7/109.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage discusses three conditions for teachers, emphasizing the integration of knowledge and the relationship between revelation, reason, and sense. The author first criticizes the superficial mixing of specializations, where everyone claims expertise in everything, leading to dilution of knowledge. The first condition is 'rusukh fi al-'ilm' (firm rooting in knowledge), which requires genuine depth. The second condition is 'ihatah wa shumul' (comprehensiveness and inclusiveness), meaning the teacher must master both the cognitive content of their field and the pedagogical skills, while also being familiar with related disciplines to avoid narrowness. The third condition is 'ri'ayat wahdat al-ma'rifah' (observing the unity of knowledge), which balances specialization with breadth, ensuring that knowledge integrates rather than fragments. The author then applies these conditions especially to Islamic education because it is directly linked to revelation (wahy), whereas other fields can rely more on human reason and secondary sources. To illustrate the organic relationship between revelation, reason, and sense, the author cites Qur'an 6:104, which describes the Qur'an as 'basa'ir' (insights). He interprets this as the Qur'an being both sensory and rational insights simultaneously. He quotes Fakhr al-Razi's tafsir explaining 'basirah' as internal perception in the heart, analogous to 'basar' for the eye. This highlights that true knowledge integrates all sources: divine revelation, rational thought, and sensory experience.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic term 'basa'ir' demonstrates that revelation, reason, and sense are integrated in Islamic epistemology, providing a unified framework for knowledge.

The Role of Reason in Revelation: General and Specific Functions
Author explains the role of reason in understanding revelation and lists its three functions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three specific functions of reason in relation to revelation and explain how the text's definitiveness affects reason's role.

Core Idea
Reason and revelation are complementary; reason affirms, understands, and applies revelation.

The author begins by critiquing those who reject ideas out of ignorance. He then establishes that reason has a clear role in understanding revelation, not as a competitor but as a partner. He outlines that reason's task varies with the text's certainty and then enumerates three concrete functions: affirming revelation, understanding the purposes of divine laws, and applying principles to changing circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's initial critique
Notice how the author starts by describing the lazy rejection of unknown ideas. This sets the stage for the need to properly understand reason's role.
2
Determine the two initial functions
The author first lists two broad means: a) determining textual signification, b) estimating intentions. Understand these as the basic operations.
3
Note the variation based on certainty
The text states that reason's work differs based on the text's definitiveness (qat'i) or conjecture (dhanni). This is a key principle: the more definitive, the less interpretive work.
This principle is central to Usul al-Fiqh.
4
Extract the three specific functions
Read carefully the numbered list on page 327: tasdiq al-wahy, fiqh al-shara'i', and applying reason to changing circumstances. Understand each.
These functions illustrate reason's active role.
5
Reflect on the integration
The author emphasizes that these roles stem from the integration of reason and revelation, not conflict.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الثالث - الوحي
ولأن الإنسان عدو ما جهل، فإن أقرب شيء يريح العاجز الكسول هو أن يسارع إلى إعلان أحكام الرفض والإنكار، دون أن يكلف نفسه عناء البحث والنقاش وفق الأصول المعتبرة، والقواعد والأسس المرعية عند الراسخين في الشريعة والحكمة على حد سواء.
وعلى هذا الأساس فإن ثمة دوراً للعقل في الوحي، وآخر للوحي في العقل،
ولنبدأ بالأول:
أولاً- دور العقل في الوحي
يقصد بدور العقل في الوحي دور المعرفة العقلية أو المعرفة الفلسفية - كما يحلو لبعض الباحثين أن يرادف بينهما (۱) في فهم الدين، فتكون معرفة العقل عبارة عن كسبه الذاتي في المعارف والعلوم المتعلقة بميادين الآفاق والأنفس، ليتحدد دوره في فهم الهدي الديني وطبيعة دوره. وسبيل ذلك:
أ. تعيين المدلول النصي.
ب. تقدير المقاصد (۲).
وبتعبير أكثر تفصيلاً نقول: إنه بناء على طبيعة دور العقل في فهم الدين، وعلى الأسس التي يقوم عليها ذلك الفهم ينهض العقل بالاجتهاد، بغية تحديد المراد الإلهي من خلال النص، عندما يصاغ بأحكام تتعلق بأفعال الإنسان فيما ينبغي أن تكون عليه.
ويختلف عمل العقل في تفهم النص باختلاف النص ذاته، من حيث وروده، ومن حيث دلالته أي من حيث القطعية والظنية. ولذلك فكلما علت حظوظ القطع سهل دور العقل، وكلما ضعفت عظم ذلك الدور، وحقت به المصاعب.
(۱) حمدي زقزوق الدين والفلسفة ١٤ .
(۲) عبد المجيد النجار، في فقه التدين فهماً وتنزيلاً، ۹۹/۱-۱۱۱.
وبصيغة أكثر تحديداً يمكن تلخيص اجتهاد العقل في فهم الدين من خلال:
أ. اجتهاد العقل في النص القطعي وروداً ودلالة.
ب. اجتهاد العقل في النص الظني وروداً ودلالة(۱).
إن هذا الدور للمعرفة العقلية إنما يتحقق من منطلق التكامل القائم بين العقل والوحي، وفي ضوء ذلك يقوم العقل بما يلي:
١ - تصديق الوحي: أي إن القرآن الكريم إنما حث العقل على التفكر والتدبر والتأمل..إلخ. لأنه يثق بقدرة العقل الصحيح على تمييز الوحي الصادق عن الادعاء الزائف للوحي. ومن جانب آخر فإنه لما كان الوحي مسؤولية والتزاماً بالواجبات وانتهاء عن المحرمات فإن تصديق العقل للوحي ضروري ليقوم بمهمته التزاماً وانتهاء، إذ هو مناط التكليف.
۲- فقه الشرائع أي إن معرفة أصول الأحكام وتشريعها عملية عقلية تتم من خلال إعمال العقل في النصوص، إذ نجد في القرآن الكريم كلمات من مثل من أجل ذلك أو (كذلك) أو (( لكي لا ، لتدل على ضرورة فقه الشرائع ومقاصدها، ولا يتم ذلك إلا عن طريق العقل.
٣- العقل والمناهج التطبيقية ونقصد بذلك جوانب الثبات والتطور في الشريعة الإسلامية. فعنصر الثبات هو تأسيس أصل المبدأ أما عنصر التطور فقابل لتطبيق المبدأ وفق شروط التطبيق المتغير من حين لآخر. ومن هنا جاء النص به كمبدأ يلتزم ولكن لم يرد النص بتفصيلاته، ليقوم العقل باختيار الصيغة الأنسب من زمان لآخر ومن بيئة اجتماعية إلى بيئة أخرى (٢). وباختصار فإن مظاهر أدوار العقل في الوحي تتجلى من خلال وظيفتين هامتين هما:
(۱) المرجع السابق، ۹۷/۱-۱۰۰.
(۲) زكي الميلاد، الفكر الإسلامي بين التأصل والتجديد، ٣٥٩-٣٦٢.
Chapter Three: Section Three - Revelation. And because man is hostile to what he is ignorant of, the closest thing that relieves the incapable lazy person is to hasten to declare judgments of rejection and denial, without bothering himself with the trouble of research and discussion according to the considered principles, and the rules and foundations observed by those firmly rooted in both Sharia and wisdom. And on this basis, there is a role for reason in revelation, and another for revelation in reason. Let us begin with the first: First: The role of reason in revelation. By the role of reason in revelation is meant the role of rational knowledge or philosophical knowledge - as some researchers like to synonymize between them (1) - in understanding religion. So rational knowledge consists of its self-acquisition of knowledge and sciences related to the fields of horizons and souls, to determine its role in understanding religious guidance and the nature of its role. The means for that are: a. Determining the textual signification. b. Estimating the intentions (2). In more detailed terms we say: Based on the nature of reason's role in understanding religion, and on the foundations upon which that understanding is based, reason undertakes ijtihad, to determine the divine intent through the text, when it is formulated in rulings related to human actions as they should be. And the work of reason in understanding the text varies according to the text itself, in terms of its transmission and its indication, i.e., in terms of definitiveness and conjecture. Therefore, the higher the chances of definitiveness, the easier the role of reason, and the weaker they are, the greater that role and the more difficulties it encounters. (1) Hamdi Zaqzuq, Religion and Philosophy, p. 14. (2) Abdul Majeed al-Najjar, On the Jurisprudence of Religiosity: Understanding and Application, 1/99-111. In more specific terms, the ijtihad of reason in understanding religion can be summarized through: a. The ijtihad of reason in the text that is definitive in transmission and indication. b. The ijtihad of reason in the text that is conjectural in transmission and indication (1). This role of rational knowledge is achieved from the standpoint of integration between reason and revelation. In light of this, reason does the following: 1. Affirming revelation: That is, the Noble Qur'an urged reason to think, ponder, contemplate, etc., because it trusts the ability of sound reason to distinguish true revelation from false claims of revelation. And on the other hand, since revelation is a responsibility and commitment to duties and avoidance of prohibitions, reason's affirmation of revelation is necessary for it to carry out its mission of commitment and avoidance, for it is the basis of obligation. 2. Jurisprudence of divine laws: That is, knowledge of the principles of rulings and their legislation is a rational process carried out through the use of reason in the texts. In the Noble Qur'an we find words like 'because of that' or 'thus' or 'so that not' to indicate the necessity of understanding the laws and their purposes, and this is only achieved through reason. 3. Reason and applied methodologies: By this we mean the aspects of constancy and development in Islamic law. The element of constancy is the establishment of the principle itself, while the element of development is the applicability of the principle according to the changing conditions of application from time to time. Hence the text came with it as a principle to be adhered to, but the text did not come with its details, so that reason may choose the most appropriate form from time to time and from one social environment to another (2). In summary, the manifestations of the roles of reason in revelation are manifested through two important functions: (1) Previous reference, 1/97-100. (2) Zaki al-Milad, Islamic Thought between Authenticity and Renewal, pp. 359-362.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage from a contemporary work on Islam discusses the role of reason (al-'aql) in relation to revelation (al-wahy). It opens with a psychological observation that ignorance breeds hostility, leading some to reject ideas without proper investigation. The author asserts that reason and revelation have mutual roles; here the focus is on reason's role in understanding revelation. Rational knowledge, including philosophy, helps in grasping religious guidance. Two concrete functions are mentioned: (a) determining the literal meaning of the text, and (b) identifying the underlying intentions or purposes (maqasid). The author then elaborates that reason's ijtihad varies based on whether the text is definitive (qat'i) or speculative (dhanni) in transmission and meaning; the more definitive, the less room for interpretation. On page 327, the author lists three specific functions of reason: (1) tasdiq al-wahy—reason verifies the truth of revelation, as the Qur'an itself invites reflection, and without rational assent, religious obligation cannot be meaningful; (2) fiqh al-shara'i'—reason comprehends the principles and objectives behind sacred laws, using linguistic cues like 'li'alla' (so that not); (3) reason and applied methodologies—reason mediates between fixed principles and changing circumstances, selecting suitable applications over time. The passage concludes by noting that these roles manifest in two overarching functions (though not fully detailed here). Throughout, the author emphasizes the complementarity of reason and revelation, not conflict.

Complementarity of Revelation and Reason
Author summarizes the complementary roles of revelation and reason and critiques the false dichotomy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the domains of revelation and reason as presented in the passage and critique the false dichotomy between them.

Core Idea
Revelation sets fixed principles; reason navigates changing means—they are partners, not rivals.

This passage clarifies that revelation and reason are not in conflict but serve complementary functions. Understanding their proper relationship is essential for Islamic sciences and for diagnosing the modern crisis of the Muslim mind.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two pillars
Find where the author states that revelation is the pillar of constants (thawabit) and reason is the pillar of variables (mutaghayyirat). Notice the parallel structure.
2
Distinguish their domains
What does revelation handle? (goals, universals, principles). What does reason handle? (means, methods, particulars). The author also mentions that revelation deals with principles and universals, while reason deals with branches and particulars.
3
Understand the relationship
The author says the relationship is mutual support, integration, and intertwining. They are not in conflict; any apparent contradiction is resolved through interpretation (ta'wil).
4
Recognize the false duality
Why does the author say the duality is baseless? He traces its origin to a foreign cultural invasion and the European reaction to church authority, not to Islamic thought.
5
Apply to Islamic education
How does this complementarity work in Islamic education? Reason interacts with the sensory world through contemplation and experimentation, guided by revelation's directives, to fulfill humanity's vicegerent role.

وحاصل القول: إن ركيزة الثوابت الوحي، وركيزة المتغيرات العقل. فالأهداف والغايات يمثلها محور الثوابت، أما المرونة والمتغيرات فتمثلها الوسائل والأساليب المتغيرة تبعاً للزمان والمكان. ولذا كان هذا منطقة عمل العقل. ومن ناحية أخرى يشتغل الوحي في قضايا الأصول والكليات، في حين يشتغل العقل في قضايا الفروع والجزئيات وذلك على نحو عام. وينعكس ذلك عملياً في ميدان التربية الإسلامية على النحو التالي: يقوم العقل الإنساني بالتفاعل مع الكون بشتى صور التفاعل الإيجابي كالتأمل والتجريب لمحتوياته الحسية والإفادة من ذلك في أداء أدوار الإنسان الاستخلافية على الأرض، في ضوء توجيهات الوحي وإرشاداته. وإذ تبين لنا أن سمة العلاقة بين الوحي والنقل هي التعاضد والتكامل والتعانق، وأن الخلاف الذي دار بين الفرق الإسلامية وبعضها ليس حول حجيتهما أو أحدهما، وإنما حول مظاهر التعارض التي قد تبرز بينهما، فيلجؤون إلى البحث عن آلية في التأويل. إذا تبين ذلك فلا مساغ ألبتة في افتعال ثنائية العقل والنقل، لتقصى الأولى على حساب الأخرى أو العكس. إن انتقال هذه الثنائية إلى العالم الإسلامي غريب، وقد تسللت إليه غداة الغزوة الثقافية لديار المسلمين، والتي أدت إلى استلاب حضاري بات العقل المسلم يعاني من ضغطها إلى الحد الذي أفقده التوازن في معيارية القيمة، كما تسبب في إضعاف الرؤية عنده، وخلخة الصوابية في تصوره للقضايا وإصداره للأحكام. ولعل اختلاق هذه القضية بين العقل والنقل أبرز مظاهر أزمة العقل المسلم المعاصر بحق. وحين نؤكد على غرابة هذا المسلك في التفكير فإنما نشير بذلك إلى أن المدرسة العقلية لم تنشأ إلا في أوروبا النهضة، بدافع رد الفعل على سلطان الكنيسة، التي أوهنت العقل من جانب، ورد اعتبار للعقل الذي بدأت تسخر منه الاتجاهات الحسية لديهم من جانب آخر.
The sum of the statement: The pillar of constants is revelation, and the pillar of variables is reason. Goals and objectives are represented by the axis of constants, while flexibility and variables are represented by the means and methods that change according to time and place. Therefore, this is the domain of reason's work. On the other hand, revelation operates in matters of principles and universals, while reason operates in matters of branches and particulars, in a general manner. This is reflected practically in the field of Islamic education as follows: The human mind interacts with the universe in various forms of positive interaction, such as contemplation and experimentation of its sensory contents, and benefits from that in performing the human vicegerent roles on earth, in light of revelation's guidance and directives. Since it has become clear to us that the characteristic of the relationship between revelation and transmitted knowledge is mutual support, integration, and intertwining, and that the disagreement that occurred among Islamic sects and some of them is not about their authority or that of one of them, but rather about manifestations of contradiction that may appear between them, so they resort to seeking a mechanism for interpretation. If that is clear, then there is absolutely no room for fabricating a duality of reason and transmitted knowledge, such that one is marginalized at the expense of the other or vice versa. The transmission of this duality to the Islamic world is strange, and it infiltrated it on the morning of the cultural invasion of Muslim lands, which led to a civilizational alienation that the Muslim mind suffers from under its pressure to the extent that it lost balance in the normativity of value, and also caused a weakening of its vision and a distortion of correctness in its perception of issues and its issuance of judgments. Perhaps the fabrication of this issue between reason and transmitted knowledge is truly the most prominent manifestation of the crisis of the contemporary Muslim mind. When we emphasize the strangeness of this path of thought, we are thereby pointing out that the rational school only arose in Renaissance Europe, as a reaction to the authority of the church, which weakened reason on one hand, and restored the status of reason that the sensory trends had begun to mock on the other hand.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological argument that delineates the proper relationship between revelation (wahy) and reason ('aql) and critiques the false dichotomy between them. The author first establishes that revelation is the foundation for constants (thawabit) such as goals and principles, while reason is the foundation for variables (mutaghayyirat) such as means and methods that change with time and place. Reason operates in the domain of flexibility, whereas revelation handles universals and principles. In practical Islamic education, reason interacts with the sensory world through contemplation and experimentation to fulfill humanity's vicegerent role, guided by revelation. The author then asserts that the true relationship between revelation and transmitted knowledge (naql) is mutual support and integration, not conflict. Any apparent contradiction is resolved through interpretation (ta'wil). Therefore, fabricating a duality where one is elevated over the other is baseless. The author traces the origin of this duality to a foreign cultural invasion and the European reaction to church authority, not to Islamic thought. This duality is identified as a key symptom of the contemporary Muslim mind's crisis, causing imbalance and distorted judgment.

Key Terms
الوحي
العقل
الثوابت
المتغيرات
النقل

Key Takeaway
Revelation and reason are not adversaries but complementary—revelation provides constants, reason manages variables in light of revelation.

Critique of Double Standards in Labeling Islamic Thought as Non-Rational
Author critiques a writer's double standard in labeling Greek thought rational and Islamic thought mystical.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and critique the logical double standard in comparing Islamic and Greek methods of reasoning, and distinguish the epistemic superiority of Islamic qiyas al-gha'ib.

Core Idea
The same method yields certainty in Islamic thought but only conjecture in Greek logic.

Many modern writers claim that Islamic thought is mystical and lacks rationality, contrasting it with Greek philosophy. But this critique fails to recognize that both traditions use analogical reasoning (qiyas al-gha'ib 'ala al-shahid). The author exposes the double standard and argues that Muslim scholars apply it with greater rigor, achieving certainty (yaqeen) rather than mere conjecture (zann). In this lesson, you will analyze this critique and its implications for understanding Islamic rationality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the double standard
Look at the writer's characterization: Greek thought as rational/objective vs Islamic as faith-based/unseen. Ask: is this distinction fair?
Notice the asymmetry in labeling.
2
Recognize the common method
Both traditions use qiyas al-gha'ib 'ala al-shahid. Note that this is a shared scientific method.
The method is 'common' as stated in the text.
3
Distinguish the epistemic outcome
Muslim scholars achieve certainty (yaqeen) through scrutiny; Aristotelian method yields only conjecture (zann). This is the crucial difference.
The text emphasizes 'scrutiny leading to certainty'.
4
Formulate the logical question
The author asks: if method is common, why the unequal labeling? This exposes inconsistency.
The rhetorical question forces a reconsideration of the labels.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما يقال عن قياس الغائب على الشاهد فذلك منهج علمي مشترك، اتبعه الأصوليون من علماء المسلمين، كما انتهجه أتباع المنهج الأرسططاليسي، بفارق جوهري هو أنه عند المسلمين من التحري بحيث يؤدي إلى اليقين، في حين أنه لا يحقق سوى الظن في القياس الأرسططاليسي(٢)، وهذا يبدد وصف الكاتب في موطن لاحق وهو ينم عن انهزام حضاري حقيقي للذات أمام الآخر - للفكر اليوناني بالعقلانية والموضوعية في مقابل الفكر الإسلامي ذي الصبغة الإيمانية الغيبية. والسؤال المنطقي هنا أو ليس قياس الغائب على الشاهد منهجاً مشتركاً بين الفريقين، فلماذا وصف الآخر بالعقلانية والموضوعية، والذات بالإيمان والغيب بما يعني غياب العقلانية والموضوعية لدى المسلمين؟
As for what is said about analogical reasoning from the observed to the unobserved, that is a common scientific method, followed by the legal theorists among Muslim scholars, and also followed by the followers of the Aristotelian method, with an essential difference: among Muslims it is carried out with such scrutiny that it leads to certainty, whereas in the Aristotelian analogy it only achieves conjecture (2). This dispels the writer's later description, which betrays a real civilizational defeat of the self before the other—attributing rationality and objectivity to Greek thought in contrast to Islamic thought with its faith-based and unseen character. The logical question here: Is not analogical reasoning from the observed to the unobserved a common method between the two groups? So why did he describe the other as rational and objective, and the self as faith and unseen, implying the absence of rationality and objectivity among Muslims?
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on a writer who contrasted Greek philosophy (rational and objective) with Islamic thought (faith-based and unseen). The author argues that both traditions use the method of qiyas al-gha'ib 'ala al-shahid (analogy from the observed to the unobserved). The key difference is that Muslim scholars apply rigorous scrutiny leading to yaqeen (certainty), while Aristotle's followers only achieve zann (conjecture). Thus, the writer's characterization is unfounded and reflects a civilizational defeat complex. The author exposes the double standard: if both use the same method, why label one rational and the other not?

Key Takeaway
The double standard in labeling Islamic thought as non-rational collapses when both traditions rely on the same analogical method, with Muslims achieving higher epistemic certainty.

The Philosophical Meaning of Hads and Its Linguistic Defense
Author defines hads in multiple philosophical senses and defends the technical usage against language purists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key philosophical definitions of hads (intuition) and explain why the technical meaning does not require literal linguistic correspondence.

Core Idea
Hads is direct sudden knowledge, defined by al-Razi as a mean between unknowns, and its technical use builds on linguistic roots.

In this passage, the author presents multiple philosophical definitions of hads (intuition) — from direct perception to sudden insight — and cites al-Fakhr al-Razi's definition as a mean between the two ends of the unknown. The passage also addresses a criticism that the philosophical use strays from the literal meaning, and defends it by explaining that technical terms are grounded in the essence of the word, not its letter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the various definitions
List the different senses of hads given: direct perception, soul's direct awareness, rapid sudden perception, and the mind's uncovering of truths by sudden inspiration.
These definitions share the theme of immediacy and lack of discursive reasoning.
2
Examine al-Razi's definition
Al-Fakhr al-Razi defines hads as 'a mean between the two ends of the unknown' and the soul's readiness to find that mean. Understand the structure: two unknowns (the extremes) and a middle term that intuition discovers.
This definition highlights the function of intuition in bridging gaps in knowledge.
3
Note the evolution into intuitionism
The concept evolved into a full epistemic school (intuitionism), where intuition is the sole path to absolute knowledge, as claimed by Henri Bergson.
This shows the expansion of a term from a mental faculty to a comprehensive epistemological doctrine.
4
Analyze the linguistic critique
A researcher objects that the philosophical use of hads meaning 'rapid transition' is not found in Arabic dictionaries. Identify the objection and the author's response.
The critic insists on literal conformity.
5
Understand the author's defense
The author argues that technical terms do not need to match literal meanings; they rely on the core essence of the word. Since 'direct perception' is a linguistic meaning, it supports the philosophical sense of quick understanding.
This principle is common in Islamic sciences: technical terms expand on linguistic roots.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المعنى الفلسفي للحدس فيأتي بمعنى: الإدراك المباشر لموضوع التفكين)(۱) . وبمعنى: «اطلاع النفس المباشر على ما يمثله لها الحس الظاهر، أو الحس الباطن من صور حسيّة أو نفسية، أو على كشف الذهن عن بعض الحقائق بوحي مفاجئ لا على سبيل الاستقراء أو الاستنتاج، ولكن على سبيل المشاهدة، التي ينبلج فيها الحق انبلاجاً)) (۳). كما يأتي الحدس بمعنى: «الإدراك السريع المفاجئ للموقف أو الحقيقة، دون حاجة إلى حس خارجي، أو استدلال (٣) . وعرفه الفخر الرازي (ت: ٦٠٤ هـ ) بأنه عبارة عن متوسط بين طرفي المجهول، واستعداد النفس لوجدان ذلك المتوسط هو الحنس ) وتطور مفهوم الحدس حتى غدا مذهباً في المعرفة يعرف بالمذهب الحدسي (Intuitionism). ويشار إلى أن هنري برجسون (Henri Bergson) الفيلسوف الفرنسي (ت: ١٩٤١م) يَعدُّ هذا المذهب السبيل الوحيد لمعرفة المطلق). وأحياناً يطلق على المذهب الذي يقول باعتماد المعرفة على الحدس (الحدسية)(1). ويستدرك أحد الباحثين على استعمال الفلاسفة للحنس بمعنى سرعة الانتقال والفهم والاستنتاج بأنه ليس استعمالاً جاءت به اللغة، ولا أقر في معاجمها (۳). وكأنه يعني حرفية المعنى، ولكن من المعلوم بأن المعنى الاصطلاحي لا يلتزم حرفية المعنى اللغوي، وإنما يعتمد على جوهره لتجسير المعنيين. وإذا كانت اللغة قد قالت بأن من معاني الحدس إدراك الشيء إدراكاً مباشراً فإن ذلك مستند قوي للاصطلاح الفلسفي القائل بسرعة الانتقال والفهم والاستنتاج.
As for the philosophical meaning of intuition (hads), it comes in the sense of: direct perception of the object of thought. And in the sense of: 'the soul's direct awareness of what the external sense or internal sense represents to it of sensory or psychological images, or the mind's uncovering of some truths by sudden inspiration, not through induction or deduction, but through witnessing, in which the truth dawns brightly.' Also, intuition comes in the sense of: 'rapid sudden perception of the situation or truth, without need for external sense or inference.' Al-Fakhr al-Razi (d. 604 AH) defined it as: a mean between the two ends of the unknown, and the soul's readiness to find that mean is intuition. The concept of intuition developed until it became a school of knowledge known as intuitionism. It is noted that Henri Bergson, the French philosopher (d. 1941 AD), considers this school the sole path to knowledge of the absolute. Sometimes the school that holds that knowledge relies on intuition is called intuitionism. One researcher criticizes the philosophers' use of hads to mean rapid transition and understanding and deduction, saying it is not a usage that came from the language, nor is it established in its dictionaries. He seems to mean literal meaning, but it is known that the technical meaning does not adhere to the literal linguistic meaning, but rather relies on its essence to bridge the two meanings. And if the language has said that among the meanings of hads is direct perception of something, then that is a strong support for the philosophical convention that means rapid transition and understanding and deduction.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'hads' (intuition) in its philosophical sense. The author begins by giving multiple definitions: direct perception of the object of thought, the soul's immediate awareness of sensory or psychological images, or the mind's discovery of truths through sudden inspiration rather than induction or deduction. Another definition is rapid sudden perception of a situation or truth without external sense or inference. The author then mentions al-Fakhr al-Razi's definition: intuition is a mean between the two ends of the unknown, and the soul's readiness to find that mean. The passage then notes that the concept evolved into a full epistemic school (intuitionism), citing Henri Bergson who considers it the only way to know the absolute. Finally, the author addresses a critique: a researcher argued that the philosophical use of hads as 'rapid transition' is not linguistically justified. The author responds by explaining that technical terms do not need to match literal meanings exactly; they are built on the core essence. Since language includes 'direct perception' among the meanings of hads, this supports the philosophical meaning of quick understanding.

Key Takeaway
Hads (intuition) in philosophy refers to immediate, direct knowledge, and its technical meaning is justified by building on the linguistic core rather than literal correspondence.

Distinguishing Hads and Ilham
Author discusses overlap between hads and ilham.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the distinction and overlap between hads (intuition) and ilham (inspiration) as presented in the passage.

Core Idea
Hads and ilham overlap but are not identical—hads has unique psychological features.

In this passage, the author addresses a confusion that arises between two important epistemological concepts: hads (intuition) and ilham (inspiration). While some scholars use the terms interchangeably, the author insists that hads retains its own distinct characteristics. Understanding this distinction is crucial for anyone studying the sources of knowledge in Islam, as it affects how we evaluate claims of intuitive certainty versus divinely inspired insights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms being discussed
Find the Arabic terms 'الحدس' and 'الإلهام' in the passage. Note that the author says some use one term synonymously with the other.
Look for the phrase 'مرادفا للمصطلح الآخر' meaning synonymously.
2
Recognize the cause of overlap
The author attributes the overlap to a 'disagreement' (خلاف). Understand that this disagreement is methodological or terminological, not necessarily substantive.
The passage begins 'ويبدو أن هذا الخلاف سبب مباشر' - this disagreement is a direct cause.
3
Extract the author's position on hads
Despite the overlap, the author affirms that hads has 'special characteristics and manifestations' (سمات ومظاهر خاصة). This is the key distinction.
Note the contrastive phrase 'وإن كان هذا لا يغير' - this does not change the fact.
4
Apply the distinction to an Islamic example
Consider a scenario: a scholar feels an immediate certainty about a ruling on a novel issue. If he can articulate the 'illa, it is likely qiyas; if not, it may be hads. If he claims divine guidance, it may be ilham. This passage helps categorize such claims.
This step connects theory to practice in Islamic law and theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبدو أن هذا الخلاف سبب مباشر في التداخل الذي يبرز أحيانا بين الحدس والإلهام، فنجد أن ثمة من يستخدم هذا المصطلح مرادفا للمصطلح الآخر (۱). وإن كان هذا لا يغير من حقيقة وجود الحدس بسمات ومظاهر خاصة. ولعل أبرز ما يستدعي التوقف في ظاهرة الحدس ما يؤكد عليه علماء النفس الحديث من أنه غدا بإمكان الإنسان الوصول إلى استنتاجات يثبت بعد ذلك صحتها، بيد أنه لا يستطيع شرح الأسس التي تقوم عليها هذه الاستنتاجات أو الطرائق التي سلكها في سبيلها. هذا مع أن الناس يختلفون في غيرها من القدرات. ومن المؤشرات الوجدانية على صحة الاستنتاج شعور المرء بالسرور والارتياح وكذلك اليقين على مستوى الذات (۳). كما أنه من الملفت للنظر حقاً ما يلاحظ من سرعة تقدير لما يحتاج إليه الموقف المفاجئ من عمل حاسم، وذلك ما يعتقد أنه من أبرز المظاهر المميزة لذوي القوى الحدسية (۳).
It seems that this disagreement is a direct cause of the overlap that sometimes appears between hads (intuition) and ilham (inspiration), for we find that some use this term synonymously with the other. Although this does not change the fact that hads has special characteristics and manifestations. Perhaps the most noteworthy point that calls for reflection in the phenomenon of hads is what modern psychologists emphasize: that it has become possible for a person to reach conclusions whose correctness is later proven, yet he cannot explain the foundations on which these conclusions rest or the methods he followed in reaching them. This while people differ in other abilities. Among the emotional indicators of the correctness of a conclusion is the person's feeling of pleasure and comfort as well as certainty at the subjective level. Also, it is truly striking the observed rapid assessment of what a sudden situation requires of decisive action, and this is believed to be one of the most prominent distinguishing features of those with intuitive powers.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage discusses the relationship between hads (intuition) and ilham (inspiration). The author notes that a disagreement among scholars has caused these two terms to sometimes be used interchangeably, though hads retains its own distinct characteristics. The main focus is on a psychological phenomenon: a person can reach conclusions that later prove correct without being able to explain the reasoning behind them. This inability to articulate the process is a key feature of intuition. Additionally, the author mentions emotional indicators of correctness, such as pleasure and subjective certainty. Finally, the passage highlights the rapid assessment needed in sudden situations as a hallmark of intuitive individuals.

الإلهام

Key Takeaway

Psychological Indicators of Intuitive Conclusions
Author lists psychological indicators of intuitive conclusions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and recognize the psychological indicators of intuitive conclusions as described in the passage.

Core Idea
Intuitive conclusions come with emotional certainty and rapid assessment, even without explicable reasoning.

Continuing from the distinction between hads and ilham, the passage delves into the psychological features of intuition (hads). Modern psychologists, as cited by the author, observe that people can reach correct conclusions without being able to explain their reasoning. Moreover, these conclusions are accompanied by feelings of pleasure and subjective certainty, and intuitive individuals are noted for their rapid decision-making in sudden situations. Understanding these indicators helps us identify when intuition is at work in Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key psychological claim
The passage says a person can reach conclusions that later prove correct, yet cannot explain the foundations or methods. This is the core of the intuitive phenomenon.
Look for the phrase 'لا يستطيع شرح الأسس' - cannot explain the foundations.
2
Extract the emotional indicators
The author mentions emotional indicators: feeling of pleasure, comfort, and subjective certainty (اليقين على مستوى الذات). These are internal signs that the conclusion is correct.
The phrase 'المؤشرات الوجدانية' refers to emotional/affective indicators.
3
Note the behavioral indicator
Rapid assessment of sudden situations requiring decisive action is highlighted as a distinguishing feature of intuitive individuals.
The passage calls it 'سرعة تقدير' (rapid assessment) and 'عمل حاسم' (decisive action).
4
Apply to an Islamic context
Consider a scholar who gives a fatwa instantly when asked about a new issue. He may feel strong certainty but cannot produce a detailed qiyas. According to the passage, this could be a case of hads. The emotional satisfaction and speed align with the described indicators.
This example ties the psychological features to real Islamic practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبدو أن هذا الخلاف سبب مباشر في التداخل الذي يبرز أحيانا بين الحدس والإلهام، فنجد أن ثمة من يستخدم هذا المصطلح مرادفا للمصطلح الآخر (۱). وإن كان هذا لا يغير من حقيقة وجود الحدس بسمات ومظاهر خاصة. ولعل أبرز ما يستدعي التوقف في ظاهرة الحدس ما يؤكد عليه علماء النفس الحديث من أنه غدا بإمكان الإنسان الوصول إلى استنتاجات يثبت بعد ذلك صحتها، بيد أنه لا يستطيع شرح الأسس التي تقوم عليها هذه الاستنتاجات أو الطرائق التي سلكها في سبيلها. هذا مع أن الناس يختلفون في غيرها من القدرات. ومن المؤشرات الوجدانية على صحة الاستنتاج شعور المرء بالسرور والارتياح وكذلك اليقين على مستوى الذات (۳). كما أنه من الملفت للنظر حقاً ما يلاحظ من سرعة تقدير لما يحتاج إليه الموقف المفاجئ من عمل حاسم، وذلك ما يعتقد أنه من أبرز المظاهر المميزة لذوي القوى الحدسية (۳).
It seems that this disagreement is a direct cause of the overlap that sometimes appears between hads (intuition) and ilham (inspiration), for we find that some use this term synonymously with the other. Although this does not change the fact that hads has special characteristics and manifestations. Perhaps the most noteworthy point that calls for reflection in the phenomenon of hads is what modern psychologists emphasize: that it has become possible for a person to reach conclusions whose correctness is later proven, yet he cannot explain the foundations on which these conclusions rest or the methods he followed in reaching them. This while people differ in other abilities. Among the emotional indicators of the correctness of a conclusion is the person's feeling of pleasure and comfort as well as certainty at the subjective level. Also, it is truly striking the observed rapid assessment of what a sudden situation requires of decisive action, and this is believed to be one of the most prominent distinguishing features of those with intuitive powers.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage discusses the relationship between hads (intuition) and ilham (inspiration). The author notes that a disagreement among scholars has caused these two terms to sometimes be used interchangeably, though hads retains its own distinct characteristics. The main focus is on a psychological phenomenon: a person can reach conclusions that later prove correct without being able to explain the reasoning behind them. This inability to articulate the process is a key feature of intuition. Additionally, the author mentions emotional indicators of correctness, such as pleasure and subjective certainty. Finally, the passage highlights the rapid assessment needed in sudden situations as a hallmark of intuitive individuals.

المؤشرات الوجدانية

Key Takeaway
Intuitive conclusions are marked by an inability to explain reasoning, emotional satisfaction, and rapid decisive action.

Method of Learning

The Quranic Principle of Dominance and Verification
Author establishes the Quranic methodological principle for evaluating external philosophies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Quranic principle of dominance and verification to evaluate any external theory or philosophy.

Core Idea
The Quran is the criterion: accept truth, reject falsehood from any source.

In dealing with non-Islamic philosophies, Muslims often wonder what stance to take. The Quran provides a clear methodology: it dominates and verifies. This lesson unpacks that principle and shows how it applies to Bergson's theory of intuition as a case study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic principle
Find the key phrase describing the Quran's stance: 'الهيمنة والتصديق' (dominance and verification). What does each word imply?
2
Understand the rule
The principle is 'إقرار الصحيح ونبذ السقيم' (affirming the sound, rejecting the unsound). This is a general rule for thinking in Islam.
3
Recognize the source of authority
Why does the Quran have this authority? The passage says: due to its definitive divine origin (مصدرية ربانية قطعية).
4
Apply the principle to Bergson's theory
The author applies this: Bergson's intuitionism is not rejected outright but tested against revelation.
Consider what parts of Bergson's theory might be sound and what unsound from an Islamic perspective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الرابع - المصادر التبعية
ولعل هذا هو الذي دفع به إلى المغالاة في أهميتها إلى الحد الذي قلّل فيه من أهمية العقل، بل وجعله غير كاف وحده في الحصول على المعرفة ولا بد من أن يؤيد بالحدس الذي اعتقد أنه أعمق من المعرفة العقلية بكثير. ومن هنا فإنه قد يبدو مفهوماً علة ذلك القيد السابق الذي وضعه أحد الباحثين وحدّد من خلاله منطقة القبول التي يعمل فيها التفكير الحدسي والتي لا تتجاوز مساحة الفن والأدب.
حسب إن جعل نظرية برجسون معياراً في القبول أو الرفض هو الذي حمل الباحث المشار إليه على أن يتلمس لبرجسون ومن يشايع رأيه العذر في موقفهم الحدسي المغالي وزهدهم في العقل إلى حدّ يشتم منه رائحة الازدراء. فمشكلة برجسون هذه الوجهة - الخلط بين مقتضيات الحياة الشخصية والتجارب الفنية والشعرية من جانب ومقتضيات المعرفة العلمية من جانب آخر. ولذلك فلا تستطيع تكذيب برجسون بيد أن ذلك محصور في مجال بعينه لا يتعداه. أما موقف القرآن الكريم من كل النظريات والفلسفات القديم منها والحديث فهو موقف الهيمنة والتصديق، أي إقرار الصحيح منها ونبذ السقيم وهذه قاعدة عامة مطّردة موجّهة لقاعدة التفكير في الإسلام، كما وأنها منهجية القرآن المعرفية في التعامل مع سائر المعارف الأخرى. وذلك يرجع إلى سبب جوهري هو مصدريته الربانية القطعية.
من هنا فإن نظرية برجسون في الحدس مأخوذة بعين الاعتبار، بيد أنها يجب أن تخضع لاختبار الوحي قبولاً أو رفضاً، وسواء كان هذا القبول أو الرفض جزئياً أم كليّاً، وفقاً لقاعدة التفكير في الإسلام واتساقاً مع منهجية القرآن المعرفية. والقرآن يدرج الحدس ضمن مصادر المعرفة الثانوية المعترف بها. وقد جاءت الإشارة واضحة إلى مثل ذلك أبرز ما تكون في قول الله تعالى على لسان يعقوب: ﴿وَقالَ يا بَنِيَّ لا تَدْخُلُوا مِنْ بابِ واحِدٍ وَادْخُلُوا مِنْ أَبْوابِ مُتَفَرِّقَةٍ وَمَا أُغْنِي عَنْكُمْ مِنَ اللَّهِ مِنْ شَيْءٍ إِنِ الْحُكْمُ إِلَّا لِلَّهِ عَلَيْهِ تَوَكَّلْتُ وَعَلَيْهِ فَلْيَتَوَكَّلِ الْمُتَوَكَّلُونَ﴾ [يوسف: ٦٧/١٢].
وعلى لسانه أيضا جاء قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَمّا فَصَلَتِ الْعِيرُ قَالَ أَبُوهُمْ إِنِّي لأَجِدُ رِيحَ يُوسُفَ لَوْلا أَنْ تُفَنِّدُونِ، قَالُوا تَاللَّهِ إِنَّكَ لَفِي ضَلَالِكَ الْقَدِيمِ، فَلَمّا أَنْ جاءَ الْبَشِيرُ أَلْقَاهُ عَلَى وَجْهِهِ فَارْتَدَّ بَصِيراً قَالَ أَلَمْ أَقُلْ لَكُمْ إِنِّي أَعْلَمُ مِنَ الله ما لا تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [يوسف: ٩٤/١٢، ٩٦].
وكان يوسف قد قال لإخوته: اذْهَبُوا بِقَمِيصِي هَذَا فَأَلْقُوهُ عَلَى وَجْهِ أَبِي يَأْتِ بَصيراً ... [يوسف: ٩٣/١٢].
إن هذه الآيات تحمل إشارات ذات مدلول على مشروعية التفكير الحدسي في الإسلام.
ولعله من قبيل الملاحظ الدقيقة المستوحاة من مثل تلك الآيات - وكان إغفالها سببًا في خلط بعض الباحثين بين الحدس والإلهام - أن من السمات الجلية في الحدس قيامه على أساس من التنبؤ والاستشراف والترقب، من غير إجهاد للحس أو العقل في القيام بعمليات إدراكية حسية أو عقلية مقصودة. ويساعد على هذا المفهوم التعريف اللغوي للحدس القائل بأنه الظن والتخمين. وقد قيل: إن من سمات المعرفة الحدسية أن لا تتم إلا من خلال توتر نفسي، ومجهود شاق مؤلم للنفاذ إلى باطن الموضوع ومتابعته في صيرورته... ولذا فإنها معاناة الموضوع المدرك لا معاينته كما في المعرفة العقلية والحسية. ومما يدل على هذا من وحي الواقع المشاهد أن الحدس لا يتحقق إلا بعد استفراغ
Chapter Three: Section Four - Subordinate Sources
Perhaps this is what drove him to exaggerate its importance to the extent that he diminished the importance of reason, even making it insufficient alone for obtaining knowledge, and it must be supported by intuition which he believed is much deeper than rational knowledge. Hence, the reason for that previous restriction placed by one researcher becomes understandable, through which he defined the area of acceptance in which intuitive thinking operates, which does not exceed the sphere of art and literature.
Taking Bergson's theory as a criterion for acceptance or rejection is what led the mentioned researcher to seek an excuse for Bergson and those who share his opinion in their exaggerated intuitive stance and their asceticism towards reason to the extent that one smells contempt. Bergson's problem, from this perspective, is the confusion between the requirements of personal life and artistic and poetic experiences on one hand, and the requirements of scientific knowledge on the other. Therefore, we cannot refute Bergson, but that is confined to a specific domain that it does not exceed. As for the stance of the Noble Qur'an towards all theories and philosophies, ancient and modern, it is a stance of dominance and verification, i.e., affirming what is sound among them and rejecting the unsound. This is a general, constant rule directing the rule of thinking in Islam, and it is the Qur'an's epistemological methodology in dealing with other branches of knowledge. This is due to a fundamental reason: its definitive divine origin.
Hence, Bergson's theory of intuition is taken into consideration, but it must be subjected to the test of revelation, acceptance or rejection, whether this acceptance or rejection is partial or total, according to the rule of thinking in Islam and consistent with the Qur'an's epistemological methodology. The Qur'an includes intuition among the recognized secondary sources of knowledge. Clear indication of this is most evident in the saying of Allah, the Exalted, on the tongue of Ya'qub: {And he said, O my sons, do not enter from one gate but enter from different gates, and I cannot avail you against Allah at all. The decision is only for Allah. On Him I rely, and on Him let those who rely rely.} [Yusuf 12:67]. And on his tongue also came His saying, the Exalted: {And when the caravan departed, their father said, Indeed, I find the scent of Yusuf, if you did not think me senile. They said, By Allah, indeed you are in your old error. And when the bearer of good tidings came, he threw it over his face, and he returned [to] seeing. He said, Did I not tell you that I know from Allah that which you do not know?} [Yusuf 12:94-96]. And Yusuf had said to his brothers: {Go with this shirt of mine and throw it over my father's face; he will become seeing.} [Yusuf 12:93]. These verses carry indicative signs of the legitimacy of intuitive thinking in Islam.
Perhaps it is among the precise observations inspired by such verses - and neglecting them was the cause of some researchers' confusion between intuition and inspiration - that one of the clear characteristics of intuition is that it is based on prediction, foresight, and anticipation, without straining the sense or reason in performing deliberate sensory or rational cognitive operations. The linguistic definition of intuition, which is that it is conjecture and estimation, helps this concept. And it has been said: Among the characteristics of intuitive knowledge is that it is only achieved through psychological tension and painful strenuous effort to penetrate the inner depth of the subject and follow it in its becoming... Therefore, it is a suffering of the perceived subject, not an observation of it as in rational and sensory knowledge. What indicates this from the inspiration of observed reality is that intuition is only realized after exhausting.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion about intuition as a subordinate source of knowledge in Islam. The author begins by critiquing Henri Bergson's overemphasis on intuition at the expense of reason. He notes that Bergson's theory is limited to the realm of art and literature and cannot be applied to scientific knowledge. The author then states the Quranic principle of 'dominance and verification' (الهيمنة والتصديق): the Quran accepts what is sound from any theory and rejects what is unsound, based on its divine origin. Therefore, Bergson's intuition theory must be tested against revelation. The Quran actually includes intuition as a secondary source of knowledge, as seen in the story of Prophet Ya'qub (Jacob) who sensed the scent of his son Yusuf from a distance, and in Yusuf's instruction to his brothers to take his shirt to their father. These verses indicate the legitimacy of intuitive thinking in Islam. The author then distinguishes intuition from inspiration (إلهام) by noting that intuition is based on prediction and anticipation without conscious sensory or rational effort, and its linguistic definition is 'conjecture and estimation' (الظن والتخمين). Intuitive knowledge involves psychological tension and painful effort to penetrate the essence of the subject, unlike rational or sensory knowledge which is a mere observation. Intuition is only achieved after exhausting effort.

Key Terms
الهيمنة والتصديق
مصدرية ربانية قطعية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the Quran's authority to evaluate other theories?
A) The Quran's historical precedence
B) The Quran's definitive divine origin
C) The Quran's linguistic inimitability
D) The Quran's comprehensive legal system

Key Takeaway
The Quranic principle of dominance and verification allows Muslims to critically engage with any philosophy, accepting truth and rejecting falsehood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a modern philosophical claim: 'Morality is subjective and culturally relative.' Using the principle of dominance and verification, identify which elements might be sound (e.g., recognition of cultural differences) and which are unsound (e.g., denial of objective moral truths).
?
Reflect on how this principle can be used in a debate with a secular philosopher: what is the basis for the Quran's authority to judge truth claims?

Intuition as a Recognized Secondary Source in the Quran
Author cites Quranic verses to prove that intuition is a legitimate secondary source of knowledge in Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Quranic evidence for the legitimacy of intuition as a secondary source of knowledge.

Core Idea
The Quran validates intuitive knowledge through prophetic examples.

While intuition is often dismissed as unreliable, the Quran includes it among legitimate sources of knowledge. The story of Prophet Ya'qub sensing Yusuf's scent from afar is a powerful example. This lesson examines the Quranic verses that support intuition and differentiate it from inspiration.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Quranic verses
Find the verses from Surah Yusuf cited in the passage. Read them in context.
The verses are 12:67, 12:94-96, and 12:93.
2
Extract the intuitive element
In each verse, identify what action or knowledge is based on intuition rather than sensory evidence or reason. Ya'qub's advice to enter through different gates and his sensing of Yusuf's scent.
Note that Ya'qub's knowledge is not based on direct observation but on a form of inner perception.
3
Understand the Quranic validation
The author states that these verses 'carry indicative signs of the legitimacy of intuitive thinking in Islam.' The Quran does not condemn Ya'qub's intuition but presents it as a valid form of knowledge.
4
Distinguish intuition from inspiration
The passage warns against confusing intuition (حدس) with inspiration (إلهام). Intuition involves effort and prediction, while inspiration is direct divine communication.
Ya'qub's knowledge is described as 'knowing from Allah what they do not know' – this might seem like inspiration, but the author classifies it as intuition based on its characteristics.

Chapter Three: Section Four - Subordinate Sources
Perhaps this is what drove him to exaggerate its importance to the extent that he diminished the importance of reason, even making it insufficient alone for obtaining knowledge, and it must be supported by intuition which he believed is much deeper than rational knowledge. Hence, the reason for that previous restriction placed by one researcher becomes understandable, through which he defined the area of acceptance in which intuitive thinking operates, which does not exceed the sphere of art and literature.
Taking Bergson's theory as a criterion for acceptance or rejection is what led the mentioned researcher to seek an excuse for Bergson and those who share his opinion in their exaggerated intuitive stance and their asceticism towards reason to the extent that one smells contempt. Bergson's problem, from this perspective, is the confusion between the requirements of personal life and artistic and poetic experiences on one hand, and the requirements of scientific knowledge on the other. Therefore, we cannot refute Bergson, but that is confined to a specific domain that it does not exceed. As for the stance of the Noble Qur'an towards all theories and philosophies, ancient and modern, it is a stance of dominance and verification, i.e., affirming what is sound among them and rejecting the unsound. This is a general, constant rule directing the rule of thinking in Islam, and it is the Qur'an's epistemological methodology in dealing with other branches of knowledge. This is due to a fundamental reason: its definitive divine origin.
Hence, Bergson's theory of intuition is taken into consideration, but it must be subjected to the test of revelation, acceptance or rejection, whether this acceptance or rejection is partial or total, according to the rule of thinking in Islam and consistent with the Qur'an's epistemological methodology. The Qur'an includes intuition among the recognized secondary sources of knowledge. Clear indication of this is most evident in the saying of Allah, the Exalted, on the tongue of Ya'qub: {And he said, O my sons, do not enter from one gate but enter from different gates, and I cannot avail you against Allah at all. The decision is only for Allah. On Him I rely, and on Him let those who rely rely.} [Yusuf 12:67]. And on his tongue also came His saying, the Exalted: {And when the caravan departed, their father said, Indeed, I find the scent of Yusuf, if you did not think me senile. They said, By Allah, indeed you are in your old error. And when the bearer of good tidings came, he threw it over his face, and he returned [to] seeing. He said, Did I not tell you that I know from Allah that which you do not know?} [Yusuf 12:94-96]. And Yusuf had said to his brothers: {Go with this shirt of mine and throw it over my father's face; he will become seeing.} [Yusuf 12:93]. These verses carry indicative signs of the legitimacy of intuitive thinking in Islam.
Perhaps it is among the precise observations inspired by such verses - and neglecting them was the cause of some researchers' confusion between intuition and inspiration - that one of the clear characteristics of intuition is that it is based on prediction, foresight, and anticipation, without straining the sense or reason in performing deliberate sensory or rational cognitive operations. The linguistic definition of intuition, which is that it is conjecture and estimation, helps this concept. And it has been said: Among the characteristics of intuitive knowledge is that it is only achieved through psychological tension and painful strenuous effort to penetrate the inner depth of the subject and follow it in its becoming... Therefore, it is a suffering of the perceived subject, not an observation of it as in rational and sensory knowledge. What indicates this from the inspiration of observed reality is that intuition is only realized after exhausting.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion about intuition as a subordinate source of knowledge in Islam. The author begins by critiquing Henri Bergson's overemphasis on intuition at the expense of reason. He notes that Bergson's theory is limited to the realm of art and literature and cannot be applied to scientific knowledge. The author then states the Quranic principle of 'dominance and verification' (الهيمنة والتصديق): the Quran accepts what is sound from any theory and rejects what is unsound, based on its divine origin. Therefore, Bergson's intuition theory must be tested against revelation. The Quran actually includes intuition as a secondary source of knowledge, as seen in the story of Prophet Ya'qub (Jacob) who sensed the scent of his son Yusuf from a distance, and in Yusuf's instruction to his brothers to take his shirt to their father. These verses indicate the legitimacy of intuitive thinking in Islam. The author then distinguishes intuition from inspiration (إلهام) by noting that intuition is based on prediction and anticipation without conscious sensory or rational effort, and its linguistic definition is 'conjecture and estimation' (الظن والتخمين). Intuitive knowledge involves psychological tension and painful effort to penetrate the essence of the subject, unlike rational or sensory knowledge which is a mere observation. Intuition is only achieved after exhausting effort.

Key Terms
الحدس
الهام
المعرفة الحدسية

D) That intuition is only for art and literature

Key Takeaway
The Quran includes intuition as a secondary source of knowledge, as demonstrated by the example of Prophet Ya'qub.

Method of Learning
intermediate
10 min
The Nature and Characteristics of Intuitive Knowledge
Author defines intuition and distinguishes it from inspiration and other knowledge types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish intuitive knowledge from other types of knowledge based on its defining characteristics.

Core Idea
Intuition is prediction through effort, not effortless inspiration.

What exactly is intuitive knowledge? The author provides a precise description: it involves prediction and anticipation without deliberate sensory or rational effort, but it requires psychological tension and painful effort to penetrate the subject. This lesson breaks down the definition and characteristics of intuition as presented in the passage, distinguishing it from inspiration and from rational/sensory knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Find the linguistic definition
The author mentions the linguistic definition of حدس: 'الظن والتخمين' (conjecture and estimation). This sets the basic meaning.
This definition highlights the element of uncertainty and guesswork.
2
Identify the key characteristics
The passage lists: prediction (تنبؤ), foresight (استشراف), anticipation (ترقب), without straining sense or reason; psychological tension and painful effort to penetrate the subject's essence.
Contrast this with the effortless nature of inspiration.
3
Understand the process
Intuitive knowledge is described as 'suffering of the perceived subject' (معاناة الموضوع المدرك) not observation. It requires following the subject in its becoming.
This suggests a dynamic, immersive engagement with the subject.
4
Differentiate from other knowledge types
Contrast intuitive knowledge with rational and sensory knowledge: rational and sensory are observation (معاينة), while intuitive is suffering and deep involvement.
The author also distinguishes it from inspiration: intuition requires effort and is based on prediction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الرابع - المصادر التبعية
ولعل هذا هو الذي دفع به إلى المغالاة في أهميتها إلى الحد الذي قلّل فيه من أهمية العقل، بل وجعله غير كاف وحده في الحصول على المعرفة ولا بد من أن يؤيد بالحدس الذي اعتقد أنه أعمق من المعرفة العقلية بكثير. ومن هنا فإنه قد يبدو مفهوماً علة ذلك القيد السابق الذي وضعه أحد الباحثين وحدّد من خلاله منطقة القبول التي يعمل فيها التفكير الحدسي والتي لا تتجاوز مساحة الفن والأدب.
حسب إن جعل نظرية برجسون معياراً في القبول أو الرفض هو الذي حمل الباحث المشار إليه على أن يتلمس لبرجسون ومن يشايع رأيه العذر في موقفهم الحدسي المغالي وزهدهم في العقل إلى حدّ يشتم منه رائحة الازدراء. فمشكلة برجسون هذه الوجهة - الخلط بين مقتضيات الحياة الشخصية والتجارب الفنية والشعرية من جانب ومقتضيات المعرفة العلمية من جانب آخر. ولذلك فلا تستطيع تكذيب برجسون بيد أن ذلك محصور في مجال بعينه لا يتعداه. أما موقف القرآن الكريم من كل النظريات والفلسفات القديم منها والحديث فهو موقف الهيمنة والتصديق، أي إقرار الصحيح منها ونبذ السقيم وهذه قاعدة عامة مطّردة موجّهة لقاعدة التفكير في الإسلام، كما وأنها منهجية القرآن المعرفية في التعامل مع سائر المعارف الأخرى. وذلك يرجع إلى سبب جوهري هو مصدريته الربانية القطعية.
من هنا فإن نظرية برجسون في الحدس مأخوذة بعين الاعتبار، بيد أنها يجب أن تخضع لاختبار الوحي قبولاً أو رفضاً، وسواء كان هذا القبول أو الرفض جزئياً أم كليّاً، وفقاً لقاعدة التفكير في الإسلام واتساقاً مع منهجية القرآن المعرفية. والقرآن يدرج الحدس ضمن مصادر المعرفة الثانوية المعترف بها. وقد جاءت الإشارة واضحة إلى مثل ذلك أبرز ما تكون في قول الله تعالى على لسان يعقوب: ﴿وَقالَ يا بَنِيَّ لا تَدْخُلُوا مِنْ بابِ واحِدٍ وَادْخُلُوا مِنْ أَبْوابِ مُتَفَرِّقَةٍ وَمَا أُغْنِي عَنْكُمْ مِنَ اللَّهِ مِنْ شَيْءٍ إِنِ الْحُكْمُ إِلَّا لِلَّهِ عَلَيْهِ تَوَكَّلْتُ وَعَلَيْهِ فَلْيَتَوَكَّلِ الْمُتَوَكَّلُونَ﴾ [يوسف: ٦٧/١٢].
وعلى لسانه أيضا جاء قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَمّا فَصَلَتِ الْعِيرُ قَالَ أَبُوهُمْ إِنِّي لأَجِدُ رِيحَ يُوسُفَ لَوْلا أَنْ تُفَنِّدُونِ، قَالُوا تَاللَّهِ إِنَّكَ لَفِي ضَلَالِكَ الْقَدِيمِ، فَلَمّا أَنْ جاءَ الْبَشِيرُ أَلْقَاهُ عَلَى وَجْهِهِ فَارْتَدَّ بَصِيراً قَالَ أَلَمْ أَقُلْ لَكُمْ إِنِّي أَعْلَمُ مِنَ الله ما لا تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [يوسف: ٩٤/١٢، ٩٦].
وكان يوسف قد قال لإخوته: اذْهَبُوا بِقَمِيصِي هَذَا فَأَلْقُوهُ عَلَى وَجْهِ أَبِي يَأْتِ بَصيراً ... [يوسف: ٩٣/١٢].
إن هذه الآيات تحمل إشارات ذات مدلول على مشروعية التفكير الحدسي في الإسلام.
ولعله من قبيل الملاحظ الدقيقة المستوحاة من مثل تلك الآيات - وكان إغفالها سببًا في خلط بعض الباحثين بين الحدس والإلهام - أن من السمات الجلية في الحدس قيامه على أساس من التنبؤ والاستشراف والترقب، من غير إجهاد للحس أو العقل في القيام بعمليات إدراكية حسية أو عقلية مقصودة. ويساعد على هذا المفهوم التعريف اللغوي للحدس القائل بأنه الظن والتخمين. وقد قيل: إن من سمات المعرفة الحدسية أن لا تتم إلا من خلال توتر نفسي، ومجهود شاق مؤلم للنفاذ إلى باطن الموضوع ومتابعته في صيرورته... ولذا فإنها معاناة الموضوع المدرك لا معاينته كما في المعرفة العقلية والحسية. ومما يدل على هذا من وحي الواقع المشاهد أن الحدس لا يتحقق إلا بعد استفراغ
