Method of Learning
intermediate
10 min
The Quranic Method for Epistemological Engagement
Author explains the Quranic approach to knowledge and the delayed study of its possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and describe the Quranic method of leading an opponent to a logical conclusion without imposing premises.

Core Idea
The Quran descends to the opponent's level and turns their own premises into logical conclusions.

This opening passage explains why the author delays the discussion of whether knowledge is possible. Rather than starting with a disputed premise, the Quranic method—and the author's approach—first examines the nature, sources, and methods of knowledge. The Quran does not force premises; it engages opponents by letting them reach conclusions through their own reasoning. We will explore how this method works and why it is crucial for Islamic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two approaches to the possibility of knowledge
Notice that some researchers treat knowledge-as-possible as an unquestioned premise (musallama), while the author delays it. Mark the contrast: the author aligns with a philosophical trend that treats possibility as a logical consequence of studying knowledge's nature.
The key term is 'ta'jīl' (delay) vs. 'ibtidā'' (beginning).
2
Extract the logical structure underlying the delay
The author argues: if knowledge has a specific nature, then it must have specific sources and methods; therefore, knowledge is possible. Recognize this as a conditional argument: the possibility of knowledge is deduced from its defined characteristics.
This is not a formal syllogism but a logical inference.
3
Analyze the Quranic method from the cited verses
Look at verse 34:24: the Quran poses a question, answers it, but forces the opponent to admit the dichotomy (guidance vs. error). Similarly, 34:46 calls for reflection without presuppositions. The method is 'tanazzul' (descending) with the opponent, leading them step by step.
The goal is to make the conclusion appear inevitable from the opponent's own starting point.
4
Examine the Abrahamic argument as a model
In 2:258, Ibrahim (AS) does not start with 'Allah exists' but with a conceded premise (giving life and death). When the opponent claims that power, Ibrahim shifts to a stronger argument (the sun), leaving the opponent confounded. This illustrates dialectical descent without insistence on initial premises.
The opponent is defeated by his own logic.
5
Synthesize the Quranic epistemological principle
The author concludes that the Quran transforms contested premises into logical results, making them shared methodological premises. This principle avoids stalemate and leads to certainty (yaqin) from within the opponent's framework.
This method is the foundation for the subsequent discussion of doubt and certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تمهيد
الفصل الأول
المعرفة بين الشك واليقين
قمين بالتنويه في هذا الموضوع أن مناسبة تأجيل هذا الفصل إلى هذا الموضع من الدراسة دون الابتداء به - كما درج على ذلك بعض الباحثين حين عدوا مسألة الحصول على المعرفة مسلّمة لا تستحق التأجيل- المسايرة المؤقتة للاتجاه الفلسفي النازع إلى تأجيل دراسة عنصر إمكان الحصول على المعرفة ليظهر كنتيجة منطقية للبحث في طبيعة المعرفة ومصادرها وطرائقها. بمعنى أنه ما دام أن ثمة معرفة ذات طبيعة محدّدة، فإن لها مصادرها وطرائقها المحدّدة كذلك، وهذا دليل منطقي على أن المعرفة ممكنة، أو أن لها حدوداً ظاهرة مميزة. وخلافاً لمنحى من سبقت الإشارة إلى بعضهم آنفاً فلست أرى في هذا المنهج مخالفة لمنهج القرآن الكريم في التعامل مع معطيات المعرفة لدى الآخر، بل إن القرآن ليتنزّل معه، حتى يدفعه دفعاً نحو الوصول إلى النتيجة المنطقية منفرداً. فتارة يطرح مقدّمة واضحة النتائج إلا أنه يبادر بسؤال يبدو وكأنه محيّر ولكن سرعان ما يدلف منه المحاور إلى تقرير النتيجة الموضوعية بنفسه . وقُلْ مَنْ يَرْزُقُكُمْ مِنَ السَّماواتِ وَالْأَرْضِ قُلِ اللهُ وَإِنَّا أَوْ إِيَّاكُمْ لَعَلَى هُدَى أَوْ فِي ضَلالٍ مُبِينٍ ﴾ [سبا: ٢٤/٣٤].
فالقرآن وإن كان قد تساءل وأجاب في آن واحد إلا أن الطرف الآخر لا يملك غير تقرير ما قرره القرآن من أن الهداية إما مع صاحب القرآن أو خصمه وأنى للضدين أن يجتمعا؟
ويدعو القرآن - تارة- إلى التجرد واطراح أي مقررات مسبقة، ليتمكن الطرف الآخر من التحقق بنفسه من حقيقة دعوة النبي - ولكن ذلك لن يكون إلا بعد إعمال العقل، وسواء كان ذلك في حال اجتماع الخصوم، أم خلوّ كل واحد بنفسه:
قُلْ إِنما أَعِظُكُمْ بِوَاحِدَةٍ أَن تَقُومُوا لِلَّهِ مَثْنَى وَفُرَادَى ثُمَّ تَتَفَكَّرُوا ما بصاحِيكُمْ مِنْ جِنَّةٍ إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا نَذِيرٌ لَكُمْ بَيْنَ يَدَيْ عَذَابٍ شَدِيدٍ (سبا: ٤٦/٣٤]. ويتنزل القرآن مع الآخر من غير إصرار منه على محاججته في شبهته ليجعــل الرد بأسلوب آخر أبلغ وأكبر :
أَلَمْ تَرَ إِلَى الَّذِي حَاجَّ إِبْرَاهِيمَ فِي رَبِّهِ أن آتاه اللهُ الْمُلْكَ إذْ قالَ إِبْراهِيمُ رَبِّيَ الَّذِي يُحْيِي وَيُمِيتُ قَالَ أَنا أَحْيِي وَأُمِيتُ قَالَ إِبْرَاهِيمُ فَإِنَّ اللهَ يَأْتِي بِالشَّمْسِ مِنَ الْمَشْرِقِ فَأْتِ بِها مِنَ الْمَغْرِبِ، فَبُهِتَ الَّذِي كَفَرَ وَاللَّهُ لا يَهْدِي الْقَوْمَ الظَّالِمِينَ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٨/٢].
ونحن نلاحظ في هذه الآيات جميعها عدم الإصرار على وضع مسلّمة ثم المضي فيها مادام الآخر غير معترف بها، ولكن منهج القرآن في التنزل معه أحالها نتيجة منطقية، ومن ثمّ مسلّمة منهجية لدى الطرفين.
والبحث في إمكان الحصول على المعرفة يأخذ منحنيين: أحدهما: البحث في الإمكان من جانب إشكال الشك واليقين والموقف منهما في القرآن الكريم والجانب الآخر من جانب البحث في الحقيقة وإمكان الحصول عليها.
Preface
Chapter One
Knowledge between doubt and certainty
It is noteworthy in this subject that the reason for delaying this chapter to this place in the study, rather than beginning with it — as some researchers have done when they considered the issue of obtaining knowledge as a premise not deserving delay — is the temporary alignment with the philosophical trend inclined to delay the study of the element of the possibility of obtaining knowledge, so that it appears as a logical result of the research into the nature of knowledge and its sources and methods. Meaning that as long as there is knowledge of a specific nature, it has its specific sources and methods as well, and this is a logical proof that knowledge is possible, or that it has manifest distinctive limits. Contrary to the approach of some I referred to earlier, I do not see in this method a violation of the method of the Holy Quran in dealing with the givens of knowledge of the other. Rather, the Quran descends with him, pushing him forcefully towards reaching the logical conclusion alone. At times it presents a premise whose results are clear, yet it initiates a question that appears perplexing, but soon the interlocutor proceeds through it to affirm the objective conclusion by himself. And say: "Who provides for you from the heavens and the earth?" Say: "Allah." And indeed, we or you are either upon guidance or in manifest error." [Saba: 34:24].
Thus the Quran, although it questioned and answered at the same time, the other party has no choice but to affirm what the Quran has affirmed: that guidance is either with the Quran's owner or his opponent, and how can opposites be united?
And the Quran calls — at times — to detachment and the rejection of any presuppositions, so that the other party can verify for himself the truth of the Prophet's call — but that will only happen after employing the intellect, whether in the case of opponents meeting or each being alone:
"Say: I only admonish you with one thing: that you stand for Allah in pairs and singly, and then reflect: there is no madness in your companion; he is only a warner to you before a severe torment." [Saba: 34:46]. And the Quran descends with the other without insisting on arguing with him about his doubt, making the reply in another manner more eloquent and greater:
"Have you not seen the one who argued with Abraham about his Lord because Allah had given him kingship? When Abraham said: 'My Lord is the one who gives life and causes death,' he said: 'I give life and cause death.' Abraham said: 'Indeed, Allah brings the sun from the east; so bring it from the west.' Then the disbeliever was confounded. And Allah does not guide the wrongdoing people." [Al-Baqarah: 2:258].
We observe in all these verses the lack of insistence on establishing a premise and then proceeding with it as long as the other does not acknowledge it. Rather, the Quran's method of descending with him turned it into a logical result, and thus a methodological premise for both parties.
Research into the possibility of obtaining knowledge takes two directions: one is research into possibility from the aspect of the problem of doubt and certainty and the stance towards them in the Holy Quran; the other is research into truth and the possibility of obtaining it.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is an introductory segment (tamhīd) that opens Chapter One on 'Knowledge between Doubt and Certainty'. The author explains why he has delayed the discussion of the possibility of knowledge to this point in the study, rather than beginning with it as some researchers do. He argues that this delay is a temporary alignment with a philosophical trend that treats the issue as a logical result of investigating the nature, sources, and methods of knowledge. According to the author, as long as there is knowledge with a specific nature, it necessarily has specific sources and methods, which is a logical proof that knowledge is possible. He then contrasts this approach with the Quranic method, asserting that the Quran does not impose premises but instead descends to the level of the opponent, leading him step by step to the logical conclusion. To illustrate, he cites Quran 34:24, where Allah asks a question and answers it, yet forces the opponent to acknowledge the dichotomy between guidance and error. In another example, the Quran calls for detachment from presuppositions and for reflection individually or in pairs (34:46). The author also mentions the famous debate of Prophet Ibrahim (AS) with Nimrod (2:258), where Ibrahim used a dialectical argument that left the opponent confounded. The author observes that in all these verses, the Quran does not insist on an initial premise that the opponent rejects; instead, through descent (tanazzul), it turns the premise into a logical outcome, thereby becoming a shared methodological premise. Finally, the author announces that the research into the possibility of knowledge will proceed along two tracks: (1) the problem of doubt and certainty in the Quran, and (2) the search for truth and the possibility of attaining it.

اليقين
التنزل

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Quranic method of engaging with opponents who do not share the same premises?
A) Insist on the premises until the opponent accepts them.
B) Descend with the opponent and turn the premises into logical results.
C) Avoid debate entirely and rely on miracles.
D) Agree with the opponent's doubts and withhold judgment.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic method for dealing with epistemological disagreements is to descend with the opponent and lead them to the logical conclusion from their own starting point, turning contested premises into shared results.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Analyze the debate between Ibrahim (AS) and Nimrod in Quran 2:258. Identify the initial premise that Nimrod accepted (giving life and death). Explain how Ibrahim (AS) used that premise to construct a logical argument that left Nimrod confounded. Write your analysis in 3-4 sentences.
?
Take a known theological dispute (e.g., the creation of the Quran, or divine attributes). Using the Quranic method described in this passage, outline a strategy for engaging with an opponent who rejects your starting premises. State the opponent's likely starting premise, and show how you can 'descend' to reach your desired conclusion.

Method of Learning
intermediate
10 min
The Possibility of Knowledge: Doubt, Certainty, and the Two Schools
Author introduces the epistemological problem of possibility of knowledge, defining doubt and certainty, and outlining two schools of thought.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main epistemological schools regarding the limits of human knowledge and explain the debate between heredity (wiratha) and acquisition (iktisab) in how knowledge is obtained.

Core Idea
Knowledge is possible, but its limits and sources are debated between sensory relativism and objective certainty.

This lesson introduces the foundational epistemological question: Can humans attain certain knowledge? The author begins by defining 'possibility' (imkan) through al-Jurjani's technical definition, then contrasts doubt (shakk) and certainty (yaqin). He outlines two competing schools—the critical/relativistic school that limits knowledge to the senses, and the objective school that allows for certain knowledge of reality. The discussion is then connected to the debate over whether knowledge is innate (heredity) or acquired through experience (acquisition), a theme central to Islamic epistemology and relevant to later discussions of revelation and reason.

Guided Path
1
Define 'imkan' using al-Jurjani
Read al-Jurjani's definition: 'the non-necessitation of existence and non-existence by the essence.' This means that possibility is a state between impossibility and necessity, where the subject does not inherently require either existence or non-existence. Apply this to the question of knowledge: Is it possible for humans to know?
This is a modal logical definition, not merely a linguistic one.
2
Contrast doubt (shakk) and certainty (yaqin)
The author sets up the inquiry by contrasting doubt as the opposite of certainty. Recognize that the entire discussion revolves around whether knowledge can overcome doubt to reach certain, objective truth.
In Islamic thought, yaqin is a high epistemic status, often associated with prophetic knowledge.
3
Identify the two schools of epistemology
The passage mentions the critical/relativistic school, which holds that human knowledge is limited to sensory input and is therefore relative, and an implied objective school that affirms certain knowledge of reality. Spot which school aligns with each view on the limits of knowledge.
The author does not name the objective school explicitly, but it is understood from the contrast.
4
Explain the heredity vs. acquisition debate
The author poses two hypotheses: knowledge is inherited (wiratha) at birth, or acquired (iktisab) from the external world. Consider how each hypothesis shifts the focus of education—either to the learner's innate capacities or to the curriculum and external sources.
This debate has direct implications for Islamic education and theories of learning.
5
Connect to methodology and revelation
The author notes that the possibility of knowledge hinges on methodology, which relies on senses, reason, and intuition. He suggests that including revelation as both a source and a method would reduce subjective influences. Recognize that this ties the epistemological question to Islamic theology's reliance on wahy.
This step foreshadows the author's later integration of Qur'anic epistemology.

الباب الرابع الفصل الأول - المعرفة بين الشك واليقين
أولاً - الشك
نتحدث عن الشك في مقابل اليقين، كما نتحدث عن إمكان الحصول على هذا الأخير فماذا يعني الإمكان ابتداء؟
يعرف الجرجاني: (ت: ٨١٦ هـ) الإمكان بقوله: (عدم اقتضاء الذات الوجود والعدم). أي أن يكون الموضوع المعروف في حال بين الامتناع والوجوب والبحث فيه يتناول الإجابة عن سؤال مفاده: هل بمقدور الإنسان أن يحصل على المعرفة؟ وإذا حصل عليها فما حدودها؟ وبمعنى آخر أكثر تحديداً: هل هي معرفة لا تعدو الظن؟ أم أنها يمكن أن تكون معرفة يقينية تُشكل حقيقةً من الحقائق الموضوعية؟
ومن المعلوم لدى دارسي نظرية المعرفة أو الإبستيمولوجيا أن هناك مذهبين سائدين في هذا المجال هما المذهب النقدي أو النسبي، ويقول محدودية المعرفة الإنسانية بحدود الحواس، وعلى الرغم من أهمية دور العقل فإن النسبية قَدَرُهَا لدى هذا المذهب الأخير.
وعلى هذا فإن تناول مسألة اليقين والشك مرتبط موضوعياً – ارتباط مقدمة ونتيجة - بأساس البحث في طبيعة المعرفة في القرآن من جهة، وبتحديد المصادر والطرائق الرئيسة والثانوية الموصلة إلى المعرفة من الجهة الأخرى، وهذا بدوره يؤكد مشروعية تناول الموضوع في هذا الموضع من الدراسة لا الابتداء به. إن الحديث عن اليقين والشك يقتضي منا التفصيل من زاوية الوراثة والاكتساب. وهنا قد يكون من المناسب الإفصاح عن توجس حصول إلباس لربما يذهب بتفكير بعض القراء إلى أنّ مقام التحدث الأصلي عن الوراثة والاكتساب إنما هو مندرج في إطار طبيعة المعرفة في القرآن ومع الاعتراف بأن من غير الممكن إيجاد خط فاصل دقيق بين الطبيعة والإمكان إلا أن منطق التحدث عن إمكان الحصول على المعرفة هو - في حقيقة الأمر - ما يتطلب من الناحية الموضوعية بحث ما إذا كان الإنسان يولد حاصلا على المعرفة بالوراثة، أم أنه يتحصل عليها باكتسابه الذاتي من العالم الخارجي، أو ما يصطلح على تسميته بالواقع الموضوعي. فإن كان الفرض الأول صواباً كان معنى ذلك أن التعلم عملية ذاتية، وهنا يتوجه الاهتمام إلى المتعلم بالدرجة الأولى، أما إن كان الفرض الثاني هو الأرجح فإن الاهتمام يصبح متجهاً نحو المقررات الدراسية والمادة العلمية المكوّنة لهذه المعرفة، وقد سبق القول عند الحديث عن طبيعة المعرفة أن المعرفة ذاتية وموضوعية في آن واحد، ولذلك فإن الاهتمام يتوجه إلى المتعلم والمادة العلمية معاً.
وحقاً فإنه ما كان لهذا الموضوع أن يبحث من الوجهة القرآنية – على الأقل- بعد كل ما مر معنا من حديث عن الطبيعة والمصدرية والطرائق، لولا أن ثمة تأثيراً من الأفكار الوافدة، وتأثراً غير مباشر من بعض الفلاسفة الإسلاميين - كالغزالي مثلاً - قد حصل بالفعل، وهذا ما سأشير إليه فيما بعد بإذن الله - تعالى-.
إن مسألة الإمكان هذه تتصل بقضية المنهجية (Methodology) وهي أعقـد قضايا العلم، لأنها تعتمد على وسائل المعرفة ممثلة في السمع والبصر والفؤاد، مما للعادات والمعتقدات والقيم والأهواء أن تتدخل وتؤثر، إلا بتجرد عزيز المنال. ولو أدرج الوحي ضمنها ولكن بوصفه مصدراً وطريقة معاً لخفف من غلواء ذلك التدخل والتأثير إلى حد كبير إن لم يقض عليه بالكلية.
ولقد بات في حكم المقرر - بعد كل ما تقدّم أن إمكان الحصول على المعرفة رهن بما هو موجود لدينا من الأفكار، ويكون الإدراك إما عن طريق الحس أو التبرير العقلي (المنطق) أو الحدس حسبما يرى (جون لوك)، وإن كان
Chapter Four: First Section - Knowledge between Doubt and Certainty
First: Doubt
We speak about doubt in contrast to certainty, and we speak about the possibility of obtaining the latter. So what does possibility mean initially?
Al-Jurjani (d. 816 AH) defines possibility as: "The non-necessitation of existence and non-existence by the essence." That is, the known subject is in a state between impossibility and necessity. The discussion addresses the question: Is man capable of obtaining knowledge? And if he obtains it, what are its limits? In other words, more specifically: Is it knowledge that does not exceed conjecture? Or can it be certain knowledge constituting an objective truth?
It is well known among scholars of epistemology that there are two prevalent schools in this field: the critical or relativistic school, which holds that human knowledge is limited to the senses, and despite the importance of the role of reason, relativism is its fate according to this latter school.
Thus, addressing the issue of certainty and doubt is objectively linked – as a connection of premise and conclusion – to the foundation of the inquiry into the nature of knowledge in the Qur'an on one hand, and to determining the primary and secondary sources and methods leading to knowledge on the other hand. This in turn confirms the legitimacy of addressing the topic at this point of the study rather than beginning with it. Indeed, speaking about certainty and doubt requires us to detail from the angle of heredity and acquisition. Here it may be appropriate to disclose a concern about possible confusion that might lead some readers to think that the original context of discussing heredity and acquisition is within the framework of the nature of knowledge in the Qur'an. And while acknowledging that it is impossible to find a precise dividing line between nature and possibility, nevertheless the logic of discussing the possibility of obtaining knowledge – in reality – requires from an objective perspective investigating whether a person is born possessing knowledge through heredity, or whether they acquire it through their own acquisition from the external world, or what is termed objective reality. If the first assumption is correct, it means that learning is an intrinsic process, and attention here is directed primarily to the learner. But if the second assumption is more likely, attention becomes directed toward the curriculum and the scientific material composing this knowledge. It has been mentioned earlier when discussing the nature of knowledge that knowledge is both subjective and objective simultaneously, and therefore attention is directed to both the learner and the scientific material together.
Truly, this topic would not have been investigated from the Qur'anic perspective – at least – after all that has passed in our discussion of nature, source, and methods, were it not for the influence of incoming ideas and indirect influence from some Islamic philosophers – like al-Ghazali for example – that actually occurred. This I will point to later, God willing.
This issue of possibility is connected to the issue of methodology, which is the most complex issue of science, because it depends on the means of knowledge represented by hearing, sight, and the heart, where habits, beliefs, values, and whims can intervene and influence, except with a rare detachment. If revelation were included among them, but as both a source and a method, it would greatly reduce, if not completely eliminate, the intensity of that intervention and influence.
It has become established – after all that has preceded – that the possibility of obtaining knowledge is contingent upon what ideas are present within us, and perception occurs either through the senses, rational justification (logic), or intuition according to (John Locke), although
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage introduces the epistemological problem of the possibility of knowledge, contrasting doubt (shakk) with certainty (yaqin). The author begins by defining possibility (imkan) using al-Jurjani's definition: 'the non-necessitation of existence and non-existence by the essence,' meaning the subject is in a state between impossibility and necessity. This leads to the question of whether man can obtain knowledge and what its limits are. Two schools of epistemology are mentioned: the critical/relativistic school, which limits knowledge to the senses, and the rational/objective school (implied). The discussion then links the issue of certainty and doubt to the research on the nature of knowledge in the Qur'an and the identification of sources and methods. The author clarifies that the proper context for discussing heredity and acquisition is within the nature of knowledge, and that there is no precise line between nature and possibility. The two hypotheses are explored: whether knowledge is hereditary (learner-focused) or acquired (curriculum-focused), concluding that knowledge is both subjective and objective. The author notes that the topic is being addressed due to influences from external ideas and philosophers like al-Ghazali. Finally, the passage ties possibility to methodology, relying on the senses, reason, and intuition, and suggests that including revelation as both source and method would mitigate subjective influences. The passage ends by stating that perception is either sensory, rational, or intuitive, citing John Locke.

The Quran's Legitimization of Seeking Certainty Through Inquiry
Author argues that seeking certainty is legitimate in the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify from Quranic verses how the Quran legitimizes the pursuit of certainty through inquiry and recognize the epistemological implication that certainty must be actively sought.

Core Idea
The Quran commands inquiry to reach certainty, not blind acceptance.

This lesson examines a key Quranic principle: far from discouraging questions, the Quran actively commands the search for certainty. We will see how the author uses Quranic evidence to establish that certainty is a legitimate goal and that doubt should be resolved through inquiry, not suppressed. This has profound implications for how we approach Islamic knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's central claim
Find the sentence where the author states that the Quran considers seeking certainty legitimate. It is near the beginning: 'في مقابل ما تقدّم يعدّ القرآن الكريم البحث عن اليقين مشروعاً' (In contrast to what preceded, the Noble Quran considers the search for certainty as legitimate).
2
Analyze the key Quranic evidence
Look at the verse from Surah Yunus (10:94): 'فَإِن كُنتَ فِي شَكٍّ مِمَّا أَنزَلْنَا إِلَيْكَ فَاسْأَلِ الَّذِينَ يَقْرَؤُونَ الْكِتَابَ مِن قَبْلِكَ' (So if you are in doubt about what We have revealed to you, then ask those who read the Scripture before you). The author uses this to show that even the Prophet is permitted to ask if in doubt, legitimizing inquiry.
3
Distinguish between Quranic certainty and human certainty
The author notes that the Quran declares itself certain (لا ريب فيه), but this does not mean every person automatically possesses certainty. Due to the disparity in intellects and understandings, people must actively seek certainty. The Quran's self-certainty does not preclude the need for inquiry.
4
Extract the epistemological principle
The author derives from this the legitimacy of an 'inquisitive education' (تربية تساؤلية) that goes beyond mere indoctrination. Certainty is not simply handed down; it requires questioning and searching with all available faculties.
5
Connect to fundamental beliefs
The author emphasizes that the fundamentals of religion (usul al-din) such as Tawhid and the Hereafter are certain, but even these truths must be reached through inquiry. The verses cited about the Hereafter (لا ريب فيه) affirm certainty, yet the context shows that believers are called to reflect and seek.

ثانياً- اليقين
مشروعية البحث عن اليقين:
في مقابل ما تقدّم يعدّ القرآن الكريم البحث عن اليقين مشروعاً، فقد أرشد فيما أرشد كل حائر متسائل أن يبحث ويسأل حتى يصل إلى اليقين، ومن ذلك سؤال العلماء والعارفين:
فَإِن كُنتَ فِي شَكٍّ مِمَّا أَنزَلْنَا إِلَيْكَ فَاسْأَلِ الَّذِينَ يَقْرَؤُونَ الْكِتَابَ مِن قَبْلِكَ [يونس: ٩٤/١٠].
رغم أن القرآن يقرر يقينيته في غير ما آية:
تَنزِيلُ الْكِتابِ لا رَيْبَ فِيهِ مِنْ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ﴾ [السجدة: ٢/٣٢].
وَذَلِكَ الْكِتابُ لا رَيْبَ فِيهِ﴾ [البقرة: ٢/٢].
وإن دلّ على شيء فإنما يدل على أن اليقينيات الكبرى التي يعتقدها بعض الناس عن علم يصل حد اليقين لا تؤذن بتعميم ذلك الاعتقاد اليقيني على مختلف الأفهام والعقول وسائر فئات الباحثين، نظراً للتفاوت الذي يطبع أفهام الناس وعقولهم، ولكن من جانب آخر لا يشفع ذلك للذين لا يوقنون من أن يبحثوا ويسألوا عن اليقين بكل ما أوتوا من قدرات وملكات ووسائل معرفة حتى يحققوا اليقين. وذلك ما يؤكد مشروعية التربية التساؤلية التي لا تكتفي بمجرد التلقين، ولا تقف عند حدود إجابة واحدة قد لا تمتلك الحجة الشافية. إن أصول الدين معارف يقينية لا مجال فيها لأي شك ابتداء بتوحيد الخالق سبحانه: قَالَتْ رُسُلُهُمْ أَفِي اللهِ شَكٍّ فَاطِرِ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالأَرْضِ [إبراهيم: ١٠/١٤]. وميدان الغيب وفي مقدمته اليوم الآخر يقيني لا ريب فيه: اللهُ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ لَيَجْمَعَنَّكُمْ إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ لَا رَيْبَ فِيهِ وَمَنْ أَصْدَقُ مِنَ اللَّهِ حَدِيثاً [النساء: ٨٧/٤]. قُلِ اللَّهُ يُحْيِيكُمْ ثُمَّ يُمِيتُكُمْ ثُمَّ يَجْمَعُكُمْ إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ لَا رَيْبَ فِيهِ [الجاثية: ٢٦/٤٥]. فَكَيْفَ إِذَا جَمَعْنَاهُمْ لِيَوْمٍ لَا رَيْبَ فِيهِ [آل عمران: ٢٥/٣]. وَبِالْآخِرَةِ هُمْ يُوقِنُونَ [البقرة: ٤/٢]. وجوهر اليوم الآخر: الجنة والنار وهما من جنس الغيب اليقيني كذلك: وَتُنذِرَ يَوْمَ الْجَمْعِ لَا رَيْبَ فِيهِ فَرِيقٌ فِي الْجَنَّةِ وَفَرِيقٌ فِي السَّعِيرِ [الشورى: ٧/٤٢].
Secondly - Certainty. Legitimacy of seeking certainty: In contrast to what preceded, the Noble Quran considers the search for certainty as legitimate. It has guided every perplexed questioner to search and ask until reaching certainty. Among that is asking the scholars and knowers: 'So if you are in doubt about what We have revealed to you, then ask those who read the Scripture before you' [Yunus 10:94]. Although the Quran declares its own certainty in more than one verse: 'The revelation of the Book, there is no doubt in it, from the Lord of the worlds' [As-Sajda 32:2], and 'This is the Book, there is no doubt in it' [Al-Baqarah 2:2]. And that indicates that the great certainties that some people believe with knowledge reaching the level of certainty do not permit generalizing that certain belief to all understandings, minds, and categories of researchers, due to the disparity that characterizes people's understandings and minds. But on the other hand, that does not excuse those who are not certain from searching and asking about certainty with all the capabilities, faculties, and means of knowledge they possess until they achieve certainty. This confirms the legitimacy of an inquisitive education that is not satisfied with mere indoctrination, nor stops at a single answer that may not possess a conclusive proof. The fundamentals of religion are certain knowledge, in which there is no room for any doubt, beginning with the oneness of the Creator: 'Their messengers said: Is there any doubt about Allah, the Originator of the heavens and the earth?' [Ibrahim 14:10]. And the realm of the unseen, foremost among which is the Hereafter, is certain with no doubt: 'Allah, there is no deity except Him. He will surely assemble you on the Day of Resurrection, about which there is no doubt. And who is more truthful than Allah in statement?' [An-Nisa 4:87]. 'Say, Allah gives you life, then causes you to die, then He will assemble you on the Day of Resurrection, about which there is no doubt' [Al-Jathiya 45:26]. 'Then how will you be when We have assembled them for a Day about which there is no doubt?' [Aal-e-Imran 3:25]. 'And of the Hereafter they are certain' [Al-Baqarah 2:4]. And the essence of the Hereafter: Paradise and Hellfire, which are also from the category of certain unseen: 'And to warn of the Day of Assembly, about which there is no doubt; a party in Paradise and a party in the Blaze' [Ash-Shura 42:7].
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage opens a new subsection on certainty (yaqin). The author first establishes that the Quran legitimizes the search for certainty, contrary to the previous condemnation of doubt. As evidence, he cites the verse from Surah Yunus where even the Prophet is told: if you are in doubt about what was revealed, ask those who read previous scriptures. This shows that inquiry is permitted. Then the author notes that the Quran itself declares its own certainty in verses like 'no doubt in it' from Surat as-Sajda and al-Baqara. The author draws an important epistemological inference: these great certainties (al-yaqiniyyat al-kubra) cannot simply be generalized to everyone, because people's intellects and understandings vary. So the Quran's self-certainty does not mean that every person automatically possesses certainty; it must be sought. Then he asserts that this does not excuse the non-certain from searching and asking with all their capacities. This underlies the legitimacy of a questioning education (tarbiya tasā'uliyya) that goes beyond rote learning and single answers lacking conclusive proof. Finally, the author emphasizes that the fundamentals of religion (usul al-din) are certain knowledge with no room for doubt, citing verses about Tawhid, the Hereafter, Paradise, and Hell. The point is that while the Quran is certain, human access to that certainty requires active inquiry.

Key Terms
يقين
شك
تربية تساؤلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the Quran command even the Prophet to ask scholars if he is in doubt?
A) Because the Quran is not actually certain.
B) To show that doubt is always forbidden.
C) To demonstrate that seeking certainty through inquiry is legitimate.
D) Because the Prophet needed to learn from others.

Key Takeaway
Seeking certainty through inquiry is not only permitted but commanded in Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify the Quranic verse (Yunus 10:94) cited by the author and explain how it supports the legitimacy of seeking certainty through inquiry. Then, find one other verse from the passage (e.g., concerning the Hereafter) and state what certainty it affirms, and how the author relates it to the need for active seeking.

The Quranic Rejection of Relativism
Author refutes epistemological relativism and affirms absolute truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the author's argument against epistemological relativism and identify the Quranic basis for absolute truth.

Core Idea
Relativism is self-defeating because it relies on absolute constants to exist.

The passage begins by asserting that truth in the Islamic framework is an absolute constant, leaving no room for relativity. The author argues that even relativists must presuppose absolute logical principles, thus refuting themselves. This lesson unpacks that argument and its implications for Muslim epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the thesis
Find the sentence stating that truth is an absolute constant and that relativity does not enter it.
2
Extract the argument against relativism
Locate the claim that no one can fully believe in or apply relativism to everything, because every thought requires absolute logical or self-evident constants.
This is a logical refutation of radical relativism.
3
Note the political critique
Recognize that the author links relativism to a conspiracy to weaken Muslim faith, while the beliefs of secularists, Crusaders, and Zionists are presented as absolute.
This highlights the hypocrisy of the relativist stance.
4
Connect to Quranic worldview
Understand that this rejection of relativism stems from the Quran's affirmation of truth as clear and certain, as seen in verses like 'So what is after the truth except error?'

الباب الرابع: الفصل الثاني - إمكان الحصول على الحقيقة المعرفية
وبالجملة فإن قضية الحقيقة في هذا الإطار تمثل إحدى الثوابت المطلقة التي لا مجال للجدل حولها، وعامل النسبية غير داخل فيها، إذ هي من البيان واليقين بحيث يغدو من قبيل العبث ادعاء حصول النسبية في شيء منها. وإن أحداً لا يستطيع - مطلقاً- أن يؤمن بمبدأ النسبية أو يطبقه على كل أمر، إذ لابد لأي فكر أياً ما كان مصدره من ثوابت منطقية أو بديهية، حتى يستطيع مجرد الوجود والقيام.
وحين تطرح دعاوى النسبية وعدم الثبات في كل شيء فإنما تُرَوَّج بهدف إضعاف عقيدة المسلمين وزعزعتها في نفوسهم، حيث إن عقائد العلمانيين، وعقائد الصليبيين والصهيونيين ثابتة راسخة مطلقة، وعلى أساسها تقوم دولهم وأنظمتهم).

التقاط الحقيقة من أي وعاء خرجت فهي ضالة المؤمن.

(۱) حسن عبد العال، مرجع سابق، ۱۳۳ - ۱۳۸. (۲) فاروق الدسوقي، قواعد منهجية للباحث عن الحقيقة في القرآن والسنة، ١٠ - ٤٨ .
Chapter Four: Section Two - The Possibility of Attaining Cognitive Truth
In summary, the issue of truth in this framework represents one of the absolute constants that admit no dispute, and the factor of relativity is not included in it, for it is of clarity and certainty such that claiming relativity in any part of it becomes a kind of folly. And no one can - absolutely - believe in the principle of relativity or apply it to everything, for any thought, whatever its source, must have logical or self-evident constants, just to be able to exist and stand.
And when claims of relativity and lack of stability in everything are raised, they are promoted with the aim of weakening the faith of Muslims and shaking it in their souls, while the beliefs of secularists, Crusaders, and Zionists are fixed, firm, and absolute, and on them their states and systems are based.
Rules for Seeking Truth
The Noble Qur'an presents a set of rules for seeking cognitive truth, which some researchers have attempted to compile, and they can be summarized as follows:
1 - Love of truth and magnifying it, as that is the goal of research in life. 'So what is after the truth except error?' [Yunus 10:32].
2 - The way to reach the truth is research, and therefore we find condemnation of blind imitation and its people in many verses, as has passed with us.
3 - Seizing the truth from whatever vessel it comes from, for it is the lost property of the believer.
4 - Stopping short of confusion in knowing the truth, for Allah is the possessor of absolute knowledge. 'And you have not been given of knowledge except a little' [Al-Isra 17:85]. And on the tongue of the Prophet: 'Say: I am not an unprecedented messenger, and I do not know what will be done with me or with you; I only follow what is revealed to me' [Al-Ahqaf 46:9].
5 - Knowledge itself is a value, as it is a path to acquiring information, according to specific methods and systems, and therefore there is distinction between scholars and the ignorant: 'Say: Are those who know equal to those who do not know?' [Az-Zumar 39:9].
6 - The relativity and probability of knowledge: 'And say: My Lord, increase me in knowledge' [Ta-Ha 20:114].
7 - The necessity of referring to the entire Qur'an to know a single Qur'anic truth.
8 - Ascribing revelation exclusively as the source, from the perspective of ascribing divinity and lordship exclusively to Allah Almighty.
9 - Knowledge through revelation and reason together.
10 - The necessity of consistency of the truth deduced from the Qur'an with other Qur'anic truths.
11 - Sincerity of intention and soundness of purpose.
In a general educational manner, we can benefit from truth in the process of education through the following:
1 - Providing the philosophy of education with an intellectual background about the reality of existence and the truths it contains, so that education can present a balanced definition of existence, its purpose, and the laws governing its movement through the experiences it offers to learners in educational situations, to affirm the balance between the theoretical and practical aspects. This is done while planning the desired educational programs and objectives.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion from a contemporary Islamic perspective, asserting that absolute truth exists and that the Quran provides a methodology for seeking it. The author begins by affirming that truth is an absolute constant that admits no relativity, arguing that even those who claim relativism rely on absolute logical or self-evident principles to make their claim. The author then criticizes the promotion of relativism as a means to weaken Muslim faith, pointing out that secularist, crusader, and Zionist ideologies themselves are presented as absolute. This sets the stage for presenting Quranic rules for seeking truth. The rules are enumerated: 1) Love and veneration of truth as the goal of life; 2) Research is the means, with condemnation of blind imitation; 3) Accept truth from any source, as it is the 'lost property of the believer'; 4) Acknowledge human limitation in absolute knowledge, citing verses that show even the Prophet does not know the unseen; 5) Knowledge is a value, distinguishing scholars from the ignorant; 6) Recognize the relativity of human knowledge, always seeking increase; 7) Consult the entire Quran for a single truth; 8) Revelation is the sole source of divine knowledge; 9) Combine revelation and reason; 10) Ensure consistency among deduced truths; 11) Sincerity and sound intention. The passage concludes with educational applications, emphasizing that the philosophy of education should be grounded in the truth of existence, balancing theory and practice. Throughout, the author uses Quranic verses and scholarly references to support the argument. The passage does not engage in formal logical argumentation but provides a methodological framework for epistemology rooted in Islamic sources.

الحقيقة المعرفية
النسبية

D) Because it is not practical.

Key Takeaway
The Quran establishes absolute truth as the foundation of knowledge, making relativism logically and theologically untenable.

Quranic Rules for Seeking Cognitive Truth
Author lists Quranic rules for seeking cognitive truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the Quranic principles for truth-seeking and apply them to a practical search for knowledge.

Core Idea
The Quran provides a comprehensive methodology for seeking truth that balances reason, revelation, and sincerity.

The author compiles a set of Quranic rules for seeking cognitive truth. These rules cover motivation (love of truth), method (research vs. imitation), epistemology (combination of revelation and reason), and ethics (sincerity). Understanding these rules equips the student with a practical framework for distinguishing truth from falsehood in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Scan the list
Identify the eleven rules and note their categories: motivation, method, epistemology, ethics.
2
Examine each rule with its Quranic basis
For each rule, find the verse or principle cited. Notice how rules 2 and 3 address taqlid and openness.
3
Observe the balance between revelation and reason
Rules 8 and 9 together establish revelation as the source of divine knowledge while reason is necessary.
4
Connect to the overall methodology
Reflect on how these rules form a coherent system: starting from love of truth, through research, accepting truth, humility, valuing knowledge, seeking increase, comprehensiveness, relying on revelation and reason, ensuring consistency, and sincerity.

وبصورة تربوية عامة فإن بإمكاننا أن نفيد من الحقيقة في عملية التربيه من
خلال ما يلي:
١ - تزويد فلسفة التربية بخلفية فكرية حول حقيقة الوجود، وما يتضمنه من حقائق كي تقدّم التربية تعريفاً متوازناً للوجود، وهدفه والقوانين الناظمة حركته عن طريق الخبرات التي تعرضها على المتعلمين في المواقف التعليمية، لتؤكد عملية التوازن بين الجانب النظري والعملي. وذلك أثناء القيام بتخطيط البرامج والأهداف التعليمية المرجوة.
(۱) حسن عبد العال، مرجع سابق، ۱۳۳ - ۱۳۸. (۲) فاروق الدسوقي، قواعد منهجية للباحث عن الحقيقة في القرآن والسنة، ١٠ - ٤٨ .
Chapter Four: Section Two - The Possibility of Attaining Cognitive Truth
In summary, the issue of truth in this framework represents one of the absolute constants that admit no dispute, and the factor of relativity is not included in it, for it is of clarity and certainty such that claiming relativity in any part of it becomes a kind of folly. And no one can - absolutely - believe in the principle of relativity or apply it to everything, for any thought, whatever its source, must have logical or self-evident constants, just to be able to exist and stand.
And when claims of relativity and lack of stability in everything are raised, they are promoted with the aim of weakening the faith of Muslims and shaking it in their souls, while the beliefs of secularists, Crusaders, and Zionists are fixed, firm, and absolute, and on them their states and systems are based.
Rules for Seeking Truth
The Noble Qur'an presents a set of rules for seeking cognitive truth, which some researchers have attempted to compile, and they can be summarized as follows:
1 - Love of truth and magnifying it, as that is the goal of research in life. 'So what is after the truth except error?' [Yunus 10:32].
2 - The way to reach the truth is research, and therefore we find condemnation of blind imitation and its people in many verses, as has passed with us.
3 - Seizing the truth from whatever vessel it comes from, for it is the lost property of the believer.
4 - Stopping short of confusion in knowing the truth, for Allah is the possessor of absolute knowledge. 'And you have not been given of knowledge except a little' [Al-Isra 17:85]. And on the tongue of the Prophet: 'Say: I am not an unprecedented messenger, and I do not know what will be done with me or with you; I only follow what is revealed to me' [Al-Ahqaf 46:9].
5 - Knowledge itself is a value, as it is a path to acquiring information, according to specific methods and systems, and therefore there is distinction between scholars and the ignorant: 'Say: Are those who know equal to those who do not know?' [Az-Zumar 39:9].
6 - The relativity and probability of knowledge: 'And say: My Lord, increase me in knowledge' [Ta-Ha 20:114].
7 - The necessity of referring to the entire Qur'an to know a single Qur'anic truth.
8 - Ascribing revelation exclusively as the source, from the perspective of ascribing divinity and lordship exclusively to Allah Almighty.
9 - Knowledge through revelation and reason together.
10 - The necessity of consistency of the truth deduced from the Qur'an with other Qur'anic truths.
11 - Sincerity of intention and soundness of purpose.
In a general educational manner, we can benefit from truth in the process of education through the following:
1 - Providing the philosophy of education with an intellectual background about the reality of existence and the truths it contains, so that education can present a balanced definition of existence, its purpose, and the laws governing its movement through the experiences it offers to learners in educational situations, to affirm the balance between the theoretical and practical aspects. This is done while planning the desired educational programs and objectives.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion from a contemporary Islamic perspective, asserting that absolute truth exists and that the Quran provides a methodology for seeking it. The author begins by affirming that truth is an absolute constant that admits no relativity, arguing that even those who claim relativism rely on absolute logical or self-evident principles to make their claim. The author then criticizes the promotion of relativism as a means to weaken Muslim faith, pointing out that secularist, crusader, and Zionist ideologies themselves are presented as absolute. This sets the stage for presenting Quranic rules for seeking truth. The rules are enumerated: 1) Love and veneration of truth as the goal of life; 2) Research is the means, with condemnation of blind imitation; 3) Accept truth from any source, as it is the 'lost property of the believer'; 4) Acknowledge human limitation in absolute knowledge, citing verses that show even the Prophet does not know the unseen; 5) Knowledge is a value, distinguishing scholars from the ignorant; 6) Recognize the relativity of human knowledge, always seeking increase; 7) Consult the entire Quran for a single truth; 8) Revelation is the sole source of divine knowledge; 9) Combine revelation and reason; 10) Ensure consistency among deduced truths; 11) Sincerity and sound intention. The passage concludes with educational applications, emphasizing that the philosophy of education should be grounded in the truth of existence, balancing theory and practice. Throughout, the author uses Quranic verses and scholarly references to support the argument. The passage does not engage in formal logical argumentation but provides a methodological framework for epistemology rooted in Islamic sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the way to reach the truth?
A) Blind imitation of scholars.
B) Research and seeking.
C) Following personal desire.
D) Accepting majority opinion.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic methodology for truth-seeking combines love of truth, active research, openness to sources, humility about human knowledge, and sincerity, all within the framework of revelation and reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Choose one of the 11 rules and find a practical example from the study of fiqh or kalam where applying that rule would prevent an error.
?
Compare the Quranic rule 'seizing truth from any vessel' with the concept of 'lost property of the believer' and explain why this encourages intellectual openness while maintaining ultimate authority of revelation.
